§ 10.01 TITLE.
   This codification of the general ordinances of the City of Nezperce is
declared to be the official City Code of the City of Nezperce.
§ 10.02 ACCEPTANCE.
   Any official copy of the code shall be received without further proof in all
courts and in all administrative tribunals of the state.
§ 10.03 AMENDMENTS.
   Any ordinance amending the code shall set forth the title, chapter and
section number of the section or sections to be amended. All such ordinances
shall comply with the provisions of the code and Idaho Code Title 50, Chapter
9, regarding passage, execution and publication of ordinances. All such
amendments shall be promptly forwarded to the codifiers by the City Clerk/
Treasurer and such ordinance shall be promptly published and inserted in its
proper place in each copy of the city code.
§ 10.04 MAINTENANCE OF CITY CODE.
   Upon receipt of each published ordinance from the codifiers, the City Clerk/
Treasurer shall promptly forward a copy of each page thereof to each person
having an official copy of the city code. The City Clerk/Treasurer may collect
a fee for each copy of the city code and an annual fee for maintenance thereof;
provided, such fees shall be established by resolution or ordinance duly passed
by the City Council.
§ 10.05 REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES.
   (A)   Repeal of existing ordinances. The ordinances contained in this code
of ordinances shall be construed as continuations thereof of existing
ordinances; but subject to the limitations and provisions of division (B)
below, all ordinances and resolutions of the city heretofore in force (except
grants, dedications, abandonments of streets and alleys and special levies for
local assessments) are hereby repealed.
(Prior Code, § 1-101)
   (B)   Effect of repealing ordinances. The repeal of ordinances as provided
herein shall not affect any right which has accrued, any duty imposed, any
penalty incurred, nor any action or proceedings as commenced any person holding
office at the time when they take effect; nor shall the repeal of any
ordinances thereby have the effect of revising any ordinance therefor repealed
or superseded.
(Prior Code, § 1-102)
§ 10.06 PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES.
   No ordinance or section thereof relating to railroad or railroad crossings
of streets and other public ways, or relating to the conduct, duties, service
or rates of public utilities, shall be repealed by the adoption of the code or
by §
10.05 of this chapter, except as this code specifically provides for such
repeal.
§ 10.07 SAVING CLAUSE.
   Any ordinance amending or repealing any section of the code shall not be
deemed or construed to abate any pending action based upon such amended or
repealed section, nor shall the passage of such ordinance prevent the arrest,
prosecution and punishment of any violation of such section committed prior to
the effective date of such ordinance.
§ 10.08 GENERAL CONSTRUCTIONAL RULE.
   In the construction of this code of ordinances and all ordinances amendatory
thereof or supplementary thereto the following rules shall be observed unless
such construction would be inconsistent with the manifest intent of the
legislative body or repugnant to the context of the ordinance.
   (A)   Intent to defraud. Whenever, by any of the provisions of this code, an
intent to defraud is required in order to constitute an offense, it is
sufficient if an intent appears to defraud any persons, association or body,
politic or any combination of persons.
   (B)   Liability of employers and agents. When the provisions of any
ordinance prohibit the commission or omission of an act, not only the person
actually doing the prohibited thing or omitting the directed act, the person
shall be guilty of the offense described and liable to the penalty set forth in
this code.
(Prior Code, § 1-103)
§ 10.09 PLURAL AND SINGULAR WORDS.
   Whenever any word in the code is used in either the singular or in the
plural form, then such word shall be deemed to include both the plural and
singular forms of such word, unless the context indicates an intent otherwise.
§ 10.10 MASCULINE AND FEMININE GENDER.
   When any person is referred to in any section of the code by use of the
masculine gender, then such reference shall be deemed to include the feminine
gender unless the context indicates an intent otherwise.
§ 10.11 PRIORITY OF ORDINANCE.
   In the event of any discrepancy or conflict between the code and any
ordinance passing or amending the same section of the code, then the provisions
of the ordinance shall prevail.
§ 10.12 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this code of ordinances, the following definitions shall
apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AGENT. A person acting on behalf of another.
   CITY. The City of Nezperce, Lewis County, State of Idaho.
   CITY ATTORNEY. An attorney appointed by the Mayor to provide general counsel
and legal assistance to the city and to prosecute or defend all civil actions
in which the city is a party.
   CLERK. The Clerk/Treasurer of the City of Nezperce, Idaho.
   COUNCIL. The lawfully elected governing body of Nezperce, Idaho.
   COUNTY. The County of Lewis, Idaho.
   CRIME. An act in violation of this code.
   DAY. Any 24-hour period from midnight to midnight.
   FELONY. A crime as defined under Idaho Code § 18-111.
   GOVERNING BODY. The Mayor and City Council of Nezperce, Idaho.
   IDAPA. Idaho Administrative Regulations. A numbering designation for all
administrative rules in Idaho which denotes rules promulgated in accordance
with the state’s Administrative Procedure Act, Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 52.
   INFRACTION. A civil public offense, not constituting a crime, which is
punishable only by a penalty not exceeding $300 plus court costs and for which
no incarceration may be imposed.
   KNOWINGLY. Imports only a knowledge that the facts exist which rings the act
or omission within the provisions of these ordinances.
   LAND, REAL ESTATE and REAL PROPERTY. Includes lands, tenements,
hereditaments, water rights, possessory rights and claims.
   LICENSE. The permission granted for the carrying on of a business, trade,
profession or occupation.
   MISDEMEANOR. Every crime, except a felony.
   MONTH. A calendar month unless otherwise expressed.
   NEGLECT, NEGLIGENCE, NEGLIGENT and NEGLIGENTLY. Imports a want of such
attention to the nature or probable consequences of the act or omission as a
prudent human ordinarily bestows in acting in his or her own concern.
   OATH. Includes AFFIRMATION and the word SWEAR includes the word AFFIRM.
Every mode of oral statement under oath or affirmation is embraced in the term
TESTIFY and every written one in the term DEPOSE.
   OCCUPANT. Any person who occupies the whole or any part of such building or
land, whether alone or with others.
   OFFENSE. A crime or other violation of this code.
   OFFICER. Include officers as boards in charge of departments and the members
of such boards.
   OPERATOR. The person who is generally in charge of or responsible for
conducting any business, profession or enterprise.
   OWNER. Any person owning real or personal property, including any part
owner, joint owner, tenant in common, joint tenant, remainderman or person
holding a life estate or reversionary interest of any kind.
   PERSON. A human being and any public or private corporation, firm,
partnership, trust, estate, sole proprietorship, association, organization,
government or any other entity recognized under state law.
   PERSONAL PROPERTY. Money, goods, chattels, effects, rights in action and all
written instruments evidencing any pecuniary obligation.
   PROPERTY. Includes both real and personal property.
   QUARTER. Any three-month period, ending with the last days of March, June,
September and December.
   RIGHT-OF-WAY. The privilege of the immediate use of the roadway or other
property.
   STATE. The State of Idaho.
   STREET. All public roads, ways, alleys and rights-of-way used for the
movement of vehicular traffic, including any public sidewalks adjacent thereto.
   TENANT or OCCUPANT. Any person who occupies any building or real property
for a consideration to the owner.
   TREASURER. The Clerk/Treasurer of the City of Nezperce, Idaho.
   WRITING. Includes printing, writing and typewriting.
   YEAR. Any one calendar year.
(Prior Code, § 1-103)
§ 10.13 CAPTIONS.
   The title of any section or division of these ordinances all be deemed to in
no wise restrict or qualify or limit the effect of the provisions set forth and
contained in such section or division.
(Prior Code, § 1-103)
§ 10.14 SEVERABILITY.
   Should any section, division or portion of this code of ordinances, or of
any ordinance which may be hereafter passed, approved and published as required
by law, be declared by any court of competent jurisdiction to be
unconstitutional or void, such adjudication shall in no way affect the
remaining portion or such section, division, part or portion of this code of
ordinances or any such ordinance hereafter passed.
(Prior Code, § 1-103)
§ 10.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   General penalty. Any person convicted of a misdemeanor or violation of
any section of this code shall be fined in a sum not exceeding $1,000 for
general misdemeanor violations, or confined in a city jail not more than 30
days, or both such fine and imprisonment, recoverable with costs, and default
of payment of any fine imposed, shall be imprisoned in the city jail for a
period of one day for each $10 of such fine.
(Prior Code, § 1-501)
   (B)   To what acts penalty shall attach. Any person who shall commit any act
declared by any section of this code to be unlawful, or who fails to perform
any act or discharge any obligations or duty required by or imposed upon him or
her by any ordinance shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and shall be
subject to the penalty fixed for the violation with like effect as if such
penalty were specifically declared in the section forbidding such act or
declaring the same to be unlawful or prescribing the day or imposing the
obligations, and where any duty is prescribed or obligation imposed, or where
any act which is of the continuing nature is forbidden or declared to unlawful,
each day such duty or obligation remains unperformed or such act continues,
shall constitute a separate offense, except where otherwise provided in this
code.
(Prior Code, § 1-502)
CHAPTER 11: CITY STANDARDS
Section
   
11.01   Corporate seal
   
11.02   Official newspaper
   
11.03   Depository designated
§ 11.01 CORPORATE SEAL.
   The official seal of the city shall be in circular in form and inscribed
thereon as follow: the word “SEAL” across the center of the circle and around
the outside shall be inscribed “CITY OF NEZPERCE, LEWIS COUNTY, IDAHO”.
(Prior Code, § 1-201)
§ 11.02 OFFICIAL NEWSPAPER.
   The Lewis County Herald, a weekly newspaper, printed and published in the
city, is hereby appointed, designated and constituted the official newspaper of
the city for publication of all ordinances and other writings as are required
under and by virtue of the laws of the state and of the said city to be
published in a newspaper.
(Prior Code, § 1-301)
§ 11.03 DEPOSITORY DESIGNATED.
   The Cottonwood Community Federal Credit Union, Nezperce, Idaho, and the
Idaho State Treasurers Investment Pool, are hereby designated as the
depositories for the city and the Clerk/Treasurer is hereby ordered, required
and directed to keep moneys belonging to the city in the depositories herein
named.
(Prior Code, § 1-401)

MAYOR
§ 30.01 DUTIES GENERALLY.
   The Mayor shall: be the chief administrative official of the city; preside
at all meetings of the Council and be empowered to vote when the Council is
equally divided; call special meetings when necessary; appoint, subject to the
approval of the City Council, all officers and employees of the city; and shall
have all other duties required and necessary for the efficient operation of the
business of the city and duties imposed by the laws of the state.
(Prior Code, § 1-1101)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Idaho Code § 50-602
§ 30.02 MAYOR TO SIGN DOCUMENTS.
   (A)   (1)   The Mayor is authorized and empowered to sign, for and in behalf
of the city, all contracts, documents and papers to which the city is a part
and to require that the conditions in any instrument are faithfully performed.
      (2)   The Mayor does not sign checks.
(Prior Code, § 1-1102)
   (B)   The Mayor is duly authorized to sign applications, grant agreements
and amendments and other documents relating to wastewater facilities planning
grants.
(Res. R2019-2, passed 2-12-2019)
§ 30.03 MAYOR TO BORROW MONEY.
   The Mayor may borrow money on the credit of the city when so authorized by
the Council.
(Prior Code, § 1-1103)
§ 30.04 MAYOR TO OFFER REWARDS.
   The Mayor, whenever he or she deems expedient, is hereby empowered to offer
a reward for the arrest and conviction of any person charged with violating any
of the ordinances of the city.
(Prior Code, § 1-1104)
§ 30.05 VETO POWER.
   The Mayor shall have the power to veto or sign any ordinance passed by the
City Council; provided that, any ordinance vetoed by the Mayor may be passed
over his or her veto by a vote of one-half plus one of the members of the full
Council, notwithstanding the veto, and should the Mayor neglect or refuse to
sign any ordinance and return the same with his or her objections, in writing,
at the next regular meeting of the Council, the same shall become a law without
his or her signature.
(Prior Code, § 1-1105)
§ 30.06 ACCOUNTS AND REPORTS.
   The Mayor shall have the power, when he or she deems it necessary, to
require any officer of the city to exhibit his or her accounts or papers, or to
make reports to the Council in writing touching any subject or matter
pertaining to his or her office.
(Prior Code, § 1-1106)
§ 30.07 MAYOR TO REQUIRE AID.
   The Mayor is hereby authorized to call on every male inhabitant of the city
over 21 years of age to aid in enforcing the laws.
(Prior Code, § 1-1107)
§ 30.08 SALARY.
   (A)   The Mayor shall receive an annual salary in the sum of $2,140.
   (B)   In addition to the monetary compensation specified in division (A)
above, the Mayor shall be responsible only for payment of the base water rate
as established in the current fee schedule for residential water service at
their primary residence within the city limits. The Mayor shall be exempt from
any water usage fees, consumption charges or tiered rate structures that exceed
the base water rate.
   (C)   The exemption provided in division (B) above shall apply only to the
Mayor’s primary residence and shall not be transferable to any other property
or person.
(Prior Code, § 1-1108) (Ord. 2019-4, passed 8-13-2019; Ord. 2025-03, passed 2-
10-2025)
CITY COUNCIL
§ 30.20 COMPOSITION.
   The legislative authority of the city shall be vested in a City Council
consisting of four members, qualified as provided by law.
(Prior Code, § 1-1201)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Idaho Code § 50-701
§ 30.21 PRESIDENT OF COUNCIL.
   At the first meeting of the Council in January following a general city
election, the Council shall, from its members, elect one Council member to be
styled as “President of the Council”. The President of the Council shall have
all powers of the Mayor when serving that office due to absence of the Mayor or
vacancy in the office of the Mayor.
(Prior Code, § 1-1202)
§ 30.22 DUTIES.
   The members of the City Council, the legislative and policy-making branch of
the government of the city, shall devote so much of their time to the duties of
their office as an efficient and faithful discharge thereof may require. They
shall attend all meetings of the Council unless lawfully excused therefrom by
the Mayor by a majority of the remaining members, perform all duties required
by them by law and as may be assigned committees to which they may severally be
appointed by the Mayor.
(Prior Code, § 1-1203)
§ 30.23 TIME AND PLACE OF MEETINGS.
   The Council shall hold regular meetings in the City Council Chambers at 606
Maple Street. The meetings are held on the second Monday of each month at 5:30
p.m in the months of October, November, December, January, February and March;
meetings will be at 7:00 a.m. in April, May, June, July, August and September.
The Mayor or one-half plus one of the membership of the Council may call
special meetings, the object of which must be submitted to the members in
writing if possible, unless waived by the Council, and the call, object and the
deposition thereof shall be entered upon the Journal by the Clerk/Treasurer. If
the regular meeting day of any month is a holiday, the meeting shall be held on
the following day at the regular hour.
(Prior Code, § 1-1204) (Ord. 2019-8, passed 9-10-2019)
§ 30.24 QUORUM AND DISCIPLINE.
   (A)   At all meetings of the Council, a majority of the full Council shall
constitute a quorum for the transaction of business; unless otherwise provided
by law, a question before the Council shall be decided by a majority of the
members present.
   (B)   For the purpose of holding regular or special meetings, a number less
than a majority may compel the attendance of absent members in such manner and
under such penalties as the Council may, by ordinance, have previously
prescribed. Regular or special meetings of the Council may, by ordinance, have
previously prescribed. Regular or special meetings of the Council may be
recessed until further notice.
(Prior Code, § 1-1205)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Idaho Code § 50-706
§ 30.25 CARE OF FUNDS.
   The City Council shall make provisions for the care and safekeeping of all
public funds of the city and for the deposit of the same.
(Prior Code, § 1-1206)
§ 30.26 RECORDS.
   The City Council shall make provisions for an adequate record system and, by
ordinance, establish a classification for retention of records in accordance
with the provisions of Idaho Code Title 50.
(Prior Code, § 1-1207)
§ 30.27 EXAMINATION OF OFFICERS’ ACCOUNTS.
   At least once in each quarter of each year, the Council shall examine,
either in open session or by committee, the accounts and doings of all officers
or other persons having the care, management or disposition of moneys, property
or business of the city.
(Prior Code, § 1-1208)
§ 30.28 PRESENTATION, PASSAGE OF ORDINANCES.
   (A)   All ordinances of the city shall be typewritten or printed and
presented to the Council by a member at any regular or special meeting. Every
such ordinance shall be read at the meetings of the Council on three different
days; at each reading, it shall be open to discussion and amendment or may be
referred to a committee unless by majority vote other disposition is made. All
ordinances which have been amended shall after the second reading be engrossed
by the Clerk/Treasurer as amended. On final passage, the yeas and nays shall be
called and recorded and a concurrence of a majority of the full Council shall
be required for passage; provided, however, that, on the vote of one-half plus
one member of the Council may dispense with the portion of this section
requiring all ordinances to be read on three different days and, on the vote,
upon the motion to dispense with this rule and the yeas and nays shall be
called and recorded.
   (B)   When any such ordinance is passed, it shall be signed by the Clerk/
Treasurer and the date of its passage by the Council shall be added thereto,
and it shall, within three days thereafter, be presented to the Mayor or, in
case of his or her absence from the city, to the President of the Council for
his or her approval. If he or she approves the same, he or she shall attach his
or her signature thereto.
(Prior Code, § 1-1209)
§ 30.29 PASSAGE OVER VETO.
   (A)   Should the Mayor not approve the ordinance, he or she shall, before
the next regular meeting after such ordinance is presented to him or her for
his or her approval, return the ordinance to the Council with his or her
objections in writing. When any ordinance is so returned by the Mayor, it shall
be reconsidered by the Council at the first regular meeting thereafter. If, on
such reconsideration, one- half plus one of the members of the full Council
shall vote in the affirmative, the ordinance shall become a law notwithstanding
the Mayor’s veto. The Clerk/Treasurer, in such cases, shall annex a certificate
to the ordinance stating the same was vetoed by the Mayor and that, on its
reconsideration, it received the required majority of votes.
   (B)   Should the Mayor refuse or neglect to sign such ordinance and return
the same with his or her objections in writing at the next regular meeting
after the same has been presented to him or her, it shall become law without
his or her signature. The Clerk/Treasurer shall annex to such ordinance a
certificate to the effect that the Mayor has failed to sign or veto the same
and it has, therefor, become a law without his or her signature.
(Prior Code, § 1-1210)
§ 30.30 VACANCY.
   In the event an office of the Council shall become vacant, through death,
removal of residence or for any other cause, the Mayor shall appoint, with the
approval of the Council, a resident of the city to fill the term until the next
general election at which such vacancy shall be filled for the balance of the
original term.
(Prior Code, § 1-1211)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Idaho Code § 50-704
§ 30.31 SALARY.
   (A)   Each member of the Council shall receive an annual salary in the sum
of $700.
   (B)   In addition to the monetary compensation specified in division (A)
above, the Council members shall be responsible only for payment of the base
water rate as established in the current fee schedule for residential water
service at their primary residence within the city limits. The Council members
shall be exempt from any water usage fees, consumption charges or tiered rate
structures that exceed the base water rate.
   (C)   The exemption provided in division (B) above shall apply only to the
Council member’s primary residence and shall not be transferable to any other
property or person.
(Prior Code, § 1-1212) (Ord. 2019-4, passed 8-13-2019; Ord. 2025-04, passed 2-
10-2025)
§ 30.32 CONTINUITY IN GOVERNMENT IN EVENT OF DISASTER OR EMERGENCY.
   (A)   As provided in § 27 of the Constitution of the state, there is thereby
established the following procedure for filling the offices of the elected
officials in the event of an emergency or disaster. In the event of a vacancy
in the office of Mayor only, the Council member having the greatest years of
tenure as an elected officer shall succeed to that office.
   (B)   In the event there are, in addition to the Mayor, also vacancies on
the Council, the Mayor shall be elected from any by the new Council, who shall
be determined as follows: members of the Planning Commission shall succeed to
the vacancies on the Council in the order of their tenure as members to the
Planning Commission, beginning with the member of the longest tenure. For
expediency, all ties shall be determined by lot.
(Prior Code, § 1-1213)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 31.01 APPOINTMENT OF OFFICERS.
   The Mayor, with the consent of the Council, shall appoint a City Clerk/
Treasurer, City Attorney, Fire Chief and such other officers as may be deemed
necessary for the efficient operations of the city.
(Prior Code, § 1-601)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Idaho Code § 50-204
§ 31.02 TERM OF OFFICE; REMOVAL.
   All appointed officers shall hold office for the term for which they were
appointed and qualified; provided that, any appointed officer may at any time
be removed by the Mayor for any cause deemed sufficient, but such removal shall
be by and with the affirmative vote of three members of the City Council;
provided that, the City Council, by the unanimous vote of all its members may,
upon their own initiative, remove any appointed officer.
(Prior Code, § 1-602)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Idaho Code § 50-206
§ 31.03 BONDS OF OFFICERS.
   The Idaho Counties Risk Management Program (ICRMP) Insurance covers the
following bonds:
 
                             Per covered occurrence and The first $5,000 of any
Employee dishonesty $250,000 in the aggregate amount    loss
                             for all claims annually
Notary public       $10,000  Per covered occurrence      
 
(Prior Code, § 1-603)
§ 31.04 PERSONNEL POLICY.
   The city’s personnel policies, and any and all amendments thereto, are
hereby adopted by reference and incorporated herein as if set out in full.
(Res. 1995-2, passed 7-11-1995; Res. 2012-2, passed 3-6-2012)
SPECIFIC OFFICERS
§ 31.15 CITY CLERK; RECORDS CUSTODIAN.
   (A)   To keep city seal, ordinances and all city records.
      (1)   The Clerk shall be custodian of the seal and affix same to
documents as provided by law or ordinance. The Clerk shall also be custodian of
all public records, documents, ordinance, resolutions and orders of the Council
and such other papers and documents as may be delivered into his or her
custody.
      (2)   The City Clerk is designated as the primary records custodian for
the city for all city departments, except for law enforcement records. The
Deputy City Clerk is designated as the alternate records custodian for the city
for all city departments, except for law enforcement records.
   (B)   To attend meetings of the Council and keep minutes and records. The
Clerk shall attend all sessions of the Council, keep a correct journal and
shall keep in a separate book a record of ordinances passed by the Council and
of the titles of such ordinances; and all ordinances not published in book form
shall be carefully indexed in numbered order by year. The Clerk shall see that
each ordinance is published as required by law and he or she shall keep on file
the proof of such publications.
   (C)   To report to Council. The Clerk shall prepare and present to the
Council, at its regular meeting each month, a full and complete statement of
the financial transaction of his or her office during the month preceding,
which said statements shall set forth all receipts for licenses issued; money
received with applications for licenses which are to come before the Council;
all other funds received by him or her as Clerk and said report shall give a
detailed explanation of disbursements. He or she shall also, at the close of
each fiscal year, present to the Council an annual report covering the
operations of the entire year, which report shall contain a description of the
bonds issued and sold during the year and the term of sale; and shall itemize
each and every expense thereof. The Clerk shall also make such additional
report and furnish such other date from the records and files of his or her
office as may be requested by the City Council or be required by law.
   (D)   To furnish copies of city records. It shall be the duty of the Clerk
to furnish any city officer with a certified copy of any record, paper of
public document on file in his or her office or in his or her custody, for the
use of such officer in the discharge of his or her official duties and he or
she shall also furnish a certified copy of any such record, paper of document
to any person not an officer of the city upon the payment in advance of the
following:
      (1)   Hard copies: first 100 pages at no cost; any above and beyond will
be $0.20/page.
      (2)   Electronic copies: a labor fee will be charged at the hourly pay
rate of the lowest paid administrative staff employee or public official of the
public agency who is necessary and qualified to process the request.
   (E)   To keep books and records. The Clerk shall keep such books and
permanent records of the transaction and business of his or her office as may
be necessary to accurately disclose all transactions and business of his or her
office. He or she shall also countersign all checks and keep a “check
register”, showing the number and amount of checks issued and the person to
whom issued and the several funds against which said check is drawn.
   (F)   To issue licenses. The Clerk shall issue all licenses, a duplicate of
which shall be kept on file, but no license shall be issued to any person
unless fees and charges fixed by law shall have first been paid, for which
payment the Clerk shall issue a receipt in duplicate, upon request. The Clerk
shall endorse upon the receipt and duplicate receipt the number of the license
issued, the number of the application for license and the duplicate of such
receipt so issued shall be kept on file with the duplicate license.
   (G)   To keep record of city bonds. The Clerk shall keep records of
outstanding bonds of the city, showing the number and amount of each, for what
and to whom said bonds were issued, and when any said bonds are purchased or
paid or canceled said record shall show the fact and, in his or her report at
the close of each fiscal year, he or she shall describe particularly the bonds
issued and sold during the year, the term of said and itemize each and every
expense thereof.
   (H)   To turn money over to Treasurer. Within ten days after the filing of
his or her monthly report as provided herein, the Clerk shall deposit with the
Treasurer all funds collected by him or her during the preceding month, less
refunds which have been authorized by the Council.
   (I)   City checks to show fund drawn upon. Each check shall show the fund
upon which the same is drawn.
   (J)   Claims filed with the city.
      (1)   All claims against the city must be filed with the Clerk, in
writing, and by him or her presented to the governing body for their auditing,
with a full account of the items, verified by the oath of the claimant or his
or her agent, if requested by the Mayor or a majority of the Council, that the
same is correct, reasonable and just and that it, nor any part thereof, has not
been paid, and no claims or demands shall be audited or allowed unless
presented as provided for this section.
      (2)   All claims for damage against the city must be filed as prescribed
by Idaho Code Title 6, Chapter 9.
(Prior Code, § 1-701) (Res. R-2018-5, passed 7-10-2018; Res. R2024-09, passed
8-12-2024)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Idaho Code § 50-219
§ 31.16 CITY ATTORNEY.
   (A)   The City Attorney shall be the legal advisor of the municipal
corporation, may represent the city in all suits or proceedings in which the
city is interested and shall perform such other duties as may be prescribed by
ordinances and resolutions duly passed. Nothing herein, however, shall preclude
any city from employing alternative additional counsel when deemed advisable.
   (B)   The City Attorney, his or her deputies or contract counsel shall
prosecute those violations of county or city ordinances, state traffic
infractions and state misdemeanors committed within the municipal limits. In so
doing, the City Attorney, his or her deputies or contract counsel shall
exercise the same powers as the county prosecutor including, but not limited
to, granting immunity to witnesses.
(Prior Code, § 1-801)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Idaho Code § 50-208a
§ 31.17 CHIEF OF FIRE DEPARTMENT.
   (A)   The Chief of the Fire Department shall have, subject to the approval
of the City Council, supervision of all the affairs and business of the
Department, control of all Fire Department property and equipment, and the work
of all the members and employees thereof, and while attending fires, answering
fire calls and returning therefrom, subject to the approval of the City
Council, shall have the authority of the police officer. The First Assistant
Chief and Second Assistant Chief shall assist the Chief of the Fire Department
in his or her duties. In the absence of the Chief of the Fire Department, they
shall perform, in their proper order, the duties of such Chief.
(Prior Code, § 1-901)
   (B)   The Fire Chief shall receive an annual salary in the sum of $700.
(Ord. 2019-4, passed 8-13-2019)
§ 31.18 CITY TREASURER.
   (A)   To receive and safely keep funds. It shall be the duty of the
Treasurer to receive and safely keep in designated depositories, as required by
law, all moneys or funds belonging to the city; to disburse the same upon an
appropriation by ordinance or resolution of the City Council after audit and
allowance by the City Council of claims therefor and, upon checks of the City
Council, countersigned by the Clerk, and not otherwise. Securities belonging to
the city, incapable of deposit in a checking account, shall be kept by the
Treasurer in a safety deposit box in some banking institution designated by the
City Council. All bonds or securities delivered to the Treasurer by the
designated depository of city funds as security for such funds shall be
deposited with the County Auditor or other public official as may be provided
by law.
   (B)   To keep proper books and records. The Treasurer shall keep in a
suitable book or books a full and accurate account of city money and funds,
showing the date of receipt thereof, the person from whom received, on what
account and to what fund the same is credited with the date of disbursement,
the person to whom disbursed, on what account and against what fund.
   (C)   To deliver all paid vouchers and checks to clerk. All checks paid and
redeemed and all vouchers shall be delivered to the Clerk immediately upon
payment.
   (D)   To issue duplicate receipts for money received. The Treasurer shall
execute and deliver, upon request, to every officer or other person paying
money or funds into the treasury a receipt thereof specifying the date of the
payment, the amount thereof and upon what fund or account the same is received.
   (E)   To deliver books and papers to successors. The Treasurer shall deliver
to his or her successor in office all books, money, papers and other property
pertaining to his or her office.
   (F)   To publish quarterly reports of receipts and expenditures. It shall be
the duty of the Treasurer to cause to be published for at least one insertion
in the official newspaper of the city, between the first and third Mondays of
April, July, October and January of each and every year a full statement of the
receipts an expenditures of the city, giving the source from hence received, to
what purpose applied.
   (G)   To collect all moneys. The Treasurer shall receive and all officers or
other persons shall forthwith pay to the Treasurer, except as otherwise
provided by this code, all money due the city on any account whatsoever.
   (H)   To make monthly report to the City Council. The Treasurer shall, at
the end of each and every month, and at other times when required by the City
Council, render an account, including in and showing, under oath, the condition
of the Treasury with a detailed statement of the specified amount in each
designated depository and of the amount and class of security held to guarantee
each deposit. Such account shall also contain a statement of receipts and
disbursements, which shall be filed with the Clerk’s office. The City Council
shall have free access to any and all books or papers in the office of the
Treasurer for the purpose of inspection or examination.
   (I)   Consolidation. The offices of the City Clerk and the Treasurer may be
consolidated upon proper resolution by the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 1-1001)
Statutory reference:
   Related provisions, see Idaho Code § 50-208
SPECIFIC ORGANIZATIONS
§ 31.30 URBAN FORESTRY BOARD.
   (A)   Creation and establishment. There is hereby created and established an
Urban Forestry Board for the city, which shall consist of five members,
citizens and residents of the community, as defined by the boundaries of the
School District, and at least one member of the City Council, who shall be an
ex officio, non-voting member.
   (B)   Term of office. The term of the five persons to be appointed by the
Mayor shall be three years; except that, the term of two of the members
appointed to the first Board shall be for only one year and the term of two
members of the first Board shall be for two years. In the event that a vacancy
shall occur during the term of any member, the successor shall be appointed for
the unexpired portion of the term.
   (C)   Compensation. Members of the Board shall serve without compensation.
   (D)   Duties and responsibilities. It shall be the responsibility of the
Board to study, investigate, counsel and develop and/or update annually, and
administer a written plan for the care, including planting, culture and removal
or disposition of trees and shrubs in parks, streets, alleys and other lands
owned or managed by the city. As a part of said plan, the Board may also, at
its discretion, provide guidance and make recommendations regarding planting
and tree care on private property within the city. Such plan will be presented
annually to the City Council and, upon their acceptance and approval, shall
constitute the official “Comprehensive Urban Forest Plan for the City of
Nezperce, Idaho”. The Board, when requested by the City Council, shall
consider, investigate, make findings, report and recommend upon any special
matter or question coming within the scope of its work.
   (E)   Amendments. Upon approval of the Comprehensive Urban Forest Plan by
the City Council, said plan including any subsequent amendments, shall become
part of this section.
   (F)   Operation. The Board shall choose its own officers, make its own rules
and regulations and keep a journal of its proceedings. A majority of the
members shall be a quorum for the transaction of business.
(Ord. 2003-3, passed 8-5-2003)
§ 31.31 FIRE DEPARTMENT; FIRE PROTECTION.
   (A)   (1)   Fire Department established. There is hereby established with
the municipality a department designated as the “Municipal Fire Department”.
(Prior Code, § 2-101)
      (2)   Personnel; duties of Chief.
         (a)   The Municipal Fire Department shall consist of a Chief of the
Fire Department, to be appointed by the governing body, and such other
personnel as the governing body may from time to time determine necessary.
         (b)   The duties of the Chief of the Municipal Fire Department shall
be as follows:
            1.   To direct the fighting of fires;
            2.   To have charge of, be responsible for and keep in good repair
all equipment and apparatus connected with or belonging to the Municipal Fire
Department;
            3.   To call and direct such fire drills and meetings as he or she
deems necessary for the training of persons in efficient fire fighting;
            4.   To have police authority while on duty as Fire Chief; and
            5.   To keep records of all fires and make reports of same to each
regular meeting of the governing body.
(Prior Code, § 2-102)
      (3)   Duties of volunteer members. It shall be the duty of the volunteer
members of the Municipal Fire Department to respond to all fire calls unless
prevented from so doing by unavoidable circumstances. They shall attend Fire
Department drills and meetings and obey such rules and regulations as are
established for the Municipal Fire Department.
(Prior Code, § 2-103)
   (B)   The City Council supports and endorses county-wide fire protection for
its citizens.
(Res. 2011-8, passed 9-6-2011)
CHAPTER 32: GENERAL ADMINISTRATIVE POLICIES

§ 32.01 COUNTY MULTI-HAZARD MITIGATION PLAN.
   The City Council does hereby adopt and support and will facilitate
implementation of the updated County Multi-Hazard Mitigation Plan, as deemed
appropriate.
(Res. R2020-2, passed 7-13-2020)
§ 32.02 EXCESSIVE FORCE POLICY.
   (A)   It is policy of the city that excessive force by local law enforcement
agencies shall not be used against individuals engaged in lawful and non-
violent civil rights demonstrations within the city boundaries.
   (B)   The City Council directs the Police Chief to implement this policy by
amending applicable Police Department procedures.
(Res. R 2016-7, passed 6-14-2016)
§ 32.03 NON-DISCRIMINATION ON DISABILITY BASIS.
   (A)   It is the policy of the city that all programs, services and
activities shall be accessible to, and usable by, individuals with
disabilities, in accordance with § 504 and the Americans with Disabilities Act,
being 42 U.S.C. §§ 12101 et seq. (ADA).
   (B)   The city shall conduct a self-evaluation, which should include the
assistance of a citizen review committee involving individuals with
disabilities, of its programs, policies, procedures and facilities to determine
those areas where discrimination may occur.
   (C)   The city shall, upon completion of the self-evaluation plan, make
revisions, modifications or other changes so as to fully comply with the letter
and intent of § 504 and the ADA.
   (D)   Further, the city shall, where building modifications are required,
develop and implement a transition plan for eliminating architectural barriers
in a timely manner in accordance with § 504 and the ADA.
   (E)   Citizens may contact the Clerk/Treasurer at PO Box 367, 606 Maple
Street, Nezperce ID 83543 or by phone 208-937-1021 for assistance, or to answer
questions regarding this policy during the hours of Monday through Thursday, 8:
30 a.m. to 4:00 p.m.
(Res. R-2018-1, passed 12-5-2017)
§ 32.04 FEE SCHEDULE.
   The city’s fee schedule, and any and all amendments, is hereby adopted by
reference and incorporated herein as if set out in full.
(Ord. 2005-9, passed - -2005; Res. 2009-1, passed 3-9-2009; Res. 2011-6, passed

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 50.01 INTENT.
   The maintenance of health and sanitation require, and it is the intention
hereof to make, the collection, removal and disposal of garbage, refuse and
dead animals within the city compulsory and universal.
(Prior Code, § 7-101)
§ 50.02 POWERS.
   This chapter empowers the city to issue license or franchise, exclusive or
non-exclusive, for the collection, removal and disposal of refuse from within
the city.
(Prior Code, § 7-102)
§ 50.03 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   COLLECTOR. The person holding a license or contract with the city, or
employed by the city, and thereby authorized and designated by the city, to
collect, handle, transport and dispose of refuse and wastes.
   GARBAGE. All putrescible wastes, except sewage and body waste, including
waster accumulated of animal food or vegetable matter, and including waste that
attends the preparation, use, cooking, dealing in or storing meat, fish, fowl,
fruit and vegetables and shall include all of such wastes or accumulations of
vegetable matter of residences, restaurants, hotels and places where food is
prepared for human consumption. The term GARBAGE shall not include recognized
industrial by-products.
   INSPECTOR. The authorized employee of the city or some individual designated
by the City Council as having the duty of the enforcement of this chapter.
   OWNER and OCCUPANT. May be used interchangeably, and shall mean every person
in possession, charge or in control of any dwelling, flat, rooming house or any
eating place, shop, place of business, manufacturing or business establishment
where garbage of other refuse is created or accumulated.
   PERSON. Every person, firm, partnership, association, institution and
corporation.
   REFUSE. Solid wastes, including garbage and rubbish.
   RUBBISH. Refuse other than garbage (tin cans, bottles, ashes, paper,
pasteboard, cardboard or wooden boxes, brush, leaves, weeds and cuttings from
trees, lawns, shrubs and gardens or other waste materials produced in normal
course of doing business or everyday living). The term RUBBISH shall not
include recognized industrial by-products.
   WASTE. Unwanted solid, liquid gaseous materials.
(Prior Code, § 7-103)
§ 50.04 ENFORCEMENT.
   The Chief of Police, or such persons as may be appointed by the Mayor and
Council, shall be responsible for the enforcement of the provisions of this
chapter, and other duties as the Council may prescribe, and there may be
designated as a member of the Police Department, a Sanitary Inspector and
Deputy Sanitation Inspector who shall enforce the same under the supervision of
the Chief of Police.
(Prior Code, § 7-104)
§ 50.05 COMPULSORY USE OF THE SYSTEM.
   Every owner and occupant of premises within the prescribed limits of the
city must use the refuse collection and disposal system herein provided, and
shall deposit or cause to be deposited in accordance with this chapter all
rubbish and garbage that is such nature that is perishable, or may decompose,
or may be scattered by wind or otherwise.
(Prior Code, § 7-105) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.06 BILLING AND COLLECTION FEES.
   (A)   From and after the effective date of this chapter, all fees for the
collection of garbage and refuse from within the city, including commercial as
well as residential users of the system, shall be payable to the city. Such
fees shall be carried on the city water bill, and the same shall be paid with
the water bill. The Water Department is hereby authorized to discontinue and or
all water, sanitation service to any premises if the entire, water and garbage
bill is not paid when due, said charges to become delinquent as provided for
water charges, and to be subject to the same penalties as have the same
remedies and powers of collection and enforcement as are provided in the case
of non-payment of water.
   (B)   In addition to any deposits required by existing ordinances to
guarantee payment of water charges, the city may require reasonable deposits
toward payment of sanitation charges, and the city shall have the right to off-
set any such deposit or deposits against any part of a water and garbage bill
which is past due.
   (C)   If any water or sanitation service to any premises is discontinued for
non-payment of fees, the city may refuse to resume any of such services to
those premises until the owner or occupant thereof shall have paid:
      (1)   All past due fees for water and sanitation services accrued since
the effective date of this chapter; and
      (2)   Any reasonable deposit required by the city as a guarantee for
payment of future services.
   (D)   This method of collection of fees is hereby extended to include the
costs of correcting or removing all accumulations of filth, clutter, rubbish,
garbage, refuse, waste or trash in or about public and private establishments,
all residences or premises whatsoever that is necessary to protect and preserve
the health, welfare, morals and safety and cleanliness of the municipality. In
the case of extensive or costly correction or removal, the city may use any
other method for recovery of the cost of correcting or removing these nuisances
that is allowed by law, plus penalties for violations as herein provided.
(Prior Code, § 7-106)
COLLECTION AND RECEPTACLES
§ 50.20 REFUSE COLLECTION.
   There is hereby established a system of refuse collection, transportation
and disposal. It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of
collecting, transporting, hauling or conveying any refuse over the street of
alleys, or to dump or dispose of the same, unless and until such person is
licensed therefor, or has a contract or franchise therefore as herein provided.
(Prior Code, § 7-107) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.21 REFUSE ACCUMULATION UNLAWFUL.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or to suffer to accumulate in
or about any yard, lot, place or premises, or upon any street, alley or
sidewalk adjacent to such lot, yard, lot, premises or the street, alley or
sidewalk adjacent thereto, to be or remain in such condition as to cause or
create a nuisance or offensive odor or atmosphere or rodent harborage, or
thereby to be or to become, or cause or create, a public nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 7-108) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.22 BURNING AND DUMPING.
   No person shall burn, incinerate, bury, dump, collect, remove or in any
other manner dispose of rubbish or garbage, except as hereinafter; provided:
   (A)   Interior incinerator. Any person may use an incinerator in the
interior of a building between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 7:00 p.m.; provided,
such incinerator meets the requirements of the Building Code;
   (B)   Exterior incinerator. Burning rubbish will be allowed in exterior
incinerators between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m.; such incinerators
shall be built of non-combustible material and shall be covered by one-half
inch wire mesh screen. In no event shall garbage be burned;
   (C)   Open burning. Burning of rubbish may be done on vacant lots by the
owner thereof upon obtaining a permit from the Fire Department for such
burning; and
   (D)   Disposal of ashes. The ashes from approved burning barrels or home
incinerators shall be removed from said barrels or home incinerators and placed
in garbage cans or suitable containers before requesting a collector to pick-up
these ashes. No glowing coals or smoldering material shall be left for
collecting unless the collector is notified of its condition by the patron and
the collector accepts the material for disposal.
(Prior Code, § 7-109) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.23 LITTERING.
   No person shall throw, discard or deposit any rubbish, garbage, refuse,
debris, trash, lighted material or other waste substances on an private or
public property, unless authorized to do so by the owner or person in charge of
such property.
(Prior Code, § 7-110) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.24 REFUSE CONTAINERS.
   It shall be the duty of every owner or occupant of any place where garbage
or rubbish is created or accumulated to at all times keep or cause to be kept
portable approved containers for the deposit therein or rubbish and garbage and
except as otherwise provided, to deposit or cause to be deposited all rubbish
and garbage therein. All garbage shall, before deposit in such can, be wrapped
in rodent- and fly-proof, shall be equipped with handles and a close-fitting
lid. Such containers shall be not less than ten gallons’ capacity, nor more
than 32 gallons’ capacity. The combined weight of any refuse container and its
contents shall not exceed 75 pounds. All metal containers shall be of not less
than 28-gauge metal or the equivalent, and be hot-dipped and fabricated to
assure non-locking cans. All other containers must be guaranteed by the
manufacturer and so labeled to be leak-proof regardless of manufacturing
process. Such lid shall not be removed, except when necessary to place garbage
and rubbish in such container or to take the same therefrom. Whenever garbage
or rubbish is placed therein or taken therefrom, such lid shall be replaced by
the person placing therein or taking therefrom such garbage or rubbish. Such
containers shall be kept in sanitary condition, with the inside and outside
thereof washed at such times as to keep the same free and clean of all
accumulating grease and decomposing material and so that no odor nuisance shall
exist. All garbage or refuse cans shall be placed in a place accessible or
places to the collector; provided that, in the case of isolated dwellings or
places of business or where reasonable access cannot be had by a truck, the
cans may be kept in such places as may be designated by the Inspector. Where
there is no alley entrance, such cans shall be placed adjacent to street curb
on collection days.
(Prior Code, § 7-111) Penalty, see §
50.99
§ 50.25 COLLECTION PERIOD.
   Collectors shall collect rubbish and garbage from each customer’s residence
at least once a week on a regularly scheduled day; provided, however, where the
collection of garbage and refuse on the established schedules would be
impracticable because of unusual or exceptional circumstances, the Council may
issue a special permit altering the time and extent of collections. The
frequency and manner of commercial collections shall be governed by each
commercial customer’s usual needs and circumstances, and these shall be
established by agreement between the customer and the collector.
(Prior Code, § 7-112)
§ 50.26 RUBBISH, SPECIAL HANDLING.
   Rubbish consisting only of cardboard, or wooden boxes, leaves, weeds and
cuttings from trees, lawns, shrubs and gardens may be kept separately without
depositing in such containers; providing that, the bulk materials, such as
leaves, shall be in a can, box, sack or receptacle for ease of loading, and
that brush or any bulky material shall be tied in bundles not to exceed four
feet in length and not to exceed 75 pounds in weight. Compost piles may be
maintained for fertilizations purposes, and matter used for the same shall not
constitute a nuisance. Nothing in this section shall be construed so as to
permit the violation of any rule or regulation of the Fire Department.
(Prior Code, § 7-113)
§ 50.27 COLLECTION: BUSINESS, HOUSES.
   To ensure the health of the inhabitants of the city, the Council hereby does
ordain that premises and businesses, such as, but not limited to, restaurants,
grocery stores, hospitals, butcher shops and establishments wherein large
accumulations of garbage occur, and are nuisances to the extent that the same
should by, and are hereby in the manner and method hereinafter provided,
designated as separate class of premises for the collection and disposal of
garbage and rubbish and the same shall be deposited separately in suitable cans
and containers. The Inspector shall designate such premises wherein large
accumulations of garbage occur and shall notify the owner of such premises or
such designation. From and after such notification by the Inspector, all
rubbish and garbage accumulated upon said premises shall be deposited
separately, in containers from garbage as approved by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 7-114)
§ 50.28 COLLECTION FEES.
   (A)   Fees and rates for the collection of garbage and refuse shall be set
by rules and regulations of the Council.
   (B)   The following fees are hereby established.
      (1)   Minimum charge. For all residential users of the system, a minimum
monthly fee of $25.72 shall be effective 10-1-2007. The minimum monthly fee for
commercial tote containers shall be $37, effective on the same date. The fee
shall entitle the user to one pick-up per week of a maximum of a 90-gallon tote
containers and commercial fees shall be increased by the same percentage (i.e.,
5%). Commercial users shall pay an administrative fee to the city of the lesser
of 10% of the monthly refuse billing or $5.75.
      (2)   Additional hauls. For each additional pick-up or haul per week, the
above minimum fee will be charged.
      (3)   Additional cans. For each additional can, bundle, box or other
container over the limit, there shall be a monthly charge of $0.75 in
residential and apartment hose pick-ups.
      (4)   Apartment billings. Billings for collections from apartments shall
be made to the same persons as the billings for water services to such
properties.
      (5)   Commercial collections. Rates and schedules for collections from
commercial premises may vary from the above established rates, depending upon
particular requirements and circumstances. For such commercial accounts wherein
the above rates do not apply, the collector shall file with the City Clerk/
Treasurer a copy of the monthly rate pr amount agreed upon by each such
commercial user and the collector. It shall be the collector’s responsibility
to furnish the City Clerk/Treasurer each month, on or before a date fixed by
the Clerk/Treasurer, with a statement of any additions and revisions to the
regular monthly charges of any customer. The city shall not be held responsible
for the failure to collect any amounts or accounts not timely furnished in
writing to the City Clerk/Treasurer in this manner. In the event the collector
and a commercial customer, either may refer the problem to the city and the
City Council shall be the final arbiter of the rate to be charged.
      (6)   Job work. The collector herein referred to shall be allowed to
enter into separate contract with patrons, outside the scope of this chapter,
under which hauling, pickups and similar work would be governed, but, the
charges imposed for the same by the collector are a matter of contract between
the patron and collector, and the city assumes no responsibility for collection
of funds under such arrangements.
      (7)   Vacation. Any premises not occupied for a full calendar month shall
not be required to pay for said sanitation service during said period, but such
persons wishing to take the advantage of this section must inform the office of
Clerk/Treasurer of the city in advance.
      (8)   Minimum refuse.
         (a)   Minimum refuse when any single person, being the occupant of a
dwelling or any married couple living primarily on Social Security or public
assistance income has refuse of such small amounts as not to require normal
pick-up collection thereof and requiring only one pick-up per month consisting
of one 32-gallon container containing only rubbish as defined herein the same
shall be picked up by the collector on the first collection day of each month
and the monthly charge shall be $1.50.
         (b)   Such container must be clearly marked by a red-painted lid so as
to be easily identifiable by the collector.
         (c)   Any persons wishing to take advantage of this section must
appear before the Council at a regular meeting and be approved in advance.
(Prior Code, § 7-115) (Ord. 2007-2, passed 9-6-2007; Res. 2017-1, passed 10-11-
2016; Res. 2022-11, passed 8-22-2022)
§ 50.29 EQUIPMENT.
   For the collection of garbage and refuse, every collector shall use a
suitable covered or enclosed truck approved by the Inspector and meeting all
other requirements, regulations, ordinances and laws of the state, its
departments or other governmental units.
(Prior Code, § 7-116)
§ 50.30 LICENSING AND CONTRACTING.
   The Mayor and Council shall be the sole authority to license, contract for
or to otherwise provide for all services pertaining to sanitary collection and
disposal within the city, let bids for, or establish reasonable fees for
licenses or franchises and is hereby authorized to enter into contracts with
one or more contractors, and establish reasonable rules ad regulations
governing the conduct and operation of such licensees or contractors. The
Council may require of any licensee of contractor a bond in a reasonable
amount, the condition of which shall be satisfactory performance of the
contract.
(Prior Code, § 7-117)
§ 50.31 MATERIALS NOT ACCEPTABLE FOR COLLECTION.
   Dirt and debris from construction or lawn renovation, rocks, stones,
concrete, automobile bodies and parts, dead animals, building materials such as
masonry, plaster, scrap lumber and similar materials, are not acceptable for
collection and the collector is not required to pick up same. Such items shall
be collected and disposed of by the building contractor, owner or occupant of
the premises.
(Prior Code, § 7-118)
§ 50.99 PENALTY.
   Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be guilty
of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined as set forth in §
10.99 or imprisonment for a term not exceeding 30 days, or both, in the
discretion of the Court.
(Prior Code, § 7-119)
