GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 91.01 WEEDS.
   (A)   All owners or occupants of any lot, block or subdivision of land are
hereby required to cut and remove all weeds there from. The said persons shall
also remove all weeds up to the center of the street or alley, along, in front
of or abutting said premises and to keep the same free from weeds.
   (B)   WEEDS, within the meaning of this section, includes all vegetable
growth that is unsightly, troublesome, useless or noxious.
   (C)   All weeds and vegetable growth that has been declared noxious,
destructive or detrimental to the agricultural interests shall be completely
and effectually destroyed. It shall be sufficient compliance with this section
if all other kinds not so declared noxious are kept closely cut to the ground.
   (D)   Whenever the growth of weeds advances to or becomes in a condition
prohibited by this section, the municipality or any of its officers shall
notify such owner or occupant to remove such growth and in default of this
being done, said municipality shall remove such growth and in default of this
being done, said municipality shall remove and cut such weeds or do any other
work necessary to place said premises in good condition. The Clerk/Treasurer
shall then certify the cost of the same and the cost therein occurred shall be
a lien upon the property.
(Prior Code, § 7-201) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.02 ABANDONED ICE BOXES, REFRIGERATORS AND CONTAINERS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to leave or permit to remain outside of
any dwelling, building or other structure, or within any unoccupied or
abandoned building, dwelling or other structure under his, her or its control,
in a place accessible to children, any abandoned, unattended or discarded ice
box, refrigerator or other container which has a door or lid, snap lock or
other locking device which may not be released from the inside, without first
removing said door or lid, snap lock or other locking device or by first
fastening, bolting or locking the same in such manner that it is impossible to
open the same by the use of the hands.
(Prior Code, § 6-401) Penalty, see §
91.99
NUISANCES
§ 91.15 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   ABANDONED. To have a motor vehicle on private property without the
permission of the person having rights to the possession of the property or on
a public street or other property open to the public for the purposes of
vehicular traffic or parking, or upon or within the right-of-way of any road or
highway, for 48 hours or longer.
   AUTOMOTIVE HOBBY PROJECT. A non-commercial accessory use involving the
restoration, maintenance and/or preservation of motor vehicles taking place
exclusively on residential private property within the city limits.
   AUTOMOTIVE HOBBY SITE. Any privately-owned real property upon which the
resident is restoring, maintaining and/or preserving one or more motor
vehicles.
   CONTAINER. A garbage can, dumpster or any other kind of storage device
customarily sold, rented, constructed or utilized for use as for temporary
storage of waste matter and lawfully located on the property in question
   FRONT YARD. All property, including driveways and entrance ways extending
between side lot lines across the frontage of a lot adjoining a public street
other than an alley, and from any side of the principal building.
   HAZARDOUS WASTE.
      (1)   Any “hazardous waste” as defined by the Resource Conservation and
Recovery Act of 1976 (42 U.S.C. §§ 6901 et seq.), as amended from time to time,
and regulations promulgated thereunder;
      (2)   Any “hazardous substance” as defined by the Comprehensive
Environmental Response, Compensation and Liability Act of 1980 (42 U.S.C. §§
9601 et seq.), as amended from time to time, and regulations promulgated
thereunder;
      (3)   Radon and material quantities of petroleum products;
      (4)   Any substance the presence of which on the property is regulated by
any federal, state or local law relating to the protection of the environment
or public health; and
      (5)   Any other substance which by law requires special handling in its
collection, storage, treatment or disposal.
   HIGHWAY. A way or place of whatever nature, publicly maintained and open to
the use of the public for purposes of vehicular travel or parking. HIGHWAY
includes street or alley. HIGHWAY does not include those portions of said way
or place which are not utilized for vehicular travel, such as those portions of
aprons, setbacks, easements, rights-of-way or property owned by the public
which extend beyond the surface area normally used for vehicular travel or
parking. Said areas are to be considered public property for purposes of this
subchapter.
   INOPERATIVE VEHICLE. Any vehicle which, in its current state, whether due to
broken, defective or missing parts, including missing or flat tires, missing
doors, missing or badly damaged windshields, or broken or defective parts which
are essential for movement, is not capable of being used as a regular means of
transportation.
   PUBLIC PROPERTY. All property owned by the public. PUBLIC PROPERTY does not
include a highway.
   REAR YARD. A yard extending between side lot lines across the rear of a lot
opposite the side(s) of a building which fronts upon a public street and from
the rear lot line to the principal building.
   UNAUTHORIZED VEHICLE. Any thing other than a lawfully registered motor
vehicle and its lawfully connected trailer, including, but not limited to, the
following: any snowmobile, any boat, any trailer which is not connected by
means of a lawful hitch to an operating, lawfully registered motor vehicle, any
camper shell or camper not mounted on a vehicle, any storage containers,
excluding city authorized garbage containers when located in conformance with
city regulations, any vehicle reported stolen and not yet recovered, and any
recreational vehicle which remains parked on a street longer than authorized in
this code.
   UNREGISTERED VEHICLE. Any vehicle which is not lawfully and currently
registered as provided in Idaho Code Title 49, Chapter 4; or any vehicle which
does not bear current annual Idaho license plates or decals; or any vehicle
which does not bear current license plates issued by another state and is not
lawfully and currently registered in that state.
      (1)   The parking, both short term and long term, of lawfully registered,
operative motor vehicles is allowed at curb side area of the streets of the
city; provided that, the motor vehicles are not parked in violation of pavement
or curb markings or regulatory signs or traffic devices; and, provided that,
they are parked in conformance with parking method regulations set out
elsewhere in this code.
      (2)   The use of the streets as a storage location for unregistered or
inoperative, motor vehicles, unauthorized items such as camper shells, boats,
unhitched trailers, storage containers or other materials is prohibited and the
owner(s) may be issued a misdemeanor citation for violating the prohibition.
The continued presence of such unlawfully stored items is inimical to the well-
being of the citizens and is hereby declared a public nuisance. All such items
shall be subject to removal as provided hereinafter, the costs of which shall
be borne by the owner(s).
   VEHICLE. A device by which any person or properly may be propelled, moved or
drawn, whether or not utilized solely upon a highway, except a device moved
solely by human power or used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks,
whether or not in a condition capable of operation or use.
   WASTE MATTER.
      (1)   Any kind of liquid or solid waste, hazardous waste, manufactured
good, appliance, fixture, furniture, machinery, vehicle, personal property or
any other thing or part thereof, whether of value or valueless, that is
demolished, discarded, dismantled, partially dismantled, dilapidated or so
worn, deteriorated, or is such a condition as to be generally unusable and or
inoperable in its existing state.
      (2)   This shall include by way of illustration only and without
limitation: trash or refuse of any kind; litter; commercial waste; industrial
or construction or demolition debris of any kind, such as rubble, broken
asphalt and concrete; crates; cartons; metal; glass; appliances or appliance
shells; boat bodies and parts; used tires; vehicle bodies and parts; commercial
or industrial equipment bodies and parts; snowmobile bodies and parts; trailers
and parts; recreational vehicle bodies and parts; mobile home and manufactured
home bodies and parts; and inoperable or damaged vehicles of any kind; and any
kind of tangible personal property or fixtures.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011)
§ 91.16 NUISANCE DECLARED.
   Pursuant to the authority granted by Idaho Code § 50-334 and correlated
other provisions, the City Council makes the following findings and
declarations.
   (A)   The accumulation and storage of waste matter on private or public
property is found to create a condition tending to reduce the value of
surrounding private property, to promote blight and deterioration and to invite
plundering, to create fire hazards, to constitute an unattractive nuisance
creating a hazard to the health and safety of minors, to create a harborage for
rodents and insects and to be injurious to the health, safety and general
welfare of entire neighborhoods and/or a significant number of persons.
   (B)   Unscreened exterior areas may be inspected at any time from a public
right-of-way with or without the involvement of the owner or occupant in
accordance with legal requirements governing administrative inspections of
private property.
   (C)   Screened exterior areas shall be inspected only during the normal
business hours of the city unless otherwise arranged, and only upon invitation
or with the concurrence of the owner or occupant or when authorized/ordered by
a court.
   (D)   Except in cases of alleged imminent hazards, if the occupant is not
the owner of the premises or dwelling unit to be inspected, the Building
Official, his or her designated representative, Code Enforcement Officer,
police officer or any authorized representative thereof shall provide notice in
writing or by telephone to the owner or designated agent as to the time and
place of inspection. The owner or designated agent may be present for the
inspection. The convenience of the owner or designated agent shall not require
the rescheduling of the inspection.
   (E)   Therefore, the presence of the following on private or public
property, unless expressly permitted herein, is declared to constitute a public
nuisance and is prohibited, and may be abated as such in accordance with the
provisions of this chapter:
      (1)   An unlicensed, abandoned, wrecked, dismantled or inoperative
vehicle, or part thereof, on private or public property, except as expressly
hereinafter permitted. However, abandoned vehicles shall be dealt with as
prescribed by Idaho Code §§ 49-1801 et seq.;
      (2)   An uncovered container holding waste matter; or such a container
with a cover which is not secure against dogs, unless said container of a type
that is not normally covered, such as compost bins, or sludge drying bins;
      (3)   Waste matter not in a container;
      (4)   Waste matter stored in such fashion that it or any of it may enter
the waters of a stream or river, directly or indirectly, or come to be in
contact with such waters;
      (5)   Waste matter or dry or dead vegetative matter so located as to
constitute a fire hazard to buildings or lands, and vegetative matter which
will in the ordinary course become such a hazard, but not hay or other
agricultural product stored in a fashion customary on farms in the community
and in accord with the applicable fire codes adopted by the city; and
      (6)   Waste matter or one or more containers which, by reason of its or
their location and character, is unsightly and interferes with the reasonable
enjoyment of adjacent or nearby property.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.17 PROHIBITED CONDUCT.
   In addition to the above, the following conduct is hereby prohibited:
   (A)   To willfully cause or permit any vehicle to be used for the
transportation of waste to be so loaded or in such condition or so uncovered
that waste matter escapes from the vehicle while being driven;
   (B)   To willfully discharge waste matter onto the surface of the earth
other than into a container or beneath the surface of the earth, or into any
stream, river or other waterbody;
   (C)   To willfully cause or allow a nuisance or permit a nuisance to
continue, on property in the possession of the offender or on any abutting
street, sidewalk or right-of-way. Any entity or person who, upon receiving
notice of the existence of a nuisance as described in the abatement procedure
set forth herein, who fails to remedy the same within the time established in
said abatement procedure, shall be deemed to have willfully allowed or
permitted a nuisance to continue;
   (D)   To allow grass to exceed six inches in height and weeds and other
growth to exceed 12 inches in height; or
   (E)   To willfully violate any other provision or requirement of this
subchapter or to fail to comply with any order issued pursuant to the
provisions of this subchapter.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.18 AUTOMOTIVE HOBBY PROJECT.
   (A)   It is the intent of this section to provide standards for the
restoration, maintenance and/or preservation of personal motor vehicles
conducted as a hobby and conducted at a person’s residence or upon private
property.
   (B)   (1)   Automotive hobby projects may only be conducted on residential
property, and only as a non-commercial project. No commercial, retail or
wholesale sales of automobiles, or automotive parts or supplies, shall be
conducted upon a site claiming lawful use as an automotive hobby project. No
restoration, repair or maintenance of motor vehicles shall be conducted upon
any residential site for which monetary compensation is received.
      (2)   All automotive hobby sites shall be maintained in a safe and
orderly manner so as not to create a public nuisance, an unsightly condition,
an undesirable condition, a health or fire hazard.
      (3)   No automotive hobby sites may contain more than four inoperable
dismantled or unregistered vehicles which constitute an automotive hobby
project. No automotive hobby projects may be stored in the front yard of any
lot. All automotive hobby sites must be located in the rear yard of any lot. If
any automotive hobby site contains more than two automotive hobby projects,
said projects must be screened from view so that it or they are not visible at
a distance of six feet observed from the property lines of adjacent properties,
by a sight-obscuring fence of not less than, nor more than six feet in height
or a hedge of not less than six feet in height.
      (4)   The restrictions set forth in this subchapter do not apply to those
automobiles stored inside of a fully-enclosed building. Further, the
restrictions set forth in this subchapter do not apply to duly registered and
licensed vehicles which are inoperable, but upon which repair is being
conducted, but only so long as said repair is conducted and completed within 60
days of the vehicle becoming inoperable. Automobiles being repaired may only be
stored or parked in improved parking areas or driveways and shall not be stored
or parked in any front yard of a residential site.
      (5)   Any motor vehicle restoration, preservation, maintenance or repair
hobby operation involving welding, painting or use of flammable liquids shall
be conduced in a safe, prudent and lawful manner.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.19 COMMERCIAL ENTERPRISES.
   No person or entity operating any commercial enterprise within the city
shall cause, allow or permit waste matter to be present upon the property being
utilized unless within a fully enclosed structure.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.20 ENFORCEMENT; RIGHT OF ENTRY; REMOVAL.
   (A)   It shall be the right of the Fire Chief or other officer or person,
designated by the Mayor of the city to inspect properties, investigate
complaints and determine whether or not a nuisance exists in accordance with
the terms of this subchapter. The Fire Chief, or such other designated officer
or person, his or her designated agent, shall be authorized to enter upon
private property or public property to investigate, remove or cause the removal
of a vehicle or parts thereof declared to be a nuisance pursuant to this
subchapter.
   (B)   The Sheriff’s Department is authorized to cause the immediate removal
of any unregistered or unauthorized vehicle, any unauthorized materials or any
vehicle reported as stolen and not yet recovered found parked or left on any
street or right-of-way. The Department is also authorized to cause to be
removed any vehicle parked on the right-of-way which is found to be
inoperative, pursuant to notification and removal procedures set forth in Idaho
Code Title 49, Chapter 18; provided, however, that, upon notification to the
Sheriff’s Department that a motor vehicle has become disabled while being
operated, such inoperative vehicle may be left parked against the curb area of
a public right-of-way for a period not to exceed 48 hours for effecting repairs
or arranging for removal.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011)
§ 91.21 ABATEMENT PROCEDURE.
   The procedure described in §§
91.22 and
91.23 of this chapter shall apply for the abatement of public nuisances other
than dangerous buildings. Regardless of the exercise of any enforcement remedy
contained in this subchapter, the city shall have the right of abatement with
respect to any public nuisance. The exercise of the right of abatement or any
procedures described below shall not be a prerequisite to exercise of any other
remedies or enforcement of the criminal provisions contained in this
subchapter.
   (A)   Abandoned vehicle. The procedures and requirements of Idaho Code §§
49-1801 et seq., or its successor provisions shall apply to all abandoned
vehicles or vehicles which constitute waste matter, or vehicles being kept,
maintained or stored in violation of the provisions of this subchapter, whether
located upon highways, public property or private property.
   (B)   Other nuisances. The abatement procedure in §§
91.22 and
91.23 of this chapter shall apply to all other nuisances.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011)
§ 91.22 WRITTEN DECLARATION.
   (A)   A nuisance may be declared by the Fire Chief or other person or
officer designated by the Mayor of the city, who, upon identification of a
nuisance, shall cause a written declaration to be issued, by mailing the same
to the last registered owner(s) of the real property upon which he or she
determines a nuisance is present, as reflected on the tax assessment roles of
the county and by posting the same in a conspicuous place on the real property
on which the nuisance is located. Each notice that is mailed shall be sent by
certified mail, return receipt requested. Notice shall be deemed to have been
provided upon mailing. Every person entitled to notice of the declaration of
nuisance shall have 30 days to remove or remedy the condition creating the
nuisance, or to request a public hearing as described below. Every notice of
declaration of nuisance shall contain the following:
      (1)   A descriptive statement of the nuisance which is declared to exist;
      (2)   Its location;
      (3)   The name of the person or persons thought to be responsible;
      (4)   A statement of a date, not less than 30 days after the mailing of
such notice, which shall be the last date on which the addressee or other
claimant of the affected property or offending objects can demand a hearing, or
cause removal or remedy of the nuisance described;
      (5)   A statement that such hearing would be for the purpose of
determining anew whether the nuisance exists;
      (6)   Directions for the mailing of such a demand for hearing to the City
Clerk/Treasurer; and
      (7)   A statement that if no hearing is demanded, or if the result of the
hearing is to the effect that a nuisance exists, the owner or other addressee
will have 30 days to commence and thereafter diligently to pursue and complete
the abatement. Also, the owner will be assessed the costs of the abatement
action against the property in like fashion as for tax assessments.
   (B)   Failure to request a public hearing within the time required shall be
deemed conclusive as to the existence of the nuisance as described in the
declaration posted and mailed.
   (C)   Upon receipt of a request for a public hearing, the Mayor shall
establish a date for a public hearing, to be held no less than ten days, nor
more than 30 days from receipt of said request. The public hearing shall be to
determine if a nuisance exists, and assessment of administrative costs for the
abatement action, and directions for removal or remedy.
      (1)   Notice of said hearing shall be provided by certified mail to any
person or entity requesting a public hearing, to the last registered owner of
the real property upon which the Fire Chief, or other official or person
designated by the Mayor, has determined a nuisance is present. Notice shall be
deemed completed upon mailing.
      (2)   The City Council shall hear all facts and testimony deemed
pertinent. The facts and testimony may include testimony, pictures, videos and
the like on the condition of the property, vehicles, waste matter or any other
evidence regarding the existence of a nuisance. The City Council shall not be
limited by the technical rules of evidence. The owner of the land on which the
alleged nuisance is located may appear in person at the hearing or present a
written statement in time for consideration at the hearing and deny
responsibility for the presence of the nuisance with his or her reasons for
such denial.
      (3)   The City Council, upon a finding that a public nuisance exists, may
impose such conditions and take such action as deemed appropriate under the
circumstances to carry out the purpose of the subchapter, including delaying
the time for removal or remedy of the nuisance or part thereof if, in its
opinion, the circumstances justify it. At the conclusion of the public hearing,
the City Council must make written findings of fact and conclusions of law, and
may order the nuisance remedied or removed from the property as a public
nuisance and disposed of as hereinafter provided and determine the
administrative costs to be charged against the owner of the parcel of land on
which the nuisance is located. The order requiring removal shall include:
         (a)   A description of the nuisance or part thereof and the correct
identification number and license number of any vehicle constituting a part, or
all, of the nuisance, if available, at the site; and
         (b)   A statement that the nuisance must be removed or remedied within
30 days of adoption of the order, unless some other time period is specified by
the City Council.
      (4)   If an interested party makes a written presentation to the City
Council, but does not appear, he or she shall be notified in writing of the
decision.
   (D)   Upon the expiration of 30 days after mailing of a declaration of
nuisance if no hearing is requested, or the later of 30 days after adoption of
the order declaring a condition to be a public nuisance, or 30 days from the
date of mailing of notice of the decision to an interested person who makes a
written presentation if such notice is required by this section, or the date
specified in the order if a date is specified, if the nuisance remains in whole
or in part, the Fire Chief or other officer or person appointed by the Mayor,
shall take steps to cause the abatement of the nuisance by removal of the
offending materials, whether by fire suppression exercise, by use of city
employees, or by letting an appropriate contract in accord with the contracting
procedures of the city. The waste matter which constitutes the public nuisance
may be disposed of by removal to a garbage transfer station, dump, scrap yard
or automobile dismantler’s yard or to any other similar facility.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011)
§ 91.23 REMOVAL COST ASSESSMENT.
   The cost of abatement, together with the administrative costs, shall be
calculated and assessed. If such amount is not paid within 30 days of the date
of abatement, the same shall become a lien upon the property pursuant to Idaho
Code §§ 50-334 and 50-1008, and shall be transmitted to the tax collector for
collection. The assessment shall have the same priority as other city taxes.
The city shall also be entitled to recover said costs in a civil action brought
by the city, and assess the same as additional penalties in a misdemeanor
prosecution.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011)
§ 91.24 ALTERNATIVE PROVISION.
   This subchapter is not the exclusive regulation of public nuisances, or the
exclusive regulation of abandoned, wrecked, dismantled or inoperative vehicles
within the city. It shall supplement and be in addition to the other regulatory
codes, statutes and ordinances heretofore or hereafter enacted by the city, the
state or any other legal entity or agency having jurisdiction.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011)
§ 91.25 EXTENT.
   The abatement of nuisances under the provisions of this subchapter shall
apply only to the corporate boundaries of the city. The city shall not extend
its authority under Idaho Code § 50-334 beyond the boundaries of the city
limits.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011)
§ 91.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   (1)   Any owner, occupant, lessor, lessee, manager or other person
having lawful control over a structure or parcel of land who causes, allows,
facilitates, aids or abets any violation of any provision of §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter or who fails to perform any act or duty required by §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter or who allows a lessee or a tenant to violate §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. Each day any violation
of any provision of §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter or the failure to perform any act or duty required by §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter exists shall constitute a separate violation.
      (2)   The owner of record, as recorded in the records of the county, of
the property upon which a violation of §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter exists shall be presumed to be the person having lawful
control over a structure or parcel of land. If more than one person shall be
recorded as the owner of the property, said persons shall be jointly and
severally presumed to be persons having lawful control over a structure or
parcel of land. This presumption shall not prevent enforcement of the
provisions of §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter against any person specified elsewhere in §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter.
      (3)   It shall not be a defense for an owner of record to plead that any
act or omission made punishable by §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter was at the time the violation occurred within the control
of a lessee or tenant pursuant to a lease or rental agreement.
      (4)   If the Mayor determines that action by the city is required to
protect the public health, safety and welfare in an area affected by a
violation of §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter, the Mayor may direct that employees of the city, or the
city’s contractors or agents, go upon the premises in question and remove,
abate or destroy the problem. The city shall be entitled to recover its expense
by civil action filed in a court of competent jurisdiction, together with costs
and a reasonable attorney’s fee. The expense may also be certified to the City
Clerk/Treasurer and transmitted to the County Treasurer, and be collected by
special assessment upon the property to the extent provided by law pursuant to
Idaho Code §§ 50-334 and 50-1008. If the certificate is recorded at the office
of the County Recorder, it shall become a lien against the property to the
extent provided by law.
      (5)   Prosecution of an offense, under this division (B), shall not
preclude the city from seeking a civil remedy for failure to comply with §§
91.15 through
91.25 of this chapter.
(Ord. 2011-3, passed 6-7-2011)
CHAPTER 92: FAIR HOUSING; NON-DISCRIMINATION
Section
Fair Housing
   
92.01   Policy
   
92.02   Assistance from city

Non-Discrimination
   
92.15   City policy

FAIR HOUSING
§ 92.01 POLICY.
   (A)   Discrimination on the basis of race, color, religion, gender or
national origin in the sale, rental, leasing or financing of housing or land to
be used for construction of housing or in the provision of brokerage services
is prohibited by Title VIII of the 1968 Civil Rights Act, being 42 U.S.C. §§
3601 to 3619 (Federal Fair Housing Law).
   (B)   It is the policy of the city to encourage equal opportunity in housing
for all persons regardless of race, color, religion, gender or national origin.
   (C)   The Fair Housing Amendments Act of 1988, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 3601 et
seq. expands coverage to include disabled persons and families with children.
   (D)   The city’s Title VI Plan, which includes the city’s Limited English
Proficiency Plan is hereby approved by the Mayor and City Council. A full copy
of the Plan is adopted by reference as if set in full herein. A full copy of
this Plan can be found in the city offices.
(Res. R2021-2, passed - -2021; Res. R-2024-08, passed 7-8-2024)
§ 92.02 ASSISTANCE FROM CITY.
   Within available resources, the city will assist all persons who feel they
have been discriminated against because of race, color, religion, gender,
national origin, disability or familial status to seek equity under federal and
state laws by referring them to the U.S. Department of Housing and Urban
Development, Office of Fair Housing and Equal Opportunity, Compliance Division.
(Res. R2021-2, passed - -2021)
§ 92.03 PUBLICITY OF POLICY.
   The city shall publicize this policy and, through this publicity, shall
encourage owners of real estate, developers and builders to become aware of
their respective responsibilities and rights under the Federal Fair Housing Law
and amendments and any applicable state or local laws or ordinances.
(Res. R2021-2, passed - -2021)
§ 92.04 MINIMUM REQUIREMENTS.
   Said program will, at a minimum, include:
   (A)   Publicizing this policy;
   (B)   Posting applicable fair housing information in prominent public areas;
   (C)   Providing fair housing information to the public;
   (D)   Preparing a fair housing assessment; and
   (E)   Declaring April as “Fair Housing Month”.
(Res. R2021-2, passed - -2021)
NON-DISCRIMINATION
§ 92.15 CITY POLICY.
   It is the policy of the city that all programs, services and activities
shall be accessible to, and usable by, individuals with disabilities, in
accordance with § 504 and the Americans with Disabilities Act, being 42 U.S.C.
§§ 12101 et seq. (ADA).
(Res. R-2018-1, passed 12-5-2017)
§ 92.16 CITY EVALUATION.
   (A)   The city shall conduct a self-evaluation, which should include the
assistance of a citizen review committee involving individuals with
disabilities, of its programs, policies, procedures and facilities to determine
those areas where discrimination may occur.
   (B)   The city shall, upon completion of the self-evaluation plan, make
revisions, modifications or other changes so as to fully comply with the letter
and intent of § 504 and the ADA, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 12101 et seq.
(Res. R-2018-1, passed 12-5-2017)
§ 92.17 TRANSITION PLAN FOR BUILDING MODIFICATION.
   Further, the city shall, where building modifications are required, develop
and implement a transition plan for eliminating architectural barriers in a
timely manner in accordance with § 504 and the ADA, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 12101 et
seq.
(Res. R-2018-1, passed 12-5-2017)
§ 92.18 CONTACT INFORMATION.
   Citizens may contact the Clerk/Treasurer at P.O. Box 367, 502 5th Avenue,
Nezperce ID 83543. The phone number is 208-937-1021, for assistance or to
answer questions regarding this policy during the hours of Monday through
Thursday, 8:30 a.m. to 4:00 p.m.
(Res. R-2018-1, passed 12-5-2017)

CHAPTER 110: ADVERTISING AND BILL POSTING
Section
   
110.01   License required

110.05   Billboards
§ 110.01 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   No person shall engage in the distribution or attaching of any signs, bills,
pictures or advertising matter unless the person shall first have been
licensed.
(Prior Code, § 4-101) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.02 LICENSE APPLICATION.
   (A)   Application for a license shall be made to the Clerk/Treasurer,
together with all necessary information, including, but not limited to, the
names of all owners and the business addresses of the same.
   (B)   Upon approval of said application by the governing body, the Clerk/
Treasurer shall issue a license.
(Prior Code, § 4-102)
§ 110.03 LITTERING STREETS, ALLEYS WITH POSTERS.
   No person shall scatter or throw upon the public thoroughfares any
handbills, posters, advertisements or papers. Nothing herein shall be construed
to authorize any person to obstruct the public thoroughfares or create any
nuisance therein. These provisions shall not interfere or prevent the posting
of notices required by law to be posted.
(Prior Code, § 4-103) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.04 POSTING ON FENCES, POLES PROHIBITED; CONSENT.
   No person shall post, paint, tack or otherwise attach any notice or other
advertising matter to any fence, wall or building or other property until first
obtaining the consent of the owner of such property. No person shall post,
paint, tack or otherwise attach any notices or advertising matter to any of the
telegraph, telephone, electric or other such poles.
(Prior Code, § 4-104) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 110.05 BILLBOARDS.
   All billboards or signboards shall conform to the following requirements.
   (A)   The clear posting or painting space on any billboard or signboard
erected upon uprights or other supports extending into the ground shall not be
of flammable material, such as wood or cloth. All posts used shall not be less
that four by six inches and not be placed more that eight feet apart and extend
to the top of the billboard or signboard. There shall not be less that one
brace and one anchor to each post. All anchors shall not be less than six by
six inches in size. Each brace shall extend from each post to its corresponding
anchor post and be not less than two by six inches in size.
   (B)   There shall be maintained in the conspicuous place on every billboard
or signboard, in printed letters, the name of the person owning or in charge
thereof.
   (C)   Every billboard or signboard, whether now or hereafter erected shall
be securely built, firmly anchored and maintained in a safe and sanitary
condition.
(Prior Code, § 4-105) Penalty, see §
10.99

111.27   License expiration
PEDDLERS
§ 111.01 UNINVITED PEDDLERS DECLARED A NUISANCE.
   The practice of going in and upon private residences in the municipality by
solicitors, peddlers, hawkers, itinerant merchants or transient vendors of
merchandise not having been requested or invited to do so by the owner or
occupant of said private residences for the purposes of soliciting orders for
the sale of goods, wares and merchandise and/or disposing of and/or peddling or
hawking the same is declared to be a nuisance and punishable as such.
(Prior Code, § 4-201) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 111.02 EXCEPTIONS.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall not apply to the sale, or soliciting
orders for the sale of milk, diary products, vegetables, poultry, eggs and
other farm and garden produce so far as the sale of the commodities named
herein is now authorized by law.
(Prior Code, § 4-202)
SOLICITORS AND CANVASSERS
§ 111.15 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any solicitor or canvasser to engage in such
business within the corporate limits of the municipality, without first
obtaining a license therefore in compliance with the provisions of this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 4-301) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 111.16 DEFINITIONS.
   A CANVASSER or SOLICITOR is defined as any individual, whether a resident of
the municipality or not, traveling either by foot or vehicle from place to
place, from house to house or from street to street, taking or attempting to
take orders for the sale of goods, wares and merchandise, personal property of
any nature whatsoever for future delivery, or for services to be furnished or
performed in the future, whether or not such individual has, carries or exposes
for sale a sample of the subject to such sale or whether he is collecting
advance payments on such sales or not; provided that, such definition shall
include any person who, for himself or herself, or for another person or firm,
hires, leases, uses or occupies any building, structure, tent, railroad boxcar,
boar, hotel room, lodging house, apartment, shop or any other place within the
municipality for the sole purpose of exhibiting samples and taking orders for
future delivery.
(Prior Code, § 4-302)
§ 111.17 APPLICATION.
   (A)   Applicants for a license under this subchapter must file with the
Clerk/Treasurer a sworn statement or application in writing on a form to be
furnished by the Clerk/Treasurer, which shall give the following information:
      (1)   Name and description of the applicant;
      (2)   Permanent home address and full local address of the applicant;
      (3)   A brief description of the nature of the business and the goods to
be sold;
      (4)   If employed, the name and address of the employer, together with
credentials establishing the exact relationship;
      (5)   The length of time for which the right to do business is desired;
      (6)   The place where the goods or property proposed to be sold, or
orders taken for the sale thereof, are manufactured or produced, where such
goods or products are located at the time said application is filed, and the
proposed method of delivery;
      (7)   A photograph of the applicant, taken within 60 days immediately
prior to the date of filing of the application, which picture shall be two
inches by two inches, showing the head and shoulders of the applicant in a
clear and distinguishing manner;
      (8)   The fingerprints of the applicant and the names of at least two
reliable property owners of the municipality who will certify as to the
applicant’s good character and business respectability or, in lieu of the names
of references such other available evidence as to the good character and
business respectability of the applicant as will enable an investigator to
properly evaluate such character and business respectability;
      (9)   A statement as to whether or not the applicant has been convicted
of any crime or violation of any laws, the nature of the offense and the
punishment or penalty assessed therefor; and
      (10)   A statement by a reputable physician of the municipality dated not
more than ten days prior to submission of the application, certifying the
applicant to be free of contagious, infections or communicable disease.
   (B)   At the time of filing, the application fee shall be paid to the Clerk/
Treasurer to cover the cost of investigation of the facts therein stated.
(Prior Code, § 4-303)
§ 111.18 INVESTIGATION AND ISSUANCE.
   (A)   Upon receipt of such application, the original shall be referred to
the Chief of Police who shall cause such investigation of the applicant’s
business and moral character to be made as he or she deems necessary for the
protection of the public good.
   (B)   If, as a result of such investigation, applicant’s character or
business respectability is found to be unsatisfactory, the Chief of Police
shall endorse on such application his or her disapproval and his or her reasons
for the same, and return the said application to the Clerk/Treasurer, who shall
notify the applicant that his or her application is disapproved and that no
license will be issued.
   (C)   If, as a result of such investigation, the character and business
respectability of the applicant are found to be satisfactory, the Chief of
Police shall endorse on the application his or her approval, execute a license
addressed to the applicant for the carrying on of the business applied for and
return said license, along with the application to the Clerk/Treasurer, who
shall upon payment of the prescribed license fee deliver to the applicant his
or her license. Such license shall contain the signature and seal of the
issuing officer and shall show the name, address and photograph of said
licenses, the class of license issued and the kind of goods to be sold there
under, the amount of fee paid, the date of issuance and the length of time the
same shall be operative, as well as the license number and other identifying
description of any vehicle used in such soliciting or canvassing. The Clerk/
Treasurer shall keep a permanent record of all licenses issued.
(Prior Code, § 4-304)
§ 111.19 FEES.
   (A)   The license fee shall be charged by the Clerk/Treasurer for such
license.
   (B)   None of the licenses fees provided for by this subchapter shall be
applied as to occasion an undue burden upon interstate commerce. In any case
where a license fee is believed to place an undue burden upon such of the fee
so that it shall not be discriminatory, unreasonable or unfair as to such
commerce. Such application may be made before, at or within six months after
affidavit and supporting testimony, show his or her method of business and the
gross volume or estimated gross volume of business and such other information
as the governing body may deem necessary in order to determine the extent, if
any, of such undue burden on such commerce. The governing body shall then
conduct an investigation, comparing applicant’s business with other businesses
of like nature and shall make findings of fact from which it shall determine
whether the fee fixed by this subchapter is unfair, unreasonable or
discriminatory as to the applicant’s business and shall fix a license fee for
the applicant an amount that is fair, reasonable and non-discriminatory or, if
the fee has already been paid, shall order a refund of the amount over and
above the fee so fixed. If fixing the fee to be charged, the governing body
shall have the power to base the fee upon a percentage of gross sales, or any
other method which will assure that the fee assessed shall be uniform with that
assessed on businesses of like nature, so long as the amount assessed does not
exceed the fees as prescribed in this subchapter. Should the governing body
determine the gross sales measure of the fee to be fair basis, he or she may
require the applicant to submit, either at the time of termination of the
applicant’s business or at the end of each three-month period, a sworn
statement of the gross sales and pay the amount of fee therefor; provided that,
no additional fee during any one calendar year shall be required after the
licenses shall have paid an amount equal to the required license.
(Prior Code, § 4-305)
§ 111.20 BONDS.
   Every applicant shall file with the Clerk/Treasurer, a surety bond, running
to the municipality with surety acceptable to and approved by the governing
body, conditioned that the said applicant shall comply fully with all the
provisions of this subchapter. Action on such bond may be brought in the name
of the municipality to the use or benefit of the aggrieved person.
(Prior Code, § 4-306)
§ 111.21 BADGES.
   (A)   The Clerk/Treasurer shall issue to each licensee at the time of
delivery of his or her license a badge, which shall contain the words “Licensed
Solicitor”.
   (B)   The period for which the license is issued and the number of the
license, in letters and figures easily discernible from a distance of ten feet.
   (C)   Such badge shall, during the time such license is engaged in
soliciting, be worn constantly by the licensee on the front of his or her outer
garment in such a way as to be conspicuous.
(Prior Code, § 4-307)
§ 111.22 LICENSE EXHIBITION.
   Solicitors and canvassers are required to exhibit their licenses as the
request of any citizen.
(Prior Code, § 4-308)
§ 111.23 DUTY OF POLICE TO ENFORCE.
   It shall be the duty of any police officer to require any person seen
soliciting or canvassing, and who is not known by such officer to be duly
licensed to produce his or her solicitor’s or canvasser’s license and to
enforce the provisions of the subchapter against any person found to be
violating the same.
(Prior Code, § 4-309)
§ 111.24 RECORDS.
   The Chief of Police shall report to the Clerk/Treasurer all convictions for
violation of this subchapter and the Clerk/Treasurer shall maintain a record
for each license issued and record the reports therein.
(Prior Code, § 4-310)
§ 111.25 LICENSE REVOCATION.
   (A)   Permits and licenses issued under the provisions of this subchapter
may be revoked by the Clerk/Treasurer after notice and hearing for any of the
following causes:
      (1)   Fraud, misrepresentation or false statement contained in the
application of license;
      (2)   Fraud, misrepresentation or false statement made in the course of
carrying on his or her business as solicitor or as canvasser;
      (3)   Any violation of this subchapter;
      (4)   Conviction of any crime or act involving moral turpitude; or
      (5)   Conducting the business of soliciting or of canvassing in an
unlawful manner or in such a manner at to constitute a breach of the peace or
to constitute a menace to the health, safety or general welfare of the public.
   (B)   Notice of the hearing for revocation of a license shall be given in
writing, setting forth specifically the grounds of complaint and the time and
place of hearing. Such notice shall be mailed, postage prepaid, to the licensee
at his last known address at least days prior to the date set for the hearing.
(Prior Code, § 4-311)
§ 111.26 APPEAL.
   Any person aggrieved by the action of the Chief of Police or the Clerk/
Treasurer in the denial of a permit or license as provided herein, or the
action of the governing body, within 14 days after notice of the action
complained of has been mailed to such person’s last known address, a written
statement setting forth fully the grounds for the appeal. The governing body
shall set a time and place for a hearing on such appeal and notice of such
hearing shall be given to the appellant in the same manner as for the notice of
hearing on revocation. The decision and order of the governing body on such
appeal shall be final and conclusive.
(Prior Code, § 4-312)
§ 111.27 LICENSE EXPIRATION.
   All licenses issued under the provisions of this subchapter shall expire on
the date specified in the said license.
(Prior Code, § 4-313)

BEER REGULATIONS
§ 112.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   BEER. Any beverage obtained by the alcoholic fermentation of an infusion of
barley, malt and/or other ingredients in drinkable water of not more that 4% of
alcohol by weight.
   RETAILER. Any person engaged in the sale or distribution of beer to the
consumer.
(Prior Code, § 5-101)
§ 112.02 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to dispose of beer without first
obtaining a proper license.
(Prior Code, § 5-102) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.03 LICENSE APPLICATION.
   Application for a retail beer license shall be made under oath to the Clerk/
Treasurer and the application shall show that the applicant possesses all the
qualifications required by this code of ordinances. Each application shall be
forwarded, after proper and adequate investigation by the Chief of Police, to
the governing body for approval or disapproval.
(Prior Code, § 5-103)
§ 112.04 LICENSE QUALIFICATIONS.
   (A)   No retail license shall be issued to any applicant who:
      (1)   Is not the bona fide owner of such business, or is not a citizen of
the United States, or has not been bona fide resident of the state for a period
of one year prior to the date of application; provided that, if the applicant
is a partnership all partners shall be such citizens, and the manager of such
business place shall be such citizen, and shall have been such resident; and/or
      (2)   Has, or any partner or actual manager or officer of which has, been
convicted of any felony within five years or has paid any fine or completed any
sentence of confinement therefore within five years.
   (B)   A retailer licensee must continue through the license period to have
all of the foregoing qualifications and none of the foregoing
disqualifications, and for failure therein, upon proof thereof to an issuer of
a license, such issuer shall revoke the license issued, and in writing sent by
United States registered mail notice each of the other issuers of a retailer’s
license to such license (licenses), stating sufficient facts for identification
of the license and the grounds and date of revocation.
(Prior Code, § 5-104)
§ 112.05 HOURS OF SALE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to sell beer between the hours of 2:00
a.m. and 10:00 a.m.
(Prior Code, § 5-105) (Ord. 2016-4, passed 1-12-2016) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.06 FEES.
   (A)   The fees for the sale of beer shall be as follows:
      (1)   Bottled and/or draught: $85;
      (2)   Bottled or canned beer not to be consumed on the premises: $47.50;
      (3)   Retail liquor: $235; and
      (4)   Retail wine: $60.
   (B)   Each license issued shall expire on December 31 of the year following
the date of issuance.
   (C)   Such license shall be transferable to qualified persons upon the
payment of a fee of $5.
(Prior Code, § 5-106) (Res. R2016-3, passed 1-12-2016)
§ 112.07 MINORS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to offer beer to any person under 21
years of age and it shall be unlawful for any person under the age of 21 years
to frequent, loiter in or about or patronize any beer dispensary, and it shall
likewise be unlawful for any owner of such beer dispensary of his or her
employees to permit any such person under 19 years of age to be in or to be
employed in such dispensary.
(Prior Code, § 5-107) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.08 LICENSE REVOCATION.
   The governing body of the municipality shall retain the right at all times
to revoke and cancel any licenses for just cause. When and license is revoked,
the licensee shall have the privilege of appearing before the governing body to
appeal such revocation. Any conduct or act on the part of the licensee which
may be sufficient cause for revocation of the license must be brought to the
attention of the governing body. The suspension or revocation of the license
granted by the state or county shall automatically revoke the license granted
hereunder.
(Prior Code, § 5-108)
LIQUOR BY THE DRINK
§ 112.20 POLICY DECLARATION.
   It is hereby declared as the policy of the municipality under its police
power, authorizing and regulating the sale of liquor by the drink and of the
licensing of dealers licensed by the state to sell liquor by the drink and as
provided under the provisions of Idaho Code Chapter 9, as amended, the
governing body be empowered and qualified under this subchapter to sell liquor
by the drink, and to provide restrictions, regulations and provisions as
authorized by law as aforesaid.
(Prior Code, § 5-201)
§ 112.21 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   INTERDICTED PERSON. A person to whom the sale of liquor is prohibited under
the laws of the state and this subchapter.
   LICENSE. A license issued by the municipality to a qualified person under
which, it shall be lawful for the licensee to sell and dispense liquor by the
drink at retail as provided by this subchapter and as provided by law.
   LICENSEE. The person to whom a license is issued under the provisions of
this subchapter.
   LIQUOR. All kinds of liquor sold by and in a state liquor store.
   PERSON.
      (1)   The person to whom a license is issued under the provisions of this
subchapter.
      (2)   Every individual, partnership, corporations, organization or
association holding a state retail liquor license, whether conducting the
business singularly or collectively.
(Prior Code, § 5-202)
§ 112.22 WHO MAY APPLY FOR LICENSE.
   The Clerk/Treasurer, upon the approval of the governing body, is hereby
authorized and directed to issue licenses to qualified applicants to whom
licenses to sell retail liquor by the drink shall have been issued by the
Commissioner of Law Enforcement of the state.
(Prior Code, § 5-203)
§ 112.23 LICENSE FEES.
   Each licensee licensed under the licenses fee to the Clerk/Treasurer in the
sum of $235. The fees shall be for the entire year and shall not be prorated,
but shall be paid in full at the beginning of each year.
(Prior Code, § 5-204) (Res. R2016-3, passed 1-12-2016)
§ 112.24 LICENSE APPLICATION.
   Upon application for a copy of his or her state application to contain the
information required under Idaho Code Chapter 9, as amended, and licensee shall
also present a copy of the state license. If any false statements shall be
contained in the state application for license, the applications for municipal
license shall be denied and no licensee shall be entitled to have a license
unless he or she has complied with the state law in connection with the
furnishing of a bond or bonds to the Commissioner of Law Enforcement, and
unless he or she has all the qualifications required by state law.
(Prior Code, § 5-205)
§ 112.25 LOCATION RESTRICTIONS.
   No license shall be issued for any premises in any neighborhood which is
predominantly residential or within 300 feet of any public school, church or
any place of worship, measured in a straight line to the nearest entrance to
the license premises, except with the approval of the governing body; provided
that, this limitation shall no apply to any duly licensed premises that, at the
time of licensing, did not come within the restricted area, but subsequent to
licensing same came therein.
(Prior Code, § 5-206)
§ 112.26 TIME OF SALE.
   No liquor shall be sold, offered for sale or given upon any licensed
premises during the following hours:
   (A)   Memorial Day, Thanksgiving and Christmas: from 2:00 a.m. to 10:00 a.m.
the following day;
   (B)   On any other day: between 2:00 a.m. and 10:00 a.m.; and
   (C)   On any day of general or primary election: until after the time when
the polls are closed.
(Prior Code, § 5-207) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.27 GAMBLING PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any licensee to permit, conduct, play, carry on,
open or cause to be opened any gambling in or upon the licensed premises or in
or upon any premises directly connected by a door, hallway or other means of
access from the licensed premises.
(Prior Code, § 5-208) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.28 RESTRICTION OF SALES BY LICENSEE.
   No license or his, her or its employed agents, servants or bartenders shall
sell, deliver or give away, or cause or permit to be sold, delivered or give
away, any liquor to:
   (A)   Any person under the age of 21 years;
   (B)   Any person actually, apparently or obviously intoxicated; and/or
   (C)   A habitual drunkard.
(Prior Code, § 5-209) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.29 INTOXICATED PERSONS.
   No intoxicated person or persons shall be permitted to remain in, loiter or
loaf in the place of business of any licensee an the licensee and his or her
agents, servants or bartenders shall give any and all necessary required
assistance to any municipal police officer or other police officer of the
county or state in evicting and removing said person or persons from the
premises.
(Prior Code, § 5-210) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.30 OFFICERS MAY EXAMINE PREMISES.
   Any police officer, sheriff or constable shall have the right at any time to
make an examination of the premises of an licensee for the purpose of
inspecting the premises, or making that arrest of any person violating any law
of the State of the United States, or any of the regulations contained in this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 5-211)
§ 112.31 LICENSES; SUSPENSION, REVOCATION AND REVIEW.
   The license of any licensee is subject to be suspended or revoked in the
judgment of the governing body for the violation of any of the provisions of
Idaho Code Chapter 9, as amended, or of any rule or regulation contained in
this subchapter and, if upon examination and determination of the facts, just
cause for revocation or suspension of license has been determined by the
governing body, an order may be made suspending the same for a period of at
least six months, and the governing body may refuse to grant a renewal of the
said license.
(Prior Code, § 5-212)
§ 112.32 CHIEF OF POLICE; DUTIES.
   It is hereby made the duty of the Chief of Police of the municipality,
knowing of any violation of this subchapter, to make complaint before the
proper officer and to assist in the prosecution and conviction of offenders.
Any officer knowingly refusing to inform against or prosecute any offender
under the provisions of this subchapter shall be subject to removal from office
by the governing body.
(Prior Code, § 5-213)
WINE REGULATIONS
§ 112.45 POLICY DECLARATION.
   It is hereby declared the policy of the municipality under its policy power,
authorizing the regulating the retail sale of wine containing not more than 14%
alcohol by volume, the licensing of dealers for the sale at retail as provided
under the provisions of Idaho Code Chapter 13, authorizing the governing body
licenses to qualified persons under this subchapter to sell wine at retail, and
to provide restrictions, regulations and provisions as authorized by law
aforesaid.
(Prior Code, § 5-301)
§ 112.46 LICENSE FEES.
   Each license under the provisions of this subchapter shall pay an annual
license fee to the Clerk/Treasurer in the sum of $60 per year; provided,
however, that, holders of a valid “Retail Liquor By the Drink License” shall
pay an annual fee to the Clerk/Treasurer of the sum of $20. The fee shall be in
full at the beginning of each year and shall expire on December 31 each year.
(Prior Code, § 5-302) (Res. R2016-3, passed 1-12-2016)
§ 112.47 LICENSE APPLICATION.
   Upon application for license, the licensee shall present for inspection a
copy of his or her state application to contain the information required under
Idaho Code Chapter 13, as amended, and licensee shall also present a copy of
the state license. If any false statements shall be contained in the state
application for license, the application for municipal license unless he or she
has complied with the state law in connection with the furnishing of a bond or
bonds to the Commissioner of Law Enforcement, and unless he or she has all the
qualifications required by the state law.
(Prior Code, § 5-303)
§ 112.48 HOURS OF SALE; PERSONS TO WHOM SALES MADE.
   The hours when wine may be sold upon licensed premises and the persons to
whom sales may be made shall be as provided by Idaho Code Chapter 13, as the
same may be amended from time to time.
(Prior Code, § 5-304)
§ 112.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Violations of any of the provisions of §§
112.20 through
112.32 of this chapter by any licensee, agent, employee, servant or any other
person of the licensee and any person violating any of the provisions of §§
112.20 through
112.32 this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction
thereof, shall be fined as set forth in §
10.99 and may be imprisoned in the municipal jail for a period of not more than
30 days, or both such fine and imprisonment.
(Prior Code, § 5-214)
   (C)   Violations of any of the provisions of §§
112.45 through
112.48 of this chapter by any licensee, agent, employee, servant of any of the
provisions of §§
112.45 through
112.48 this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction
thereof, shall be fined as set forth in §
10.99 and may be imprisoned in the county jail for a period of not less than
one day, nor more than 30 days, or both such fine and imprisonment.
(Prior Code, § 5-305)

OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC ADMINISTRATION
§ 130.01 AID IN ESCAPE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to aid or assist any person to escape
from lawful confinement, or who shall assist any person to escape from the
custody of any peace officer.
(Prior Code, § 6-101) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.02 AID TO AN OFFENSE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to in any way or manner, said, abet,
counsel, advise or encourage any other person in the commission of any of the
acts mentioned herein, or in any manner encourage the commission of such
offense hereby defined.
(Prior Code, § 6-102) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.03 ESCAPES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person convicted of any offense or in lawful
custody to escape from custody.
(Prior Code, § 6-114) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.04 FALSE PRETENSES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to obtain any food, drink, goods, wares
or merchandise under false pretenses or who shall enter any public place and
call for refreshments, or food or other articles and receive the same and
refuse to pay for same, or depart without paying for same or satisfying the
person from whom he or she received the food, refreshments, goods, wares and
merchandise.
(Prior Code, § 6-115) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.05 FALSE REPRESENTATION.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to falsely represent himself or herself
to be an officer of the municipality or who shall attempt to impersonate any
such officer or who shall without authority perform any official act therein on
behalf of an officer.
(Prior Code, § 6-116) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.06 STATE LAW OFFENSES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to commit any act or fail to perform any
requirement which is prohibited or required by state law, insofar as such laws
are applicable to municipal government herein or depending upon the even of any
such scheme, lottery or enterprise.
(Prior Code, § 6-121) Penalty, see §
10.99

   Lottery, see §

§ 130.07 GIVING ASSISTANCE TO POLICE OFFICERS.
   It shall be unlawful for any male citizen over the age of 18 years to refuse
or neglect to render assistance to any police officer when called upon for such
assistance or aid in the suppression of riot or other unlawful assemblage or in
the arrest of any person who has committed an offense.
(Prior Code, § 6-122) Penalty, see §
10.99

   It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere willfully with, resist,
delay, obstruct, molest or threaten to molest any officer in the municipality
in the exercised of his or her official duties.

OFFENSES AGAINST PERSONS AND PROPERTY
§ 130.20 ASSAULT OR BATTERY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to commit assault or battery.
(Prior Code, § 6-103) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.21 LOTTERY; ASSISTING; SCHEMES.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to aid or assist either by
printing, writing, advertising, publishing or otherwise, in setting up,
managing or drawing any lottery, or scheme, or in selling, or disposing of any
ticket, chance or share therein, or for any person to use or permit to be used
any building or premises for any said purposes.
(Prior Code, § 6-104)
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in any lottery of scheme
for the disposal or distribution of property by chance among persons who have
paid or promised to pay any valuable consideration for the chance of obtaining
such property or portion of it, or for any share of interest is such property
upon any agreement, understanding or expectation that it is to be distributed
or disposed of by lot or chance whether such scheme be called lottery, raffle
or gift enterprise, or be whatever name the same be known, and no person shall
contrive, prepare, set up or establish any such scheme or lottery. It shall be
unlawful for any person to sell, give or in any manner whatsoever furnish or
transfer to or for any other person any ticket, understood to be or to
represent any ticket, chance, share or interest in any property or thing
involved, in any enterprise mentioned.
(Prior Code, § 6-126)
Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.22 BEER; PROCURING FOR OR SELLING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to procure, sell or give away any
intoxicating liquor to any person under the age of 21 years or any person under
21 years of age to purchase, attempt to purchase or otherwise procure or
consume intoxicating liquor.
(Prior Code, § 6-106) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.23 CRUELTY TO ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to torture or cruelly bear, starve or
otherwise ill-treat any animal in his or her care or charge, whether belonging
to himself or herself or any other person.
(Prior Code, § 6-107) Penalty, see §
10.99

or upon any pubic thoroughfare any material or substances injurious to person
or property.
(Prior Code, § 6-108) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.25 LUG WHEELS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for tractors with wheels injurious to pavement to be
permitted upon the public thoroughfares unless the operator of such vehicle
shall first plank the streets.
(Prior Code, § 6-128) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.26 MALICIOUS INJURY TO PROPERTY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully and maliciously injury,
deface, mutilate, remove, pull down, break or in any manner interfere with or
molest or secret or destroy any real or personal property belonging to or under
control of any person or property.
(Prior Code, § 6-129) Penalty, see §

   It shall be unlawful for any person to commit petit larceny.
(Prior Code, § 6-137) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.28 TRESPASSING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to take down any fence or to let down
any bars, or to open any gate in or on the property of another without the
consent of the owner, occupant or person in charge thereof.
(Prior Code, § 6-141) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.29 WATER FLOWING UPON STREETS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any water to flow into or upon
any public thoroughfare.
(Prior Code, § 6-144) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.30 PROPERTY NUISANCES.
   (A)   Destruction of building inimical to safety or health.
      (1)   It shall be unlawful to maintain any building or property so
dilapidated or in such condition as to menace the public health or safety and
the governing body of the municipality may cause the destruction or removal of
the same at the expense of the person creating, causing or maintaining such
building or property.
      (2)   The municipality may buy a special assessment on the land or
premises where such building or property is situated sufficient to defray the
cost of abating the nuisance thereby created.
(Prior Code, § 6-132)
   (B)   Property owner to abate. It shall be the duty of the owner of any
property whereon any nuisance exists, the manager or person in charge thereof
to remove, abate or destroy the same without delay.
(Prior Code, § 6-133)
   (C)   Sanitary Inspector to abate. Whenever any nuisance exists for the
abatement, creation or removal of which no responsible person can be found, it
shall be the duty of the properly designated municipal officer to remove, abate
or destroy the same or cause the same to be done.
(Prior Code, § 6-134)
   (D)   Who is liable. It shall be unlawful for any person to create or
maintain any nuisance, or cause the same to exist, or for any person to
knowingly permit a nuisance to be rented, maintained or to exist on premises
owned by him or her or under his or her control.
(Prior Code, § 6-135)
Penalty, see §
10.99
Cross-reference:
   Nuisances, see §§
91.15 through
91.25
§ 130.31 HAZARDOUS WASTES.
   The County Sheriff’s Department is hereby designated as the first responder
in the event of a hazardous waste incident within the city limits.
(Res. 1993-1, passed 2-1-1993)
OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC PEACE AND MORALS
§ 130.45 DISORDERLY CONDUCT.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in any illegal or improper
diversion, or to use insulting, indecent or immoral language, or to be guilty
of any indecent, insulting or immoral conduct or behavior.
(Prior Code, § 6-109) Penalty, see §
10.99

   It shall be unlawful for any person to exhibit, pass, give or deliver to
another any obscene, loud or indecent book, pamphlet, picture, card, print,
paper, writing, mold, cast or figure, or to have same in his or her
possessions.
(Prior Code, § 6-110) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.47 DISTURBING THE PEACE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully or maliciously or
intentionally or unnecessarily disturb the peace and quiet of another or of any
neighborhood or family or religious congregation or other assembly by loud or
unusual noises or indecent behavior or by offensive or unbecoming conduct, or
for any person to threaten, quarrel, fight to provoke an assault or batter, or
curse or swear or utter any obscene or vulgar or indecent language in the
presence of another.
(Prior Code, § 6-111) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.48 DRUNKENNESS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to be found drunk, intoxicated or under
the influence of intoxicating liquor upon any public thoroughfare or other
public place.
(Prior Code, § 6-112) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.49 ENCOURAGING DELINQUENCY.
   Any person who by any act or neglect encourages, aids or causes a child to
come within the purview of the Juvenile Corrections Act, being Idaho Code § 20-
501 et seq., or who after notice that a driver’s license if any child has been
suspended or revoked under the provisions of the Juvenile Corrections Act who
knowingly permits or encourages said child to operate a motor vehicle during
the period that such driver’s license is suspended shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 6-113) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.50 FORNICATION.
   It shall be unlawful for any unmarried person to have sexual intercourse
with an unmarried person of the opposite sex.
(Prior Code, § 6-117) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.51 FRAUDULENTLY AVOIDING PAYMENT OF ADMISSION FEES.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to fraudulently enter without payment of
the proper admission fees any theater, ballroom, lecture, concert or other
place where admission fees are charged; provided, however, that, nothing herein
contained shall be deemed to prohibit or restrict the free admission of police
officers, engage in the performance of police duties, to any place of public
entertainment or amusement.
(Prior Code, § 6-118) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.52 FURNISHING WEAPONS AND OTHER ARTICLES TO PRISONERS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to furnish or attempt to furnish or take
into jail or to deliver or attempt to deliver to any prisoner therein confined,
or in the custody of any officer, any weapon, tool, intoxicating liquors, drug
or other article without the consent of the officer in charge.
(Prior Code, § 6-119) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.53 GAMBLING.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to deal, play or conduct, either as
owner, employee or lessee, whether for hire or not, any game of faro, monte,
roulette, lansquenet, rouge et noir, ronde, Indian stick game or any game
played with cards, dice or any other device for money, checks, credit or other
representative of value.
(Prior Code, § 6-120) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.54 INDECENT EXPOSURE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to appear in a state of nudity or in any
indecent or lewd dress or condition in any public place or in any such place to
make any indecent exposure of his or her person or private parts thereof, or
the private parts of another, or to conduct himself or herself in a lewd or
lascivious way.
(Prior Code, § 6-123) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.55 JUNK RESTRICTED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to store or keep any old articles or
materials which may be classified as “junk”, adjacent to or in close proximity
to any school house, church, public park, public grounds, business buildings or
residence without first providing proper and tight buildings for the storage of
the same.
(Prior Code, § 6-124) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.56 LOUD SPEAKERS OR SOUND TRUCKS.
   It shall be unlawful to play, use or operate any device known as a sound
truck, loud speaker or sound amplifier, radio or phonograph, with loud speaker
or sound amplifier or any instrument of any kind or character which emits loud
and raucous noises and it attached to and upon any vehicle unless such person
in charge of such vehicle shall have first applied to and received permission
for the Chief of Police to operate any such vehicle equipped and used as in
this section described.
(Prior Code, § 6-127) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.57 MINORS IN POOL HALLS.
   It shall be unlawful for any proprietor, manager or employee of any public
pool or billiard hall or other business establishment wherein intoxicating
liquor or alcoholic beverages are sold to be consumed on the premises to permit
or allow any child or minor under the age of 21 years to frequent or loiter in
such establishment; provided, however, that, the same shall no be illegal in
places of business that are duly licensed by the state as restaurants.
(Prior Code, § 6-130) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.58 OBSCENE CONDUCT.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to urinate or stool in any place open to
public view, or to be guilty of any lewd, lascivious or obscene conduct or to
sing a lewd or obscene song, ballad or other words in any public place, or any
other place where other persons are present or to indecently exhibit any
animal.
(Prior Code, § 6-136) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.59 RIOT.
   It shall be unlawful when two or more persons assemble for the purpose of
disturbing the peace or, for the purpose of committing any unlawful act, for
any such person to fail or refuse to immediately disperse upon an order to do
so by a police officer. It shall be unlawful for any person, except public
officers and persons assisting in preserving the peace, to remain present at
the place of such riot, rout or unlawful assembly.
(Prior Code, § 6-139) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.60 CIGARETTES OR TOBACCO TO MINORS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or give away, directly or
indirectly, to any person under the age of 21 years, any cigarettes or tobacco
or any compounds of tobacco used in filling up or making up of a cigarette, or
who shall give to minors any cigarette papers.
(Prior Code, § 6-140) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.61 UNLAWFUL ASSEMBLY.
   It shall be unlawful for two or more persons to assemble together for the
purpose of disturbing the peace or for the purpose of committing an unlawful
act, and to not disburse upon the command of an officer so to do.
(Prior Code, § 6-142) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.62 VAGRANCY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person without visible means of support who has
a physical ability to work who does not seek employment or labor or who does
not work when employment is offered him or her; for any person to seek alms as
a business; for any person to roam about from place to place without any lawful
business; for any idle or dissolute person or associate of known thieves to
wander about the streets at a late and unusual hour of the night, or to lodge
in any other place than is kept for lodging purposes without the permission of
the owner of the property in possession thereof; or for any person to
habitually consort with common prostitutes, habitual drunkards or any users of
narcotics.
(Prior Code, § 6-143) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 130.63 FIREWORKS.
   (A)   Definition. For the purpose of this section, the following definition
shall apply unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
      PYROTECHNICS. Any sparkler, squib, rocket, firecracker, Roman candle,
fire balloon, signal light, railroad track torpedo, flashlight composition,
fireworks of other devices or compositions used to obtain visible or audible
pyrotechnic displays.
(Prior Code, § 6-701)
   (B)   Fireworks prohibited; exceptions. No person shall, within the
municipality, have, keep, store, use, manufacture, sell, handle or transport
any pyrotechnics; provided, however:
      (1)   Nothing in this section shall be held to apply to the possession or
use of signaling devices for current daily consumption by railroads, trucks and
others requiring them; and
      (2)   The Chief of Fire Department or the Clerk/Treasurer may, upon due
application, issue a permit to a properly qualified person forgiving a
pyrotechnic display of fireworks in the public parks or other open places.
(Prior Code, § 6-702)
Penalty, see §
10.99
CHAPTER 131: WEAPONS AND FIREARMS
Section
   
131.01   Definition
   
131.02   Concealed weapons
   
131.03   Discharging firearms
   
131.04   Exceptions; permits
§ 131.01 DEFINITION.
   Wherever the term FIREARMS is used in this chapter, the term shall mean any
instrument used in the propulsion of shot, shell or bullets or other harmful
objects by the action of gunpowder exploded within it, or by the action of
compressed air within it, or by the power of springs and including what are
commonly known as “air rifles” and “B-B guns”.
(Prior Code, § 6-501)
§ 131.02 CONCEALED WEAPONS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to carry concealed upon his or her
person any brass knuckles, revolver, pistol, dagger, stiletto or other deadly
weapon.
(Prior Code, § 6-502) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.03 DISCHARGING FIREARMS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge firearms of any kind or
description within the limits of the municipality; provided, however, that,
this shall not apply to police officers in the discharge of their duties.
(Prior Code, § 6-503) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 131.04 EXCEPTIONS; PERMITS.
   (A)   The governing body may at any time, upon application, grant permits to
shooting fixed localities and under fixed rules.
   (B)   Such permits shall be in writing attested by the Clerk/Treasurer
conforming to such requirements as the governing body shall demand, and the
permit thus issued shall be subject to revocation at any time by action of the
governing body.
(Prior Code, § 6-504)
CHAPTER 132: CURFEW
Section
   
132.01   Hours of curfew
   
132.02   Responsibility
§ 132.01 HOURS OF CURFEW.
   No child under the age of 16 years shall be or remain upon the public
thoroughfares of the municipality, unless accompanied by a parent, guardian or
other adult person having at the time the care, custody or control of such
child, after the hour of 10:00 p.m. on Sunday, Monday, Tuesday, Wednesday and
Thursday of each week and after the hour of 11:00 p.m. on Friday and Saturday
of each week during the months of November 1 to March 31 of each year or after
the hour of 11:00 p.m. of each day of the week during the months of April 1 to
October 31 of each year.
(Prior Code, § 6-601) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 132.02 RESPONSIBILITY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person having at the time the care, custody or
control of any child under the age of 16 years, to allow or permit such child
to be or remain upon the public thoroughfares of the municipality after the
hours hereinabove mentioned.
(Prior Code, § 6-602) Penalty, see §
10.99
