GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 155.001 TITLE.
   This chapter shall be known as the “Nezperce Zoning Ordinance”.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.002 ZONING DISTRICTS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following zoning district
classifications shall apply to lands situated within the city, as further
provided in this chapter:
 
Zone A  East Residential Zone
Zone B  West Residential Zone
Zone C  Commercial and Mixed-Use Zone
Airport Airport
Zone D  Industrial Zone
Zone E  Wellhead Protection Zone
 
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.003 ZONING DISTRICT BOUNDARIES AND ZONING MAP; AMENDMENTS.
   (A)   Applicability. All lands within the city are hereby zoned and shall be
subject to the zoning district classification as designated and set forth
herein. All lands situated within any such designated zoning district shall be
subject to all provisions of this chapter made applicable in the designated
zoning district in which said lands are situated under this chapter. Any
amendments to any zoning district classifications, designations or perimeter
description of any designated zoning district as initially established under
this section shall be made in compliance with state law then in effect.
   (B)   Adoption of initial zoning map. Each zoning district designated
pursuant to §
155.002 of this chapter includes those lands within said zoning district as set
forth herein. The city shall maintain a zoning map accurately depicting the
designated zoning district classification and zoning district boundaries
applicable to all lands within the city, including identifying the perimeter
boundary description of each zoning district designated pursuant to this
chapter. The City Clerk/Treasurer shall maintain the current duly approved
zoning map at the City Hall and shall make the same available for public
inspection during normal business hours.
   (C)   Amendments. Any amendments to zoning district classifications, zoning
district boundaries or the zoning map shall be made in compliance with state
law then in effect.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.004 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning. The word “structure”
shall include the word “building”, and the word “lot” shall include the word
“plot”.
   ACCESSORY BUILDING/ACCESSORY USE. Any accessory or subordinate building
situated on the same lot on which the main building is situated, the use of
which is ancillary or accessory to use of the main building. ACCESSORY USE
means any use occurring on a lot ancillary to or in conjunction with the
primary use of the lot or the main building situated thereon.
   ACREAGE. Any tract or parcel of land that has not been platted as part of
any plat.
   ALLEY. A street or way shown on the official plat of the city or its
additions and designated thereon as an alley.
   APARTMENT. A room or suite of rooms in a multiple-family structure that is
used, occupied, arranged, designated or intended to be used or occupied as a
separate dwelling unit.
   AUTOMOBILE/MOTOR VEHICLE. A motor vehicle of any kind or nature used or
designed for use to transport passengers or their belongings. The term MOTOR
VEHICLE shall mean any vehicle that is self-propelled.
   AUTOMOBILE REPAIR. General or specialized maintenance, repair, rebuilding or
reconditioning of motor vehicles of any kind or nature, including, but not
limited to, general maintenance, collision service, body, frame or fender
straightening and repair; and painting of motor vehicles.
   AUTOMOBILE SERVICE STATION. An establishment where fuels and lubricants, or
accessories for used or intended to be used in motor vehicles are sold at
retail; however, where the sale of said goods is only incidental to the
provision of services, the establishment shall be classified as a “public
garage”.
   AUTO WRECKING OR JUNK YARD.
      (1)   Any place where two or more motor vehicles not in running
condition, or parts thereof, are stored in the open and are not being restored
to operation; or
      (2)   Any land building or structure used for wrecking or storing of such
motor vehicles or parts thereof and including any farm machinery or parts
thereof, stored in the open and not being restored to operating condition, and
including the commercial salvaging and scavenging of any other goods, articles
or merchandise.
   BASEMENT. Any part or story any building partly or wholly below adjoining
ground level grade that is used, designed or intended to be used for occupancy
or storage. Where more than one-half of its height is above the average
adjoining ground level grade, a BASEMENT shall be counted as a story for
purpose of height measurement.
   BILLBOARD. Any structure or portion thereof used, designed or intended to be
for placement of signs or advertisement for outdoor display. This definition
does not include any bulletin boards used to display official court or public
office notices, or a sign advertising the sale or lease of the premises on
which the sign is located.
   BED AND BREAKFAST. An owner-occupied dwelling or a non-owner-occupied
guesthouse that is located on the same lot as the owner-occupied dwelling,
used, designed or intended to be used for lodging of temporary guests or
tenants for remuneration with or without provision of meals, with no more than
three guestrooms.
   BOARDING HOUSE. A owner-occupied dwelling, other than a bed and breakfast,
hotel or motel, used, designed or intended to be used for lodging and provision
of meals to temporary guests or tenants for remuneration, with more than three
guest rooms.
   BUILDING. Any structure having a roof supported by columns or walls, and
designed or intended for the shelter, support, enclosure or protection of
persons, animals or chattels.
   BUILDING AREA. A lot is the space remaining after adherence to the minimum
open space or setbacks required under this chapter.
   BUILDING HEIGHT.
      (1)   The vertical distance measured from the sidewalk level or its
equivalent established grade opposite the middle of the front of the building
to:
         (a)   The highest point of the roof in the case of a flat roof;
         (b)   To the deck line of a mansard roof; or
         (c)   To mean height level between eaves and ridge of a gable, hip or
gambrel roof.
      (2)   Provided that, where buildings are set back from the street line,
the HEIGHT OF THE BUILDING may be measured from the average elevation of the
finished lot grade at the front of the building.
   BUILDING LINE. The same as a FRONT YARD SETBACK LINE.
   CARPORT. A structure attached or made a part of the main structure which is
open to the weather on at least two sides, intended for the use of sheltering
one or more motor vehicles.
   CITY. The City of Nezperce, Lewis County, Idaho.
   CONDITIONAL USE. Any use of any land, building or structure prohibited in
the zoning district wherein said land, building or structure is situated under
this chapter that may be or has been authorized by the city pursuant to a duly
issued conditional use permit as provided in this chapter and as otherwise
permitted by law.
   CONTAINER HOME. A dwelling constructed with any cargo container, shipping
container or semi-trailer, or any portion thereof, incorporated into its
structure.
   COURT. An open, unoccupied space, other than a yard, on the same lot with a
building and bounded on two or more sides by such building.
   CURB GRADE. The established elevation of the curb measured at the center of
the front of a building. Where no curb has been established, the city shall
establish such curb level or its equivalent for the purpose of this chapter.
   DEVELOPMENT AGREEMENT. A written commitment of an owner or developer made to
the city concerning the use or development of the subject parcel pursuant to §§
155.005,
155.130 through
155.148,
155.200 through
155.204 and
155.215 through
155.217 of this chapter.
   DISTRICT. A designated area within the city limits for which the regulations
and provisions governing the use of land, buildings or structures are uniform
for each class of use permitted therein.
   DWELLING. A building or structure, or any portion thereof, but not an
automobile house trailer, used, designed or intended to be used for residential
occupancy, including one-family and multiple dwellings, but not including
hotels, boarding and lodging housed.
   DWELLING, SINGLE-FAMILY. Includes that definition provided in Idaho Code §
67-6531. For the purposes of this chapter, the classification SINGLE-FAMILY
DWELLING shall include any home in which eight or fewer unrelated mentally and/
or physically handicapped or elderly persons reside; and which is supervised.
   DWELLING, MULTIPLE. A building or portion thereof designed for occupancy by
three or more families living independently of each other.
      (1)   Resident staff, if employed, need not be related to each other or
to any of the mentally and/or physically handicapped or elderly persons
residing in the home.
      (2)   No more than two of such staff shall resided in the dwelling at any
one time.
   DWELLING ROW. A row of three to six attached one-family dwellings, not more
than two and one-half stories in height, nor more than two rooms deep.
   DWELLING, TWO-FAMILY. A building or portion thereof designed for occupancy
by two families living independently of each other.
   DWELLING UNIT. One or more rooms in a dwelling designed primarily for
occupancy by one family unit for residential purposes.
   ESTABLISHED GRADE. The sidewalk line grade adjoining the front lot line of
building or structure.
   FAMILY. One or more persons occupying a dwelling or dwelling unit and living
as a single household unit.
   FRONTAGE. All real property on one side of a street between two intersecting
streets or natural barriers.
   GARAGE, PRIVATE. An accessory building for the storage of not more than
three motor vehicles, of which not more than one shall be commercial vehicle of
not more than two-ton capacity.
   GARAGE, PUBLIC. A building, other than a private garage, used for the care,
repair or equipment of automobiles, or for vehicles parked or stored for
remuneration, hire or sale.
   GUEST HOUSE. A building or structure, detached or semi-detached from than
the main building on the same lot, used, designed or intended to be used as a
dwelling for temporary guests.
   HOME OCCUPATION. Any use of any dwelling for commercial purposes conducted
entirely within the dwelling and carried on by the inhabitants thereof, which
use is incidental and ancillary to the use of the dwelling for residential
purposes; and, provided that, no goods are sold or offered for sale on the
premises, except such as may be produced on the premises by the owner of the
premises or members of the owner’s family.
   HOSPITAL or SANITARIUM. A building or structure used, designed or intended
to be used for providing ill or injured persons medical, mental or surgical
care, treatment or allied services.
   HOTEL. A building, other than a bed and breakfast, boarding house or motel,
with a common entrance or entrances, used, designed or intended to be used for
the lodging of transient or long-term stay guests for remuneration with or
without provision of meals.
   INSTITUTION. A building occupied non-profit business or enterprise for
public or semi-public use.
   KENNEL. Any premises, other than a veterinary office, animal shelter,
grooming facility or pet shop, on which four or more dogs are maintained,
harbored, possessed, boarded, bred or cared for.
   LABORATORY. A place devoted to experimental study such as testing or
analyzing of substances. Manufacturing of a product or products is not
permitted within this definition.
   LOADING SPACE. An off-street space or area on the same lot ancillary to a
building or contiguous group of buildings used, designed or intended to be used
for the temporary parking of a vehicle for loading or unloading merchandise or
materials for commercial purposes, and which abuts upon a street, alley or
other lawful means of motor vehicle access.
   LOT.
      (1)   A parcel or plot of land held under fee ownership by one or more
owners, inclusive of any open spaces required by this chapter.
      (2)   Without limitation of the foregoing general definition, the term
LOT shall also be deemed to include, but is not limited to, any parcel or plot
of land:
         (a)   Platted and identified as a separate lot or parcel on any duly
recorded townsite or subdivision plat; or
         (b)   Assessed as a unique tax parcel by the County Assessor for real
property tax purposes.
   LOT, CORNER. A lot situated at the intersection of two or more streets.
   LOT DEPTH. The horizontal distance between the front and the rear lot lines.
   LOT FRONTAGE. The front of a lot shall be that boundary of a lot along a
public street and, for a corner lot, the front shall be the shorter of the lot
boundaries along a street.
   LOT, INTERIOR. A lot other than a corner lot.
   LOT, REVERSED CORNER. A corner lot, the rear of which abuts upon the side of
another lot whether across an alley or not.
   LOT WIDTH. The horizontal distance between the side lot lines.
   MANUFACTURED HOME/MOBILE HOME. A structure, constructed after 6-15-1976, in
accordance with the HUD manufactured home construction and safety standards,
and is transportable in one or more sections, which, in the traveling mode, is
eight body feet or more in width or is 40 body feet or more in length, or when
erected on site, is 320 or more square feet, and which is built on a permanent
chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling with or without a permanent
foundation when connected to the required utilities, and includes the plumbing,
heating, air conditioning and electrical systems contained therein; except
that, such term shall include any structure which meets all the requirements of
this definition, except the size requirements and with respect to which the
manufacturer voluntarily files a certification required by the Secretary of
Housing and Urban Development and complies with the standards established under
42 U.S.C. §§ 5401 et seq. MOBILE HOME means a factory-assembled structure or
structures generally constructed prior to 6-15-1976, and equipped with the
necessary service connections and made so as to be readily movable as a unit or
units on their own running gear and designed to be used as a dwelling unit or
units with or without a permanent foundation.
   MODULAR BUILDING/HOME. Any building or building component, other than a
manufactured or mobile home, that is of closed construction and is either
entirely or substantially prefabricated or assembled at a place other than the
building site. MODULAR HOME means any modular building used, designed or
intended to be used as a dwelling. Commercial coach buildings shall not be used
for dwelling purposes.
   MOTEL. A building, other than a bed and breakfast, boarding house or motel,
with a separate exterior entrance for each guest unit, used, designed or
intended to be used for the lodging of transient or long-term stay guests for
remuneration with or without provision of meals.
   MOTOR HOME. A motor vehicle which is designed, constructed and equipped as a
dwelling place, living abode or sleeping place (either permanently or
temporarily) and is equipped for use as a conveyance on streets and highways.
   NON-CONFORMING USE/LOT/STRUCTURE. A use, lot or structure, as applicable,
that was legally established prior to enactment of this chapter, but that is
not in compliance with this chapter due to enactment of this chapter,
subsequent ordinance amendment, annexation, change of zoning, eminent domain or
similar governmental action.
   NURSING HOME or REST HOME. A public or private hospital or institution,
other than a hospital used, designed or intended to be used primarily for
providing residential accommodations to the care of the aged, ill or infirm.
   PARKING AREA, PRIVATE. An open area for the parking of privately-owned motor
vehicles not open for public use.
   PARKING AREA, PUBLIC. An open area, other than street, alley or public way,
used, designed or intended to be used for the temporary parking of two or more
motor vehicles and is available for public use, whether or not compensation for
parking use is charged by the owner.
   PARKING SPACE. An area, enclosed or unenclosed, which has adequate access to
a public street or alley, sufficient in size to store one automobile.
   PLAT. Any duly recorded subdivision, village or townsite plat, including,
but not limited to, any revisions or amendments thereto.
   PORCH. A roofed entrance to a building, projecting out from the wall or
walls of the main structure and commonly open in part to the weather.
   RECREATION AREA. Areas of active play or recreation, such as parks,
playgrounds, sports fields, golf courses, school yards, picnic grounds or other
areas where turf provides a playing surface or serves other recreational
purposes.
   RECREATIONAL VEHICLE. A motor home, travel trailer, fifth-wheel trailer,
park model recreational vehicle, truck camper or folding camping trailer, with
or without motive power, designed for recreational or emergency occupancy. It
does not include pick-up hoods, shells or canopies designed, created or
modified for occupational usage. School buses or van-type vehicles which are
converted to recreational use are defined as RECREATIONAL VEHICLES.
   SIGNS, OUTDOOR ADVERTISING. Billboard of any type or material, installed any
place for outdoor advertising purposes.
   STORY. The portion of a building included between such floor and the ceiling
next above.
   STRUCTURAL ALTERATIONS. Any change which would prolong the life of the
supporting members of a building or structure, such as a bearing walls,
columns, beams or girders.
   STRUCTURE. Any thing constructed or erected, either on the ground or on
something having location on or above the ground. The term STRUCTURE includes a
building and accessory building.
   TEMPORARY GARAGE. A temporary garage is also known as a portable outdoor
building or a portable garage designed to provide shelter for various types of
vehicles or chattels.
   TERRACE, OPEN. A level and rather narrow plane or platform which, for
purposes of this chapter, is located adjacent to one or more faces of the main
structure.
   TINY HOUSE. A dwelling that is 400 square feet or less in floor area,
excluding lofts.
   TRAILER HOUSE/HOME. A vehicular unit, mounted on wheels designed to provide
temporary living quarters for recreational, camping, travel or emergency use
and of such size or weight as not to require special highway movement permits
when towed by a motorized vehicle.
   USE. The purpose for which land or a building is intended, designed,
arranged or maintained or for which it is then actually being used.
   YARD. An open space unoccupied and unobstructed from the ground upward on
the same lot with a main building, except as otherwise provided in this
chapter.
   YARD, FRONT. A yard extended across the full width of the lot and situated
between the front line of the lot and the nearest line of the principal
building.
   YARD, REAR. A yard extending across the full width of the lot and situated
between the rear line of the lot and the nearest line of the principal
building.
   YARD, SIDE. The part of the yard situated between the main building and a
side lot line, and extending from the required front yard (or from the front
lot line, if there is no required front yard) to the required rear yard.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.005 PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION; APPLICABILITY.
   (A)   “Planning and Zoning Commission” and “Commission”, as used in this
chapter, means the duly formed and appointed Planning and Zoning Commission of
the city then existing consistent with Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as
amended. In the event the city has not duly formed or appointed a separate
Planning and Zoning Commission then existing, the City Council shall be and
shall have and exercise all powers, authorities, duties and discretion of the
Planning and Zoning Commission as provided under this chapter, Idaho Code Title
67, Chapter 65, as amended, and as otherwise provided by law.
   (B)   Unless otherwise provided in this code of ordinances, the provisions
of this chapter are general provisions which shall apply to all chapters under
this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
ZONES A AND B - RESIDENTIAL
§ 155.020 APPLICABILITY.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall apply to all lands situated within
Zone A or Zone B, subject to all other applicable provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.021 PERMITTED USES.
   Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, permitted uses in Zones A and
B are:
   (A)   Accessory buildings;
   (B)   Apartment houses;
   (C)   Boarding houses and bed and breakfast;
   (D)   Manufactured home courts or parks subject to the provisions of this
chapter;
   (E)   Condition uses authorized under a duly issued conditional use permit;
   (F)   Dwellings;
   (G)   Home occupation;
   (H)   Nursing or rest homes;
   (I)   Temporary buildings, and uses for construction purposes for a period
not to exceed one year;
   (J)   Truck gardening and other horticultural uses, where no building is
involved and not operated for profit; and
   (K)   Use customarily incident to any of the above uses.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.022 BUILDING HEIGHT.
   No building or structure, nor the enlargement of any building or structure,
within Zone A or Zone B shall be hereafter erected or maintained to exceed two
and one-half stories, nor shall it exceed 35 feet in height.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.023 YARDS; LOT AREAS.
   No building or structure, nor the enlargement of any building or structure,
shall be hereafter erected or maintained in Zone A or Zone B unless the
following described yards and lot areas are provided and maintained in
connection with such building, structure or enlargement.
   (A)   Front yard. Each lot upon which a dwelling is constructed shall have a
front yard of not less than 20 feet, measuring from the back of the right-of-
way, plus the five-foot setback. Where lots comprising 40% or more of the
frontage between two intersecting streets are developed with buildings have
front yards with a variation of not more than 20 feet in depth, that average of
such front yards shall establish the minimum front yard depth for the entire
frontage. In no case shall a front yard of more than 50 feet be required.
   (B)   Side yard. On interior lots, there shall be a side yard on each side
of a main building of not less than five feet. Apartment houses, wherever
erected or established as such, shall have a side yard of not less than one-
fourth the height of the building to the eaves or top of coping.
      (1)   On corner lots, the side yard requirements shall be the same as for
interior lots; except that. there shall be maintained on a side yard of not
less than ten feet on the side adjacent to the street which intersects the
street upon which the building or structure maintains frontage.
      (2)   On a reversed corner lot, there shall be maintained a setback from
the side street of not less than 50% of the front yard required on the lots in
the rear of such corner lots, but such setback need not exceed 20 feet. No
accessory building on a reversed corner lot shall project beyond the front yard
required on the adjacent lot to the rear, nor be located nearer than five feet
to the side of an adjacent lot.
   (C)   Accessory buildings. Accessory buildings shall not encroach upon the
front yard. They may encroach upon the side yards; provided, no buildings are
closer to the lot lines than five feet; provided further that, on a corner lot,
accessory buildings shall not encroach upon the front or side yards adjacent to
the abutting streets.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.024 MANUFACTURED HOME REQUIREMENTS.
   Manufactured homes, as defined in §
155.004 of this chapter, shall be permitted within Zones A and B, subject to
all applicable provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.025 BOUNDARIES.
   (A)   Zone A: East Residential Zone. Those certain lands situated within the
following described portions of the city: commencing at the point of

Block 3); subject to the Well 1 Wellhead Protection Overlay Zone.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
ZONE C - COMMERCIAL-MIXED USE
§ 155.040 APPLICABILITY; BUSINESS DISTRICT.
   (A)   Applicability. The provisions of this subchapter shall apply to all
lands within Zone C, subject to all other applicable provisions of this
chapter.
   (B)   Business District. Within the Zone C, there shall be a corridor of
property known as the “Business District”. The BUSINESS DISTRICT is hereby
defined as being and including all lands abutting each side of Oak Street from
(north to south) 3rd Avenue to 7th Avenue and (east to west) from Maple to Pine
Street.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.041 PERMITTED USES.
   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, the following uses are permitted
in Zone C:
   (A)   Any use permitted in Zone A or Zone B, with the exception that no
livestock (including, but not limited to, horses, beef, sheep or goats), except
chickens shall be permitted in Zone C; and
   (B)   The following additional uses are permitted in Zone C:
      (1)   Agricultural implement sales and service;
      (2)   Air conditioning and heating sales and service;
      (3)   Apartments;
      (4)   Auction rooms;
      (5)   Auditoriums;
      (6)   Auto painting, upholstery repairing, reconditioning and body and
fender work when done within the confines of a structure;
      (7)   Automobile and truck sales and service shops;
      (8)   Automobile service station;
      (9)   Bakeries, when including retail sales;
      (10)   Banks, credit unions and other financial institutions;
      (11)   Barbershops and beauty shops;
      (12)   Battery and tire service stations;
      (13)   Beverage distributors, but not including bottling plants;
      (14)   Book or stationery stores;
      (15)   Bookbinding;
      (16)   Business, music, dance or commercial schools;
      (17)   Catering establishments;
      (18)   Conditional uses authorized under any duly issued conditional use
permit;
      (19)   Departments, furniture and home appliance stores;
      (20)   Drugstores;
      (21)   Dry cleaners employing facilities for not more than 1,000 pounds
of dry goods per day and using a dry cleaning solvent that has a flashpoint no
lower than 140°F and stored in a tank of no more than 500-gallon capacity;
provided that, a solvent having a flashpoint lower than 140°F may be used if
there is no more than one gallon such solvent on the premises at any one time;
      (22)   Electrical appliance and repair shops;
      (23)   Employment agencies;
      (24)   Expressing, baggage and transfer delivery stores;
      (25)   Florist shops and greenhouses when including retail stores;
      (26)   Frozen food lockers;
      (27)   Garages, public for storage of private passenger automobiles, RVs,
but not including repair service;
      (28)   Grocery, fruit or vegetable stores;
      (29)   Hardware stores;
      (30)   Hospitals, sanitariums and medical dental, therapy and counseling
offices;
      (31)   Hotels;
      (32)   Ice manufacturing;
      (33)   Laboratories;
      (34)   Launderettes and laundromats;
      (35)   Laundries employing facilities for not more than 1,000 pounds of
dry goods per day;
      (36)   Lumber and retail and wholesale yards;
      (37)   Manufacturing or processing which is clearly incidental to retail
use is permitted. Such manufacturing or processing is limited to that which
employs not more than ten persons in the manufacturing or processing;
      (38)   Meat market or poultry stores, if no slaughter or stripping is
involved;
      (39)   Motels;
      (40)   Offices;
      (41)   Painting and decorating shops;
      (42)   Parking areas;
      (43)   Pet shops or animal hospitals when conducted wholly within
enclosed buildings;
      (44)   Photographer’s or artist’s studios;
      (45)   Plumbing, electrical, heating and roofing supply and workshops;
      (46)   Printing, publishing and issuing of newspapers, periodicals, books
and other reading matter;
      (47)   Printing shops;
      (48)   Professional services, including, but not limited to, legal,
accounting, engineering, architectural, investment and financial, insurance and
real estate services;
      (49)   Radio and television sales services;
      (50)   Recreation places;
      (51)   Restaurants;
      (52)   Retail stores and services, but expressly excluding those uses
listed in Industrial D Zone;
      (53)   Schools, public and private;
      (54)   Shoe repair shops;
      (55)   Signs, outdoor advertising;
      (56)   Storage of household goods;
      (57)   Tailor and dressmaking shops;
      (58)   Taverns, billiard and pool rooms or retail sale of alcoholic
liquors, subject to the regulations of other provisions of this code of
ordinances;
      (59)   Taxi service stations;
      (60)   Telephone exchange buildings;
      (61)   Temporary buildings incidental only to construction of a permitted
use;
      (62)   Theaters, indoor (not including outdoor theaters);
      (63)   Trailer sales when conducted within buildings;
      (64)   Undertaking establishments;
      (65)   Veterinary clinics and animal hospitals;
      (66)   Wholesale establishments, excluding a building, the principal use
of which is for a storage warehouse; and
      (67)   Use customarily incidental to any one of the above uses and
accessory buildings and parking areas, when located on the same lot.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.042 ADDITIONAL CONDITIONAL USES; PROHIBITED USES.
   (A)   Additional conditional uses. In addition to any other conditional use
that may be permitted by the city in Zone C as provided in this chapter, the
City Council may authorize automobile, truck agricultural implement and trailer
sales lots in Zone C.
   (B)   Prohibited uses. Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter,
the following uses shall be prohibited in Zone C unless otherwise authorized by
the City Council as provided in this chapter:
      (1)   Livestock except chickens; and
      (2)   Manufactured/mobile home courts or parks, or recreational vehicle
courts or parks, and any individually located mobile home either single-wide or
double-wide, or any single-wide manufactured homes, unless authorized by duly
issued conditional use permit or temporary occupancy permit pursuant to this
chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.043 YARDS.
   No front or side yards shall be required; except that, when a building or
group of buildings abuts upon a residential district, a yard shall be provided
on the side of the lot abutting the residential district, such yard having a
width of not less than five feet.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.044 BUILDING HEIGHT.
   No building or structure, nor the enlargement of any building or structure,
shall exceed 40 feet in height.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.045 BOUNDARIES.
   Those certain lands situated within the following described portions of the
city: commencing at the northwest corner of city limits at State Highway 62;
thence running in a easterly direction along the northern boundary of city
limits to its point of intersection between Tax #D-107 and Tax #D-98; thence
running in a southeasterly direction between the boundary of parcel tax #D-107
and parcel tax #D-98 to its point of intersection with the northern boundary of
Nezperce Lots 1 through 5, Block 5; thence running in a easterly direction
along the northern boundary of Nezperce Lots 1 through 5, Block 5, to its point
of intersection with the centerline of Maple Street; thence running in a
southerly direction along the centerline of Maple Street to its point of
intersection with the centerline of 3rd Avenue; thence running in an easterly
direction along the centerline of 3rd Avenue to its point of intersection with
the centerline of the first alley located east of Maple Street; thence running
in a southerly direction along the centerline of the first alley located east
of Maple Street to its point of intersection with the centerline of 4th Avenue;
thence running in a westerly direction along the centerline of 4th Avenue to
its point of intersection with the centerline of Maple Street; thence running
in a southerly direction along the centerline of Maple Street to its point of
intersection with the centerline of 7th Avenue; thence running in a westerly
direction along the centerline of 7th Avenue to its point of intersection with
the centerline of Pine Street; thence running in a northerly direction along
the centerline of Pine Street to its point of intersection with the centerline
of 5th Avenue; thence running in a westerly direction along the centerline of
5th Avenue to its point of intersection with the centerline of Walnut Street;
thence running in a northerly direction along the centerline of Walnut Street
to its point of intersection with the centerline of 4th Avenue; thence running
in a easterly direction along the centerline of 4th Avenue to its point of
intersection with the centerline of Pine Street; thence running in a northerly
direction along the centerline of Pine Street to its point of intersection with
city limits; thence running in a northwesterly direction along city limits near
State Highway 62; and commencing at the point of intersection of the centerline
of the unnamed street located between Maple Street and Cedar Street and city
limits; thence running in an easterly direction along the northern boundary of
city limits near 1st Avenue to its point of intersection with the centerline of
Cedar Street; thence running in a southerly direction along the centerline of
Cedar Street to its point of intersection with the centerline of 2nd Avenue;
thence running in a westerly direction along the centerline of 2nd Avenue to
its point of intersection with the centerline of the first alley located west
of Cedar Street; thence running in a southerly direction along the centerline
of the first alley located west of Cedar Street to its point of intersection
with the centerline of 4th Avenue; thence running in a westerly direction along
the centerline of 4th Avenue to its point of intersection with the centerline
of the unnamed street located between Maple Street and Cedar Street; thence
running in a northerly direction along the centerline of the unnamed street
located between Maple Street and Cedar Street to its point of intersection with
the northern boundary of city limits near 1st Avenue; and commencing at the
point of intersection at the centerline of 2nd Avenue and the centerline of
Cedar Street; thence running in an easterly direction along the centerline of
2nd Avenue to its point of intersection with the centerline of the alley
located between Cedar Street and Beech Street; thence running in a southerly
direction along the centerline of the alley located between Cedar Street and
Beech Street to its point of intersection with the southern boundary of Lots 11
and 12, Block 13; thence running in a westerly direction along the southern
boundary of Lots 11 and 12, Block 13, to its point of intersection with the
centerline of Cedar Street; thence running in a northerly direction along the
centerline of Cedar Street to its point of intersection with the centerline of
2nd Avenue.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
ZONE D - INDUSTRIAL
§ 155.060 APPLICABILITY.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall apply to all lands situated within
Zone D, subject to all other applicable provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.061 PERMITTED USES.
   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, the following uses are permitted
in Zone D:
   (A)   Any use permitted in Zone A, Zone B or Zone C; and
   (B)   The following additional uses are permitted in Zone D:
      (1)   Agricultural uses, including, but not limited to, farming;
      (2)   Artificial limb manufacturing;
      (3)   Blacksmith shops;
      (4)   Beverage bottling and distributing stations;
      (5)   Box manufacturing;
      (6)   Building equipment, sand and gravel yards and yards for
constructing equipment, maintenance or operating equipment of public agencies
or public utilities, or materials or equipment of similar nature;
      (7)   Carpet and rug cleaners;
      (8)   Carting, express hauling or storage yards;
      (9)   Conditional uses authorized under any duly-issued conditional use
permit;
      (10)   Cement block manufacture, when done wholly within a building;
      (11)   Electrical appliance and electronic instrument and assembly;
      (12)   Furniture manufacturing and upholstering;
      (13)   Grain elevators and seed processing plants;
      (14)   Greenhouses, wholesale growers only;
      (15)   Heating and sheet meal fabrications when not operated as part of a
retail plumbing and heating shop;
      (16)   Laboratories for scientific experiments;
      (17)   Machine shops and metal product manufacturing;
      (18)   Plastic products manufacturing, but not including the processing
of the raw materials;
      (19)   Processing and sale of feed grains;
      (20)   Public utility electric substations and distribution centers, gas
regulation centers and underground gas holder stations;
      (21)   Sawmills and planer mills;
      (22)   Sport shooting ranges as may otherwise be permitted by law;
      (23)   Storage and warehouses;
      (24)   Storage of flammable liquids, fats or oil in tanks, each of 50,000
gallons or less capacity, but only after the location and protective measures
have been approved by local governing officials;
      (25)   Tool and dye shops;
      (26)   Truck or bus storage yards, including truck terminals;
      (27)   The manufacture, compounding, assembling or treatment of articles
of merchandise from the following list of previously prepared materials: bone;
tanned leather; paper; plastics; cellophane; canvas; cloth; cork; feathers;
felt; fiber; furs; glass; hair; horn; precious or semi-precious metals or
stones; shell; textiles; wood;
      (28)   The manufacture of pottery and figurines or any other similar
ceramic products using only previously pulverized clay and kilns fired only by
electricity or gas; and
      (29)   Any other manufacturing establishment that can be operated without
creating objectionable noise, odor, dust, smoke, gas, fumes or vapor and that
has a use compatible with the use and occupancy of adjoining properties.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.062 SETBACK REQUIREMENTS.
   No yard area shall be required, except when a lot abuts any lot situated
within Zone A or Zone B, in which case there shall be a rear yard not less than
20 feet and no materials or equipment shall be stored within the 20 feet to any
such residential lot or lots.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.063 BUILDING HEIGHT.
   There shall be no height restriction for structures within Zone D.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.064 MANUFACTURED AND MOBILE HOMES.
   (A)   Manufactured homes, multi-sectional mobile homes not more than 20
years old or multi-sectional mobile home that has been rehabilitated in
accordance with the provisions of Idaho Code Title 44, Chapter 22, may be
permitted in Zone D.
   (B)   Any single-wide mobile home in place and installed as of the date of
enactment of this chapter shall be permitted to continue in place within Zone
D, but may not be moved to any other place in the city unless they are:
      (1)   Rehabilitated as required by law; and
      (2)   Moved to and sited in a manufactured/mobile home court or park, or
recreational vehicle court or park as may be otherwise permitted under this
chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.065 BOUNDARIES.
   Those certain lands situated within the following described portions of the
city: commencing at the point of intersection with the southern boundary of
city limits along State Highway 162 and the centerline of Walnut Street; thence
running in a easterly direction along the centerline of State Highway 162 to
its point of intersection with the centerline of Oak Street; thence running in
a northerly direction along the centerline of Oak Street to its point of
intersection with the northern boundary of Nezperce S 15-foot Lot 7, Block 47;
thence running in a easterly direction along the northern boundary of Nezperce
S 15-foot Lot 7, Block 47, to its point of intersection with the centerline of
the alley between Oak Street and Maple Street; thence running in a northerly
direction along the centerline of the alley between Oak Street and Maple Street
to its point of intersection with the northern boundary of Nezperce Lots 5 and
6, Block 47, Scale House; thence running in an easterly direction along the
northern boundary of Nezperce Lots 5 and 6, Block 47, Scale House and the
northern boundary of Nezperce Lots 7 and 8, Block 46, to its point of
intersection with the northern boundary of Nezperce Lots 7 and 8, Block 46, and
the centerline of the first alley located east of Maple Street; thence running
in a southerly direction along the centerline of the first alley located east
of Maple Street to its point of intersection with the southern boundary of 8th
Avenue; thence running in an easterly direction along the southern boundary of
8th Avenue to its point of intersection with the southern boundary of city
limits near the extension of the unnamed street located between Cedar Street
and Maple Street; thence running in a southwesterly direction along city limits
to the point where city limits turns due south; thence running in a southerly
direction along the eastern boundary of city limits of Mowry’s Addition to the
city situated within the city limits to its point of intersection with the
centerline of 10th Avenue; thence running in a westerly direction along the
centerline of 10th Avenue to its point of intersection with the western
boundary of city limits of Mowry’s Addition; thence running in a northerly
direction along the western boundary of city limits of Mowry’s Addition to its
point of intersection where city limits turns to the southwest along the
southern boundary of the Lux Addition to the city situated within the city
limits; thence running in a southwesterly direction along city limits of the
Lux Addition to its point of intersection with the western boundary of city
limits of the Lux Addition; thence running in a northerly direction along the
western boundary of city limits of the Lux Addition and the centerline of
Walnut Street to the point of intersection with the southern boundary of city
limits along State Highway 162; and commencing at the northwest corner of city
limits at the northwest corner of Johnson’s Addition; thence running in an
easterly direction along the northern boundary of city limits of Johnson’s
Addition to its point of intersection with the eastern boundary of Johnson’s
Addition parcel Tax #D-103 (N three-fourths of Lot 11 and all of Lot 12 and
vacated alley adjacent to Lots 1, 2 and 3, Block 3); thence running in a
southerly direction along the eastern boundaries of Johnson’s Addition parcel
Tax #D-103 (N three-fourths of Lot 11 and all of Lot 12 and vacated alley
adjacent to Lots 1, 2 and 3, Block 3) and Johnson’s Addition parcel Tax #D-104
(Lots 7 through 10 and S Lot 11, Block 3) to the southeast corner of Johnson’s
Addition parcel Tax #D-104 (Lots 7 through 10 and S one-fourth Lot 11, Block
3); thence running in a westerly direction along the southern boundary of
Johnson’s Addition parcel Tax #D-104 (Lots 7 through 10 and S one-fourth Lot
11, Block 3) to its point of intersection with the western boundary of city
limits of Johnson’s Addition; thence running in a northerly direction along the
western boundary of city limits of Johnson’s Addition to the northwest corner
of city limits at the northwest corner of Johnson’s Addition.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
ZONE E - WELLHEAD PROTECTION PLAN
§ 155.080 TITLE.
   This subchapter shall be known as the “Wellhead Protection Plan”.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.081 PURPOSE.
   (A)   It is the purpose of this subchapter to promote the public health,
safety and general welfare, and to minimize public and private losses due to
contamination of the public water supply, and to formalize ground water
protection/pollution abatement and control procedures.
   (B)   Specific goals are to:
      (1)   Protect human life and health;
      (2)   Ensure that the public is provided with a sustainable safe potable
water supply;
      (3)   Minimize expenditure of public money for pollution remediation
projects;
      (4)   Minimize regulations on land use; and
      (5)   Minimize business interruptions.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.082 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   BEST MANAGEMENT PRACTICES (BMPs). Those methods, measures or practices to
prevent or reduce water pollution and include, but are not limited to,
structural and non-structural controls and operation and maintenance
procedures.
   COMMUNITY WATER SYSTEM. A public system which serves at least 15 service
connections used by year-round residents or regularly serves at least 25 year-
round residents.
   FACILITY. Any business or corporation that is built, installed or
established to serve a particular purpose.
   FEED LOT. A parcel of land whereon there is contained an operation of
feeding or raising animals in excess of 100 animal units per acre or in excess
of 500 animal units per parcel of land. One animal unit is equivalent to one
beef cow, steer, feeder or fat beef animal or one horse; seven-tenths swine;
six and seven-tenths sheep; 33 hens, capons, broiler or ducks; and ten geese or
turkeys.
   HAZARDOUS WASTE DISPOSAL FACILITY. A hazardous waste treatment, storage or
disposal facility which receives hazardous material as described in 40 C.F.R. §
260.1.
   HAZARDOUS WASTE OR MATERIAL. Any waste or material which because of its
quantity, concentration, physical, chemical or infectious characteristics may:
      (1)   Cause or significantly contribute to an increase in mortality or an
increase in serious irreversible or incapacitating reversible illness;
      (2)   Pose a substantial present or potential hazard to human health or
to the environment when improperly treated, stored, transported, disposed of or
otherwise managed; and
      (3)   Any material or substance designed as a hazardous or toxic
substance, defined by 40 C.F.R. § 260.1, or any material or substance
designated as a hazardous or toxic substance by the state, acting through the
Division of Environmental Quality or any successor agency.
   INJECTION. The subsurface emplacement of fluids.
   LIVESTOCK CONFINEMENT OPERATION. Any lot, corral, pasture or facility where
one or more apply:
      (1)   The lot size is less than one acre;
      (2)   The number of animal units exceeds the number of animals permitted
in the zone they are located;
      (3)   The animals are supplemented or fed food other than grass;
      (4)   The pasture is overgrazed; and
      (5)   Animals are confined, or stabled and fed, or maintained for a total
of 45 days or more in any 12-month period.
   NON-COMMUNITY WATER SYSTEM. A public water system that is not a community
water system.
   OVERLAY WELLHEAD PROTECTION DISTRICT. Overlay wellhead protection districts
are delineated using one of the following methods:
      (1)   Calculated fixed radius;
      (2)   Arbitrary fixed radius;
      (3)   Simplified variable shapes;
      (4)   Semi-analytical and analytical methods;
      (5)   Hydro-geologic mapping;
      (6)   Numerical modeling; and
      (7)   Follow the guidelines established in the state’s Wellhead
Protection Plan.
   PUBLIC WATER SYSTEM.
      (1)   A system that provides the public with piped water for human
consumption, if such system has at least 15 service connections or regularly
serves an average of at least 25 individuals daily at least 60 days out of the
year. Such term includes:
         (a)   Any collection, treatment, storage and distribution facilities
under control of the operator of such system, and used primarily in connection
with such system; and
         (b)   Any collection or pretreatment storage facilities not under such
control that are used primarily in connection with such system.
      (2)   A PUBLIC WATER SYSTEM is either a community water system or a non-
community water system.
   SANITARY LANDFILL. A solid waste disposal operation where the wastes are
spread on land in thin layers, compacted to the smallest practical volume and
covered with cover material once each day of operation in order to safeguard
against environmental pollution, nuisances and health hazards.
   TIME OF TRAVEL DISTRICTS (TOT). The time required for a contaminate to move
in the ground from a specific point to a well. The area over which contaminates
will typically travel during a specified period in a specified type of aquifer,
as defined by the Idaho Department of Equality.
   UNDERGROUND INJECTION WELL. Any excavation or artificial opening into the
ground which meets the following three criteria:
      (1)   It is a bored, drilled or dug hole, or is a driven mine shaft or a
driven well point;
      (2)   It is deeper than its largest straight-line surface dimension; and
      (3)   It is used for or intended to be used for injection.
   WELLHEAD. The upper terminal of a well, including adapters, ports, seals
valves and other attachments.
   WELLHEAD PROTECTION OVERLAY DISTRICT (WHP). A land used designation on the
land use map or a zoning designation on a zoning map, that modifies the basic
underlying designation in some specific manner. The WELLHEAD PROTECTION OVERLAY
DISTRICT will also appear in the “Hazardous Component” of the Comprehensive
Plan. A map will define specific area districts centering around wells
supplying drinking water to a public water system, as defined in this section.
   WELLHEAD PROTECTION OVERLAY DISTRICT Ia. A minimum fixed radius extending no
less than 50 feet radially from the wellhead supplying potable water to the
city’s public water supplies.
   WELLHEAD PROTECTION OVERLAY DISTRICT Ib. A three-year time of travel
district (TOT), as defined herein.
   WELLHEAD PROTECTION OVERLAY DISTRICT II. A six-year time of travel district
(TOT), as defined herein.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.083 WELLHEAD PROTECTION OVERLAY DISTRICT.
   There is hereby established a Wellhead Protection Overlay District
identified and described as all the area within the six-year TOT district
around public water supplies for the city where the city wells are located as
more particularly identified herein: Wellhead Protection Zone Well 1 located at
5th Avenue and Fir Street; Well 4 located at 5th Avenue and Ash Street. It is
further established that these areas be composed of three districts: Wellhead
Protection Overlay District Ia; Wellhead Protection Overlay District Ib; and
Wellhead Protection Overlay District II, as they are defined in §
155.082 of this chapter, and as they are specifically named and legally and
arithmetically described herein.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.084 PERMITTED USES.
   (A)   Zone Ia. Permitted uses within Zone Ia shall be limited to necessary
wellhead equipment, wellhead facility buildings, water storage tanks and
approved landscaping and disinfection equipment and chemicals.
   (B)   Zone Ib and Zone II. The following uses may be permitted within Zone
Ib and Zone II of the well head protection area:
      (1)   Most uses will not comply with existing ordinances, county, state
and federal regulations pertaining to the discharge of contaminates. Permitted
uses shall use best management practices (BMPs) and monitoring wells may be
required as part of permitting requirements; and
      (2)   Only the following underground injection wells will be allowed:
         (a)   Deep well injection (below 18 feet in depth):
            1.   Geothermal heat;
            2.   Heat pump return; and
            3.   Cooling water return.
         (b)   Shallow well injection only (less than 18 feet in depth):
            1.   Storm runoff;
            2.   Agricultural runoff water;
            3.   Special drainage water;
            4.   Aquifer recharge;
            5.   Aquifer remediation; and
            6.   Septic systems (general).
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.085 EXISTING FACILITIES.
   Requirements for facilities existing within the wellhead protection areas in
Zones Ia, Ib and II are as follows.
   (A)   Upon the request of the Planning and Zoning Commission, or the Public
Works Superintendent, facilities shall provide copies of all federal, state and
local facility operation approval permits and ongoing environmental and safety
procedures already in use with regard to pollution control measures.
   (B)   Facilities shall have the responsibility of devising and filing with
the city a contingency plan satisfactory to the county for the immediate
notification to the county officials in the event of an emergency.
   (C)   Existing facilities that do not conform with the new restrictions
within the overlay districts will be allowed to continue operating as normal.
The non-conforming facility may be sold and the new owners will not be required
to update the facility unless other federal, state or local regulations require
it.
   (D)   Expansion of any use any more than 20% of physical facilities or
production components, whether any single or multiple increments, will require
full review, to determine if the expansion will pose a hazard or threat to the
existing ground water quality. Approval will only be granted when the Planning
and Zoning Commission determines there is no hazard or threat to the ground
water quality.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.086 RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   Zone Ia Wellhead Protection Area. The following uses or conditions,
including, but not limited to, shall be and are hereby prohibited within Zone
Ia of the Wellhead Protection Overlay District:
      (1)   Surface use of storage of hazardous material expressly including
herbicide and pesticide applications the soils, ground water or surface water;
      (2)   Sanitary landfills;
      (3)   Hazardous waste facility;
      (4)   Underground storage tanks;
      (5)   Sanitary sewer lines;
      (6)   Underground injection wells;
      (7)   All other facilities involving the collection, handling,
manufacture, use, storage, transfer or disposal of any solid or liquid material
or waste having a potentially hazardous impact on ground water quality;
      (8)   Disposal of waste oil, oil filters, tires and all other petroleum
products;
      (9)   Septic tanks and drain fields; and
      (10)   Animal feedlots.
   (B)   Zone Ib Wellhead Protection Area. The following uses or conditions,
including, but not limited to, shall be and are hereby prohibited within Zone
Ib of the wellhead protection areas whether or not such use or condition may
otherwise be ordinarily included as part of a use permitted under this division
(B):
      (1)   Sanitary landfills;
      (2)   Animal feedlots;
      (3)   Hazardous waste facility;
      (4)   Deep underground injection wells;
      (5)   All manufacturing or industrial businesses involving the
collection, handling, manufacture, use, storage, transfer or disposal of any
hazardous solid or liquid material or waste having potential impact on ground
water;
      (6)   Existing sewer lines shall not lay within 50 feet of a wellhead or
upon installation of new sanitary systems and sewer lines shall not lay within
150 feet of a wellhead;
      (7)   Existing septic tanks or drain fields shall not lay within 100 feet
of a wellhead and new installation of septic tanks or drain fields shall not
fall within 200 feet of a wellhead public water system;
      (8)   Junk or salvage yards;
      (9)   Disposal of waste oil, oil filters, tires and all other petroleum
products; and
      (10)   Land uses activities posing a hazard or threat to existing ground
water quality as deemed by the Planning and Zoning Commission and the Board of
County Commissioners during review process of applications.
   (C)   Zone II Wellhead Protection Area. The following uses or conditions,
including, but not limited to, shall be and are prohibited within Zone II of
the wellhead protection area, whether or not such use or condition may
otherwise be ordinarily included as part of a use permitted under division (B)
above:
      (1)   Sanitary landfills;
      (2)   Hazardous waste disposal facility; and
      (3)   Land use activities posing a hazard or potential threat to existing
ground water quality as deemed by the Planning and Zoning Commission and the
Board of County Commissioners during review process of applications.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.087 NEW WELLS.
   Prior to the development of new wells for the purpose of supplying potable
water to any public community water system, the proposed well site will be
delineated in accordance with §
155.083 of this chapter, using anticipated yields to determine time of travel
zones. The delineated areas will then be inventoried for potential contaminate
sources and the proposed site evaluated as to potential adverse impact to the
well site.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.088 ADMINISTRATION GENERALLY.
   (A)   Policies and procedures. The policies and procedures for
administration of any wellhead protection zone established under this chapter,
including, without limitation, those applicable to non- conforming uses,
exceptions, enforcement and penalties, shall be the same as provided in the
existing Building Code as the same is presently enacted and from time to time
amended.
   (B)   Final approval. Final approval for any proposed use will be granted by
the city that the wellhead overlay zone was established for. If the wellhead
zones were established for a privately-owned company, then final approval will
come from either the county or city depending on where the water company is
located (i.e., city or county limits).
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.089 VIOLATIONS; APPLICABILITY.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful and a misdemeanor for any person to occupy or use
the land within the designated with the Wellhead Protection Overlay District of
Zones Ia, Ib and II, contrary to, or in violation of, any of the provisions of
this subchapter, punishable by fine, jail, or both, as provided under state
law.
   (B)   This subchapter shall apply to all lands within the city. If provided
under the City/County Area of City Impact Ordinance, this subchapter shall also
apply with the City/County Area of City Impact.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.090 BOUNDARIES.
   Those certain lands situated within the wellhead protection overlay zones
for the following city wells as provided in this subchapter, as amended,
situated within the city: Well 1 located west of Willow Street near 5th Avenue
and Well 4 located west of Ash Street near 5th Avenue.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
MUNICIPAL AIRPORT
§ 155.105 TITLE.
   The provisions in this subchapter shall be known and may be cited as the
“Nezperce Municipal Airport Zoning Ordinance”.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.106 APPLICABILITY.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall apply all lands with the Airport
Zone situated within the city, subject to all other applicable provisions of
this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
Cross-reference:
   Airport generally, see
Chapter 153
§ 155.107 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   AIRPORT. The Nezperce Municipal Airport.
   AIRPORT ADMINISTRATOR. A person nominated by the Mayor and confirmed by the
City Council to administer and assist in enforcing the regulations of this
chapter.
   AIRPORT ELEVATION. Three thousand two hundred one feet above mean sea level,
unless otherwise reported in the Idaho Airport Facilities Directory.
   APPROACH SURFACE. Applied to each end of the runway based on the type of
approach available. The APPROACH SURFACE is longitudinally centered in the
extended runway centerline and extends outward and upward from the end of the
primary surface. The inner edge of the APPROACH SURFACE is the same width as
the primary surface (200 feet). The surface expands uniformly to a width of 500
feet at a horizontal distance of 3,000 feet from each end of runway.
   APPROACH, TRANSITIONAL, HORIZONTAL AND CONICAL ZONES. These zones are set
forth in §
155.108 of this chapter.
   BOARD OF ADMINISTRATION. The Zoning Commission of the city is the City
Council.
   CONICAL SURFACE. A surface is an inclined surface at a slope of 20 to one
(20:1) extending upward and outward from the periphery of the horizontal
surface for a horizontal distance of 4,000 feet.
   HAZARD TO AIR NAVIGATION. An obstruction determined to have a substantial
adverse effect on the safe and efficient utilization of the navigable airspace.
   HEIGHT. For the purpose of determining the height limits in all zones set
forth in this subchapter and shown on the zoning map, the datum shall mean sea
level elevation unless otherwise specified.
   HORIZONTAL SURFACE. A horizontal plane 150 feet above the established
airport elevation, the perimeter of which in plan coincides with the perimeter
of the horizontal zone.
   NON-CONFORMING USE. Any preexisting structure, and object of natural growth
which is inconsistent with the provisions of this chapter or an amendment
thereto.
   OBSTRUCTION. Any structure, object of natural growth or other object,
including a mobile object, which exceeds a limiting height set forth in §
155.109 of this chapter.
   PERSON. An individual, firm, partnership, corporation, company, association,
joint stock association or governmental entity. PERSON includes a trustee, a
receiver, an assignee or a similar representative of any of them.
   PRIMARY SURFACE. A surface of longitudinally centered on a runway. When the
runway has a specially prepared hard surface, the PRIMARY SURFACE extends 200
feet beyond each end of that runway. When the runway has no specially prepared
hard surface, or planed hard surface, the PRIMARY SURFACE ends at each end of
that runway. The width of the PRIMARY SURFACE is set forth in §
155.108 of this chapter. The elevation of any point on the PRIMARY SURFACE is
the same as the elevation of the nearest point on the runway centerline.
   RUNWAY. A defined area on an airport prepared for landing and takeoff of
aircraft along its length.
   STRUCTURE. An object, including a mobile object, constructed or installed by
humans, including, but with limitation, buildings, towers, cranes, smokestacks,
earth formations and overhead transmission lines.
   TRANSITIONAL SURFACES. These extend outward at 90-degree angles to the
runway centerline and the runway centerline extended at a slope of seven feet
horizontally for each foot vertically from the sides of the primary and
approach surfaces to where they intersect the horizontal and conical surfaces.
   TREE. Any object of natural growth.
   UTILITY RUNWAY. A runway that is constructed for and intended to be used by
propeller driven aircraft of 12,500 pounds’ maximum gross weight and less.
   VISUAL RUNWAY. A runway intended solely for the operation of aircraft using
visual approach procedures.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.108 AIRPORT ZONE; SUBZONES.
   In order to carry out the provisions of this subchapter, there are hereby
created and established certain subzones within the Airport Zone which include
all of the land lying beneath the approach surfaces as they apply to the
Nezperce Municipal Airport. Such subzones are shown of the Nezperce Municipal
Airport zoning map, consisting of one sheet, dated, which is attached to the
ordinance codified in this chapter and is on file in the City Clerk/Treasurer’s
office. An area which is located in more than one of the following subzones is
considered to be only in the zone with the more restrictive height limitation.
The various subzones are established and defined as follows.
   (A)   Utility Runway Visual Approach Zone. The inner edge of this approach
zone coincides with the width of the primary surface and is 250 feet wide. The
approach zone expands outward uniformly to a width of 1,250 feet at a
horizontal distance of 5,000 feet from the primary surface. Its centerline is
the continuation of the centerline of the runway.
   (B)   Transitional Zones. The transitional zones are the areas beneath the
transitional surfaces.
   (C)   Horizontal Zones. The horizontal zone is established by swinging arcs
of 5,000 feet radii from the center of each end of the primary surface of each
runway and connecting the adjacent arcs by drawing lines tangent to those arcs.
The horizontal zone does not include the approach and transitional zones.
   (D)   Conical Zone. The conical zone is established as the area that
commences at the periphery of the horizontal zone and extends outward therefrom
a horizontal distance of 4,000 feet.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.109 HEIGHT LIMITATIONS.
   (A)   Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, no structure shall be
erected, altered or maintained, and no trees or vegetation shall be allowed to
grow in any subzone created by this subchapter, any height of which exceeds the
applicable height limit herein established for such subzone established
follows:
      (1)   Utility Runway Visual Approach Zone. Slopes 20 feet outward for
each foot upward beginning at the end of and at the same elevation as the
primary surface and extending to a horizontal distance of 5,000 feet along the
extended runway centerline;
      (2)   Transitional Zones. Slope seven feet outward for each foot upward
beginning at the sides of and at the same elevation as the primary surface and
the approach surface, and extending to a height of 150 feet above the airport
elevation;
      (3)   Horizontal Zone. Established at 150 feet above the airport
elevation or at a height of 3,351 feet above mean sea level; and
      (4)   Conical Zone. A conical zone is an inclined surface at a slope of
20 to one (20:1) extending upward and outward from the periphery of the
horizontal surface for a horizontal distance of 4,000 feet. The elevation at
the outer edge of the conical zone is 3,551 feet MSL.
   (B)   Nothing in this subchapter shall be construed as prohibiting the
construction or maintenance of any structure, or growth of any tree to a height
up to 50 feet above the surface of the land, except as otherwise in this
chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.110 USE RESTRICTIONS.
   Notwithstanding any other provisions of this subchapter, no use may be made
of land or water with any zone or subzone established under this subchapter in
such a manner as to create electrical interference with navigational signals or
radio communications between the airport and aircraft, making it difficult for
pilots to distinguish between airport lights and others, result in glare in the
eyes of pilots the airport, create fire strike hazards or otherwise in any way
endanger or interfere with the landing, takeoff or maneuvering or aircraft
intending to use the airport.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.111 NON-CONFORMING USES.
   (A)   Regulations not retroactive. Except as otherwise provided in this
section, the provisions of this subchapter are subject to the provisions of §
155.108(B) of this chapter, pertaining to non-conforming uses, lots and
structures.
   (B)   Marking and lighting. Notwithstanding division (A) above, the owner of
any existing non- conforming structure or tree is required to permit the
installation, operation and maintenance thereon of such markers and lights as
shall be deemed necessary by the Airport Administrator, to indicate to the
operators of aircraft in the vicinity of the airport the presence of such
airport obstructions. Such markers and lights shall be installed operated and
maintained at the expense of the city.
   (C)   Non-conforming uses; abandoned or destroyed. Whenever the Airport
Administrator determines that a non-conforming tree or structure has been
abandoned or more than 80% torn down, physically deteriorated or decayed, that
particular non-conforming condition shall be changed or eliminated as to comply
with the restrictions set forth in this subchapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.112 VARIANCES.
   (A)   Variances; general.
      (1)   Except as others provided in this section, a variance of any
requirement, specification or standard under this subchapter may be applied for
and granted in the same manner as provided for variances under §§
155.200 through
155.204 of this chapter.
      (2)   In addition, the application for a variance shall be accompanied by
a determination from the Federal Aviation Administration as to the effect of
the proposal on the operation of air navigation facilities and the safe,
efficient use of navigable airspace.
      (3)   (a)   Variances may only be granted under the conditions identified
under §§
155.200 through
155.204 of this chapter, together with a finding by the City Council that
granting the variance will not create a hazard to air navigation or the public.
         (b)   Additionally, no application for a variance may be granted
unless a copy of the application has been furnished to the city’s Airport
Administrator for opinion as to the aeronautical effects of granting the
variance.
         (c)   Applications for variances shall be made to the Airport
Administrator upon a form published for the purpose.
      (4)   The Airport Administrator shall indicate upon the application his
or her recommendations and shall forthwith transmit them to the City Council
for consideration in processing the application.
   (B)   Additional conditions; marking lights. In addition to any other
conditions attached to the variance by the City Council, any variance granted
may, if such action is deemed advisable to effectuate the purpose of this
subchapter, require the owner of the structure or tree in question to install,
operate and maintain at the owner’s expense, such markings lights as deemed
necessary by the city.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.113 ENFORCEMENT.
   It shall be the duty of the Airport Administrator and Mayor to administer
and enforce the provisions of this subchapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.114 CONFLICTING REGULATIONS.
   Where there exists a conflict between any of the regulations or limitations
prescribed in this subchapter and any other regulations applicable to the same
area, whether this conflict be with respect to the height of structures, or
trees or any other matter, the more stringent limitation or requirement shall
govern and prevail.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.115 BOUNDARIES.
   Those certain lands situated within the following described portions of the
city: commencing at the point of intersection between parcel tax #D-107 and
parcel tax #D-98, said point of intersection located at the northern boundary
of city limits; thence running in a southeasterly direction between the
boundary of parcel tax #D-107 and parcel tax #D-98 to its point of intersection
with the northern boundary of Nezperce Lots 1 through 5, Block 5; thence
running in a easterly direction along the northern boundary of Nezperce Lots 1
through 5, Block 5, to its point of intersection with the centerline of Maple
Street; thence running in a southerly direction along the centerline of Maple
Street to its point of intersection with the centerline of 3rd Avenue; thence
running in an easterly direction along the centerline of 3rd Avenue to its
point of intersection with the centerline of the first alley east of Maple
Street; thence running in a southerly direction along the centerline of the
first alley east of Maple Street to its point of intersection with the
centerline of 4th Avenue; thence running in a easterly direction along the
centerline of 4th Avenue to its point of intersection with the centerline of
the unnamed street located between Maple Street and Cedar Street; thence
running in a northerly direction along the centerline of the unnamed street
located between Maple Street and Cedar Street to its point of intersection with
the northern boundary of city limits near 1st Avenue; thence running in a
westerly direction along the northern boundary of city limits near 1st Avenue
to the point where city limits turns in a northwesterly direction along the
airport; thence running in a northwesterly direction near the airport to its
point where city limits turns in a westerly direction; thence running in a
westerly direction to its point of intersection between parcel tax #D-107 and
parcel tax #D-98.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
SUPPLEMENTAL REGULATIONS AND REQUIREMENTS
§ 155.130 ZONING OF STREETS AND PUBLIC WAYS.
   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, all streets, alleys and public
ways shall be deemed to be situated in the same zoning district as the real
property within the city immediately abutting such street, alley or public way.
Where the centerline of a street, alley or public way is a zoning district
boundary, the zoning of such street, alley or public away abutting or part of
said zoning district shall apply to the centerline of said street, alley or
public way unless otherwise specifically designated in this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.131 UNAUTHORIZED DEVELOPMENT OR USE PROHIBITED; NON- CONFORMANCES.
   (A)   Unauthorized development or use prohibited. Unless otherwise provided
under this chapter, no structure may be erected, converted, enlarged,
reconstructed or structurally altered, nor shall any structure or lands be
developed or used for any purpose, except in compliance with this chapter.
   (B)   Non-conforming use/lot/structure. Unless otherwise provided in this
chapter, all non-conforming uses, lots and structures established prior to
enactment of this chapter may be continued and shall not constitute a violation
of this chapter, subject to the following terms and conditions.
      (1)   Notwithstanding any minimum requirements for lot size within the
applicable various zoning district, structures may be built, expanded,
reconstructed, occupied or used on a non-conforming lot that existed prior to
the enactment of this chapter; provided that, such structures and uses are
otherwise compliance with this chapter and all other applicable laws,
regulations, codes and ordinances.
      (2)   A structure occupied by a non-conforming use may be maintained and
repaired after enactment of this chapter; provided that, all such maintenance
and repairs shall be made and undertaken in compliance with this chapter and
all other applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances. Examples of
allowed maintenance are painting, re-roofing and steps to ensure safety and
compliance with building codes.
      (3)   When a structure housing a non-conforming use is illegally modified
or expanded, the non- conforming status of the structure or use shall be lost.
      (4)   A non-conforming structure may not be replaced except in compliance
with this chapter, but may be maintained, repaired or internally altered
provided that there is no increase in the degree of non-compliance with this
chapter.
      (5)   Expansion of any non-conforming use (and the structures and
buildings housing them) exceeding 20% of gross floor area is prohibited unless
authorized by permit issued by the City Council in accordance with the
procedures for issuance of conditional use permits under this chapter.
      (6)   Non-conforming uses may be converted to other uses upon issuance of
a permit by the City Council in accordance with the procedures for issuance of
conditional use permits under this chapter, if the City Council finds that:
         (a)   The conversion will not violate a policy of the city’s
Comprehensive Plan;
         (b)   The conversion will not unduly burden transportation or service
facilities;
         (c)   The conversion will not result in adverse impacts to surrounding
properties;
         (d)   The use proposed will be equal or less in intensity, impact and
demand for services; and
         (e)   The conversion will otherwise in the best interest of the city.
      (7)   When a non-conforming use has been materially changed, enlarged or
expanded, the non- conforming status shall be lost unless the change in use is
authorized to continue by permit issued by the City Council in accordance with
the procedures for issuance of conditional use permits under this chapter.
Unless authorized under a duly issued permit, the subject lands and structures
may only be used in compliance with this chapter.
      (8)   A non-conforming use that is discontinued for a continuous period
of one year after the date of enactment of this chapter shall be presumptively
deemed to have been abandoned or discontinued. Thereafter, the subject lands
and structures may only be used in compliance with this chapter; provided,
however, that, this division (B)(8) shall not deprive the use of the structures
or other improvements on private property based solely on non-use of the
structures and improvements for their designed purposes for a period of ten
years or less.
      (9)   Non-conforming status shall be lost when a non-conforming structure
or a structure occupied by a non-conforming use is destroyed by fire or other
calamity or casualty to the extent that the cost of restoration is 50% or more
of the assessed value of said structure, unless the non-conforming status is
authorized to continue by permit issued by the City Council in accordance with
the procedures for issuance of conditional use permits under this chapter.
Unless authorized under a duly issued permit, the affected structure or
building may only be used in compliance with this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.132 HEIGHT OF STRUCTURES AND ANTENNAS.
   (A)   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, no structure may be erected
to exceed by more than 25 feet height of the applicable structure height limits
for the zoning district in which it is situated.
   (B)   Communications, television, telephone, internet, radio or similar
aerials and antennas shall not exceed 60 feet in height above the ground level.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.133 YARD AREA; CALCULATION.
   (A)   No space which, for the purpose of a structure has been counted or
calculated as part of a side yard, rear yard, front yard, court or other open
space required by this chapter may, by reason of change in ownership or
otherwise, be counted or calculated to satisfy or comply with a yard, court or
other open space requirement of or for any other building.
   (B)   The minimum yards or other open spaces, including lot areas per family
required by this chapter for each and every building existing or for any
building hereafter erected, shall not be encroached upon or considered as a
yard or open space requirements for any other building,
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.134 TERRACES.
   An open terrace, but not including a roofed-over porch or terrace, may
occupy a front yard provided the unoccupied portion of the front yard has a
