depth of not less than 15 feet. A one-story bay window may project into a front
yard not more than three feet. Overhanging eaves, including gutters, may
project over the minimum required side yard not more than 24 inches.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.135 MANUFACTURED HOMES.
   Development standards for a manufactured home or mobile home on any lot are
as follows.
   (A)   Any manufactured home or mobile home installed, placed or situated on
any lands within the city after enactment of this chapter for purposes of
occupancy or use as a dwelling shall:
      (1)   Have an enclosed living space of not less than 1,000 square feet;
      (2)   Have a non-metallic, wood or asphalt shingle roof, shall have a
pitched roof with a slope not greater than a nominal three feet in height for
each 12 feet in width and a minimum six-inch eave, or gutter and eave attached
to the entire perimeter of the roof;
      (3)   Have exterior siding and roofing which in color, material and
appearance is similar to the exterior siding and roofing material commonly used
on residential dwellings within the community;
      (4)   Be installed and placed on an excavated and backfilled foundation
and enclosed at the perimeter such that the home is located not less than 12
inches above the grade, and be permanently affixed, with the running gear and
towing hitch removed and set upon a foundation base having an anchoring system
that is totally concealed under the structure; and
      (5)   Comply with all other applicable requirements of the zoning
district in which the manufactured home or mobile home is situated (such as lot
size and setback requirements), and comply with all other applicable laws,
regulations and ordinances.
   (B)   The assembly, installation, placement and siting of the manufactured
home or mobile home shall otherwise comply with this chapter and all other
applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.136 ONE DWELLING PER LOT.
   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, no more than one structure,
manufactured home or mobile home may be constructed, maintained or used as a
dwelling or dwelling unit on any lot.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.137 SUBSTANDARD LOTS.
   The city may, by duly granted conditional use permit, allow any lot that
does not meet the requirements of this chapter for yards, courts or other area
of open space to be utilized for single-family residential purposes so long the
requirements for such yard, court or open space is within 75% of that required
by this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.138 ACCESS TO PUBLIC WAY REQUIRED.
   No building may be constructed, erected or maintain upon any lot that does
not abut upon a public street, or that does not then have perpetual legal right
of access from the lot to a public street established of record as shown in the
official property records of the county. Said perpetual legal right of access
shall be a minimum width of 25 feet unless said legal access was established of
record as a lesser width prior to enactment of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.139 TRAFFIC/SIGHT OBSTRUCTIONS.
   Unless authorized by the City Council, no owner of any lot shall cause,
permit or suffer any trees, shrubbery, hedges, walls, fences, gates, buildings,
structures or other improvements, or any portion thereof, situated on said lot
to encroach upon, obstruct or interfere with the use of any public sidewalk,
alley, street or public way, or to obstruct or interfere with traffic
visibility from any adjacent public sidewalks, alleys, streets or public ways.
Unless otherwise authorized by the City Council, all such improvements on any
lot shall be maintained at a distance of six to 12 inches from inside the
exterior lot boundary. All such improvements situated on the lot with within 50
feet of the corner of the block in which said lot is situated shall not exceed
three feet in height above the curb line for the adjacent street.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.140 EXISTING CONSTRUCTION PROJECTS.
   Nothing in this chapter shall be deemed to require any change in the place,
construction or designed use of any structure upon a lot which actual
construction was lawfully commenced prior to enactment this chapter, and the
construction of which has been diligently carried on and is completed within
one year from the date of enactment of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.141 ACCESSORY BUILDINGS.
   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, accessory buildings shall be
subject to the following additional regulations.
   (A)   Where an accessory building is structurally attached to a main
building, it shall be subject and must conform to, all provisions of this
chapter applicable to the main building.
   (B)   An accessory building may not be located nearer than five feet to any
interior lot line and not nearer than five feet to the rear lot line on any
lot.
   (C)   An accessory building shall not be erected on any lot prior to
construction of the main building on said lot.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.142 STANDS FOR SALE OF MERCHANDISE OR PRODUCE PROHIBITED.
   Unless permitted by the city provided in this section, the storage, display
or sale of goods, merchandise or produce shall not be permitted on or from any
public property, public sidewalks, streets, alleys or public ways situated
within any zoning district. The City Council may issue permits allowing such
activities on terms and conditions the City Council deems in the best interest
of the city; provided, however, that, the effective duration of any such permit
so issued shall not exceed four days in any one calendar month per applicant.
The City Council may place such other conditions on any permit issued by the
City Council pursuant to this section as it deems in the best interest of the
city.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.143 MAINTENANCE OF PROPERTY; GARBAGE CANS, RECEPTACLES.
   Unless otherwise authorized by the city, no owner or occupant of any lot
shall cause, permit or suffer any solid waste, garbage, junk, inoperable or
abandoned vehicles, or other refuse collected or generated on or from said lot
to accumulate upon said lot outside of an enclosed structure situated on the
lot:
   (A)   So as to constitute a public or private nuisance or health or safety
hazard to any person or property;
   (B)   So as to obstruct any public property, public sidewalk, public street,
alley or public way; or
   (C)   In any manner in violation of any applicable laws, regulations, codes
or ordinances.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.144 PARKING.
   All bed and breakfasts, boarding houses, motels, hotels and apartments shall
have off-street parking equal or greater to the number of guest rooms available
for rent.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.145 SIDING AND ROOFING.
   Structures of any kind or character within the city shall be roofed and
sided in accordance with the applicable provisions of the city’s Building Code.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.146 SHIPPING CONTAINERS.
   Shipping containers, as that term is generally understood in the freight
industry, and enclosed cargo van trailers, sometimes locally known as semi-
trailers, as herein defined, in permanent use as of the effective date hereof
may continue to be used; provided that, its location does not change in Zones
A, B and C. Shipping containers are allowed for business use in the Business
District of Zone C and in Zone D and does not have to be permanently placed in
one location.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.147 CONDITIONAL USES; CONDITIONAL USE PERMITS.
   (A)   Authority to issue; allowable conditional uses in any zoning district.
      (1)   The City Council may issue conditional use permits to authorize use
of lands within the city not otherwise permitted in a zoning district under
this chapter, subject to the provisions of this section. The term CONDITIONAL
USE PERMIT, as used in this chapter, shall have the same meaning as a special
use permit as provided in Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended.
      (2)   Unless otherwise provided by this chapter, the following uses of
lots and structures may be permitted by the city as a conditional use within
any zoning district by issuance of a conditional use permit subject to the
provisions of this chapter:
         (a)   Accessory buildings, structures and parking areas for any
permitted conditional use;
         (b)   Banks, credit unions and other financial institutions;
         (c)   Bed and breakfasts, boarding houses and lodging houses;
         (d)   Billboards;
         (e)   Bus terminal, railroad passenger station or any other
transportation terminal facilities;
         (f)   Cemeteries, crematories or mausoleums;
         (g)   Churches and accessory buildings used for religious teaching;
         (h)   Communication antennae and towers;
         (i)   Community halls and centers, public or private;
         (j)   Extraction of gravel, sand or other raw materials;
         (k)   Florist shops and greenhouses;
         (l)   Grocery, mini-marts and convenience stores;
         (m)   Hospitals, sanitariums, clinics, quick-care clinics and medical,
dental, therapy and counseling offices;
         (n)   Libraries and museums;
         (o)   Municipal and government buildings, structures and facilities;
         (p)   Nursery schools, day nurseries and childcare centers;
         (q)   Parking lots and areas, public and private;
         (r)   Police stations, fire stations or place for storage of municipal
property or equipment;
         (s)   Professional services, including, but not limited to, legal,
accounting, engineering, architectural investment and financial, insurance and
real estate services;
         (t)   Public administration buildings, auditoriums, gymnasiums or any
other publicly-owned structures;
         (u)   Public or private park or playground, including rodeo and sports
arenas and grounds;
         (v)   Public or private utility facilities, including, but not limited
to, water, sewer, garbage, communications, telephone, television, internet,
electricity and other similar facilities;
         (w)   Public or private monuments;
         (x)   Railroad right-of-way;
         (y)   Recreation centers and facilities, public or private;
         (z)   Schools, public or private;
         (aa)   Sport shooting ranges as may otherwise be permitted by law;
         (bb)   Manufactured/mobile home and recreational vehicle courts and
parks may be permitted as a conditional use within Residence Zones A or B, and
Zone D within the city, and may be additionally be located within Zone C if
outside the Business District;
         (cc)   Telephone or communication exchange facilities;
         (dd)   Undertaking establishments; and
         (ee)   Veterinary clinics and hospitals.
   (B)   Applications; fees. Applications for conditional use permits must be
filed with the City Clerk/Treasurer and shall be referred to the City Council
for hearing and decision as hereafter provided. Applications must be signed by
the applicant and the record fee title owner of the subject lot consenting to
the application. The applicant shall provide the city all information deemed
necessary by the City Council to process the application. The City Council may
by resolution from time to time establish and amend a fee schedule for
conditional use permit applications, including fees sufficient to pay the cost
of any notices, publications and inspections required by law or otherwise
deemed necessary to process the application. The applicant shall pay the
applicable conditional use permit application fee at the time the application
is filed with the city. The city shall have no obligation to process any
application filed with the city unless the applicable application fee is paid
in full by the applicant. The City Council shall have the authority to waive
all or any portion of the applicable application fee when it deems such a
waiver to be in the best interest of the city.
   (C)   Hearing; decision; conditions; judicial review. Prior to granting or
denying a conditional use permit, the city shall comply with the notice and
hearing requirements under Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended,
applicable to special use permit applications. Unless otherwise determined by
resolution of the City Council, the public hearing on the application shall be
initially commenced within 30 days after all notices required by law have been
duly given. In addition:
      (1)   The approval or denial of any conditional use permit application
shall be based upon standards and criteria which are set forth in the
Comprehensive Plan, this chapter, other applicable city ordinances and as
otherwise provided by law, including, but not limited to, Idaho Code Chapter
65, Title 67, as amended. In addition, no conditional use permit may be granted
unless the City Council finds that issuance of the conditional use permit is:
         (a)   Consistent with the city’s Comprehensive Plan; and
         (b)   In the best interest of the public.
      (2)   The approval or denial of any application provided for in this
section shall be accompanied by a written decision of the city in compliance
with Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended;
      (3)   The City Council may attach conditions to conditional use permits
issued as deemed in the best interest of the city, including, but not limited
to, any conditions authorized under Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as
amended; and
      (4)   Judicial review of any final decision of the city under this
section may be taken in the same manner as provided for judicial review of
final local land use planning decisions under Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65,
as amended.
   (D)   Applicability/non-transferability of permits. Unless otherwise
provided in the issued conditional use permit, a conditional use permit issued
by the city shall apply to and run with the lot for which the permit is issued
only, and shall inure to benefit of the owner and the owner’s successors in
interest to the subject lot. A conditional use permit is not transferable from
one lot to another. A conditional use permit shall not be considered as
establishing a binding precedent to grant other or additional conditional use
permits.
   (E)   Violation. It shall be a violation of this chapter for any person to
violate any term or condition of any conditional use permit issued by the city
pursuant to this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.148 DEVELOPMENT AGREEMENTS.
   (A)   In addition to any other conditions authorized under this chapter, the
city may require or permit as a condition of issuing any conditional use
permit, or other permit or license, or for granting any variance or request to
rezone, that the subject lot owner and developer, or either of them, enter into
a development agreement with the city containing the lot owner’s and/or
developer’s written commitment to the city concerning the use or development of
the subject lot as provided in Idaho Code § 67-6511A, as amended, on and
containing such terms and conditions as the City Council deems in the best
interest of the city.
   (B)   (1)   All development agreements shall be in writing, and shall be
duly executed acknowledged by the lot owner and/or developer as may be
applicable.
      (2)   Developer agreements shall be recorded in the official real
property records of the County Recorder.
   (C)   (1)   Unless terminated, a developer agreement made or amended
pursuant to this section is binding on the developer and all owners of the
subject lot, and shall also be binding on every subsequent owner, and each
other person acquiring an interest in lot as provided in this section.
      (2)   A development agreement is binding on the lot owner and developer
even if it is unrecorded; however, an unrecorded development agreement is
binding on all subsequent owners or other person acquiring an interest in the
lot only if the subsequent owner or other person has actual notice of the
commitment.
   (D)   A development agreement may only be amended or terminated, in whole in
part, upon compliance with the notice and hearing provisions of Idaho Code §
67-6509, as amended. A development agreement may be terminated, and any zoning
designation upon which the use is based reversed, for violation of any term or
condition of the development agreement as provided in §§
155.215 through
155.217 of this chapter.
   (E)   (1)   Requiring or permitting any development agreement as a condition
of any conditional use permit, other permit or license, variance or request for
rezone, shall not obligate the city to recommend, issue, grant or adopt any
such conditional use permit, other permit or license, variance or request for
rezone, or any ordinance necessary to effectuate the same.
      (2)   Nothing in this section is intend to, nor shall it, apply to,
prohibit, impair or otherwise affect the authority of the city to place
conditions on issuing or granting any conditional use permit, variance or
rezone request that the city determines does not necessitate a development
agreement with the lot owner or developer.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
MANUFACTURED/MOBILE HOME AND RECREATIONAL VEHICLE COURTS AND PARKS
§ 155.160 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   HOUSING SPACE. A plot of ground within a manufactured/mobile home or
recreational vehicle court or park designated for the accommodation of one
mobile home, manufactured home or recreational vehicle for occupancy.
   MANUFACTURED HOME, MOBILE HOME and RECREATIONAL VEHICLE. The terms
“manufactured home”, “mobile home” and recreational vehicle” shall each have
the same definitions as provided in §
155.004 of this chapter.
   MANUFACTURED/MOBILE HOME COURT OR PARK. Any lot upon which two or more
manufactured homes or mobile homes, or any combination thereof, are situated
for purposes of occupancy by person(s) other than the owner of said parcel or
lot, including, but not limited under, any long-term or short-term rental or
lease arrangement with the owner.
   RECREATIONAL VEHICLE COURT OR PARK. Any lot, including but not limited to
any manufactured/mobile home court or park, upon which two or more recreational
vehicles are situated for purposes of occupancy by person(s) other than the
owner of said parcel or lot, including, but not limited under, any long-term or
short-term rental or lease arrangement with the parcel or owner.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.161 APPLICABILITY; RV PARK PERMIT REQUIRED.
   (A)   Compliance. Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, this
subchapter shall apply to all manufactured/mobile home courts and parks, and
all recreational vehicle courts and parks, within the city. All manufactured/
mobile home courts and parks and all recreation vehicle courts and parks within
the city subject to this subchapter shall be in compliance with the provisions
of this subchapter.
   (B)   RV park permits required. No person shall own, maintain or operate any
recreational vehicle court or park within the city without a recreational
vehicle park permit issued by the city as provided in this subchapter.
      (1)   Authority to issue. The City Council may issue recreational vehicle
park permits (hereafter “RV park permits”) pursuant to this section.
      (2)   Applications; fees.
         (a)   Applications for RV park permits must be filed with the City
Clerk/Treasurer and shall be referred to the City Council for decision as
hereafter provided. Applications must be signed by the applicant and the record
fee title owner of the affected property consenting to the application, and
shall include a written plan for the proposed recreational vehicle park,
including, but not limited to, the following information:
            1.   The extent and area used for recreational vehicles parking
purposes;
            2.   Roadways and driveways;
            3.   The location of housing spaces sites and for motor vehicle
parking;
            4.   The location and number of sanitary conveniences, including
toilets, service rooms, washrooms, laundries and utility rooms, to be used by
the occupants of recreational vehicles;
            5.   Method and plan of sewage disposal, coupled with
certifications by the State Sanitarian that the plan of sewage disposal would
be approved upon completion;
            6.   A method and plan of garbage removal, all in accordance with
the city’s solid waste standards;
            7.   A method and plan for water supply, for potable water, a plan
for light, for fire protection and irrigation all as required by the Fire Code
and the state’s Department of Health and Welfare Health District; and
            8.   Provide reasonable plans for appropriate attractive
landscaping.
         (b)   The application shall also include all other information deemed
necessary by the city to process the application. The City Council may by
resolution from time to time establish and amend a fee schedule for
applications for RV park permits, including fees sufficient to pay the cost of
any notices, publications or inspections required by law or otherwise deemed
necessary by the city to process the application. The applicant shall pay the
applicable application fee at the time the application is filed with the city.
The city shall have no obligation to process any application filed with the
city unless the applicable application fee is paid in full by the applicant.
The City Council shall have the authority to waive all or any portion of the
applicable application fee when it deems such a waiver to be in the best
interest of the city.
   (C)   Hearing; decision; conditions; judicial review. Prior to granting or
denying a RV park permit, the city shall comply with the notice and hearing
requirements under Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended, applicable to
special use permit applications. Unless otherwise determined by resolution of
the City Council, the public hearing on the application shall be initially
commenced within 30 days after all notices required by law have been made. In
addition:
      (1)   The approval or denial of any application shall be based upon
standards and criteria which are set forth in the Comprehensive Plan, this
subchapter and other applicable city ordinances and regulations, as otherwise
provided in Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended. In addition, no RV
park permit may be granted unless the City Council finds that issuance the
permit is:
         (a)   Not inconsistent with the city’s Comprehensive Plan; and
         (b)   In the best interest of the public.
      (2)   The approval or denial of any application provided for in this
section shall be accompanied by a written decision of the city in compliance
with Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended;
      (3)   The City Council may attach conditions to RV park permits issued as
deemed in the best interest of the city, including, but not limited to, any
conditions authorized under Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended; and
      (4)   Judicial review of any final decision of the city under this
section may be taken tn the same manner as provided for judicial review of
final local land use planning decisions under Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65,
as amended.
   (D)   Non-transferability of permits. Unless otherwise provided in the
issued RV park permit, an RV park permit issued by the city shall apply to and
run with the land for which the permit is issued only, and shall inure to
benefit of the owner and the owner’s successors in interest to said land. An RV
park permit is not transferable from one parcel of land to another. An RV park
permit shall not be considered as establishing a binding precedent to grant
other conditional use permits.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022) Penalty, see §
155.999
§ 155.162 EXCEPTION; EXISTING COURTS/PARKS; VARIANCES.
   (A)   Notwithstanding any other provision of this subchapter, manufactured/
mobile home and recreation vehicle courts and parks existing within the city as
of the date of enactment of this subchapter shall be exempt from the provisions
of this subchapter as non-conforming uses, subject to provisions of §§
155.005,
155.130 through
155.148,
155.200 through
155.204 and
155.215 through
155.217 of this chapter as may be applicable.
   (B)   Except as others provided in this section, a variance of any
requirement, specification or standard under this subchapter may be applied for
and granted in the same manner as provided for variances under §§
155.005,
155.130 through
155.148,
155.200 through
155.204 and
155.215 through
155.217 of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.163 IMPROVEMENTS.
   (A)   In addition to all other requirements under this subchapter, all
manufactured/mobile home and recreational vehicle courts or parks shall have or
provide:
      (1)   A convenient means of pedestrian and vehicular access to each unit
space, parking areas and service buildings;
      (2)   An adequate lawful supply of potable water;
      (3)   Lawful method for disposal of sewage and solid waste generated from
or collected on the site;
      (4)   Electrical service for lighting and power; and
      (5)   Diversion of surface water away from buildings, unit spaces,
service and recreational areas, and its disposal for the site.
   (B)   All improvements required under this subchapter shall be:
      (1)   Designed and constructed in compliance with ail applicable laws,
regulations, codes and ordinances; and
      (2)   Kept in good, safe, clean and sanitary condition and repair by the
owner of said court or park.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.164 ADDITIONAL REQUIREMENTS; SPACING, ROADS AND THE LIKE.
   (A)   General. Each manufactured/mobile home and recreational vehicle court
or park shall be designed, constructed and maintained in compliance with the
provisions of this subchapter. The owner of any proposed new manufactured/
mobile home or recreational vehicle court or park created or established after
enactment of this chapter must prepare and submit a site plan for approval by
the city indicating the layout of housing spaces, roads, walks, service
buildings, service areas, utilities and grading within said court or park prior
to commencement of construction or operation of said court or park.
   (B)   Spacing requirements.
      (1)   Recreational vehicles.
         (a)   The minimum space between recreational vehicles, and between
said recreation vehicles and any structure, must be as follows:
            1.   Side to side spacing: not less than 15 feet; and
            2.   End to end spacing: not less than ten feet.
         (b)   No recreational vehicle housing space shall be located closer
than 25 feet from the right-of-way line of a main street or ten feet from any
court or park property line. All spacing requirements shall be as measured from
the closest point on the recreational vehicle’s body to the nearest other
recreational vehicle, structure, street or property line as applicable.
      (2)   Mobile homes and manufactured homes. The minimum setback and
spacing requirements for mobile homes and manufactured homes situated within
any manufactured/mobile home court or park shall be the same as applicable in
the applicable zoning district as if said units were framed construction house
and/or buildings.
   (C)   Roads, walks and parking areas.
      (1)   General requirements. Safety and convenience must be a major
consideration in the layout of roads, walks and parking areas within any
manufactured/mobile home or recreational vehicle court or park. All roads
within said court or park must be continuous, unless a road ends in an
appropriate cul-de-sac the design of which shall be in accordance with Chapter
157.
      (2)   Servicing. Suitable vehicular access for firefighting equipment
delivery of fuel, removal of garbage and refuse and for other necessary
services must be provided, and shall otherwise be in compliance with all
applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances.
      (3)   Widths of main access road. Main access roads within any trailer,
double-wide manufactured home or recreational vehicle court or park shall be
two lane, with an improved traveled width of not less than 38 feet wide.
      (4)   Parking area. The same number of off-street motor vehicle parking
spaces must be provided within the court or park as the number of manufactured/
mobile home and recreational vehicle housing spaces within the court or park.
   (D)   Service buildings. Each manufactured/mobile home or recreational
vehicle court or park that provide more than one housing space for recreational
vehicles must provide one or more service buildings containing the requisite
number of plumbing fixtures and other service equipment as described in this
section. Each required service building must conform to the following
requirements.
      (1)   Location. The service building shall be located not more than 200
feet from any dependent recreational vehicle housing space.
      (2)   Construction. The design and construction of service buildings must
conform to all applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances, including,
but not limited to, the Federal Americans with Disabilities Act, being 42
U.S.C. §§ 12101 et seq.
      (3)   Restroom facilities. Separate men’s and women’s restrooms must be
provided and distinctly marked. A vestibule or screen wall must be provided to
prevent direct view into the restrooms when exterior doors are open.
      (4)   Plumbing. Adequate laundry facilities, which must be separate and
apart from toilet rooms. Furthermore, there must be separate shower facilities
for men and women. All plumbing installations shall be made and maintained in
compliance with all applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances.
      (5)   Electrical. All electrical installations shall be made and
maintained in compliance with all applicable laws, regulations, codes and
ordinances.
      (6)   Refuse collections. Refuse collection facilities must conform and
be maintained in compliance with all applicable laws, regulations, codes and
ordinances.
      (7)   Site engineering.
         (a)   Grading and drainage must be designed and constructed so that
water will drain away from housing spaces, service buildings and common areas
within the court or park, and off the site in a manner in compliance with all
applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances.
         (b)   Walks, driveways and retaining walls must be so constructed as
not to interfere with drainage.
      (8)   Slopes of housing spaces, roads, walks and service areas.
         (a)   Housing spaces must be graded toward abutting roadway to prevent
surface water draining across adjacent housing spaces. Grading under housing
spaces shall be provided to prevent puddling of water.
         (b)   Where swales for the carriers of storm water are needed or
required between housing spaces and any roadway, they must be of a shallow
type, generally not to exceed eight inches in depth.
         (c)   Unless otherwise specified by a licensed engineer or the city,
the following minimum and maximum slope values shall be applicable:
 
                 Minimum Slope Percent Maximum Slope Percent
Housing space     0.50                  5
Recreation areas  0.50                  4
Roads             0.50                  8
Sod/planted areas 1.00                  10
Walks             0.50                  10
 
      (9)   Construction of roads, parking areas, walks and service areas.
         (a)   Roads and parking areas. Roads must be constructed of concrete
or asphalt or of gravel, crushed stone, slag or other locally available
suitable materials, with a light bituminous surface treatment, and treated with
a legally acceptable dust preventive material. Roads must be crowned at the
center to shed water to drainage facilities.
         (b)   Walks. Walks must be constructed of concrete unless the
developer proposes an alternate plan which would provide safe and stable
footing from among the following other materials, asphalt, gravel, fine stone
or cinders. Any plan must show the proposed location of sidewalks, paths and
streets within any court with each such improvements being separately located,
identified and defined. Sidewalks shall be located adjacent to all interior
streets unless waived by the City Council for good cause shown.
      (10)   Management. In every manufactured/mobile home or recreational
vehicle court or park that provides more than one housing space for
recreational vehicles, there shall be an on-site office attended by the person
in charge of said court or park. It is hereby made the duty of the park owner
and each attendant or person in charge on-site to:
         (a)   Maintain all roads, common areas and service buildings in a
clean, orderly and sanitary conditional at all times;
         (b)   Prevent animals kept or harbored within the court or park from
running at large or otherwise becoming a nuisance;
         (c)   Maintain the required office area at least one approved fire
extinguisher or such additional numbers as the otherwise required by the Fire
Code; and
         (d)   Prevent open fires within the court or park, except as allowed
in approved appliances or enclosures.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.165 UNLAWFUL ACTS; TEMPORARY OCCUPANCY PERMITS.
   (A)   Additional unlawful acts.
      (1)   It shall be unlawful for any person to park any mobile home,
manufactured home or recreational vehicle upon or within any street, alley,
way, highway or other public place within the city, except that motorized
recreational vehicles may be parked in vehicle parking spaces designated by the
city or highway agency with jurisdiction; provided that, they are parked in
compliance with all applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances. Unless
otherwise authorized by the city or highway agency with jurisdiction, no mobile
home, manufactured home or recreational vehicle parked, whether lawfully or
unlawfully, upon or within any street, alley, way, highway or other public
place within the city may be occupied or used for residential, dwelling or
business purposes for any period of time while so parked.
      (2)   It shall be unlawful for any person to park any mobile home,
manufactured home or recreational vehicle on any private property within the
city:
         (a)   Without the consent of the owner of said private property; and
         (b)   As otherwise in compliance with this subchapter and all
applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances.
      (3)   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, it shall be unlawful for
any person to use or occupy any recreational vehicle situated upon any lot for
residential or dwelling purposes for any period of time exceeding a total of
seven days in any calendar year, except within an approved manufactured/ mobile
home or recreational vehicle court or park, as defined in this subchapter.
   (B)   Temporary occupancy permits.
      (1)   Authority to issue. Notwithstanding any of the other provisions of
this chapter, the City Council may issue temporary occupancy permits
authorizing temporary use and occupancy of any recreational vehicle otherwise
prohibited under this chapter as provided in this section.
      (2)   Temporary occupancy permits.
         (a)   Authority to issue. The City Council may issue temporary
occupancy permits to authorize temporary use or occupancy of a recreational
vehicle otherwise prohibited under this subchapter as provided in this section.
         (b)   Applications; fees.
            1.   Applications for temporary occupancy permits must be filed
with the City Clerk/Treasurer and shall be referred to the City Council for
decision as hereafter provided. Applications must be signed by the applicant
and the record fee title owner of the lot where the recreational vehicle will
be used or occupied under the permit consenting to the application. The
applicant shall provide the city all information deemed necessary by the City
Council to process the application, including, but not limited to:
               a.   The legal description of the lot where the recreational
vehicle will be used or occupied;
               b.   The name and address of the record owner of said lot;
               c.   The scope of the intended use or occupancy, including the
number of persons who will use/occupy the recreational vehicle; and
               d.   The requested duration for the permit.
            2.   The City Council may, by resolution, from time to time
establish and amend a fee schedule for applications for temporary occupancy
permits, including fees sufficient to pay the cost of any notices, publications
or inspections required by law or otherwise determined necessary by the city to
process the application. The applicant shall pay the applicable application fee
at the time the application is filed with the city. The city shall have no
obligation to process any application filed with the city unless the applicable
application fee is paid in full by the applicant. The City Council shall have
the authority to waive all or any portion of the application fee when it deems
such a waiver to be in the best interest of the city.
         (c)   Hearing; decision; conditions; judicial review. Prior to
granting or denying a temporary occupancy permit, the city shall comply with
the notice and hearing requirements under Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as
amended, applicable to special use permit applications. Unless otherwise
determined by resolution of the City Council, the public hearing on the
application shall be initially commenced within 30 days after all notices
required by law have been duly given. In addition:
            1.   The approval or denial of any application shall be based upon
standards and criteria set forth in the Comprehensive Plan, this chapter and
other applicable city ordinances and regulations, as otherwise provided in
Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended. In addition, no temporary
occupancy permit may be granted unless the City Council finds that issuance of
the conditional use permit is:
               a.   Consistent with the city’s Comprehensive Plan; and
               b.   In the best interest of the public.
            2.   The approval or denial of any application provided for in this
section shall be accompanied by a written decision of the city in compliance
with Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended.
         (d)   Duration. Notwithstanding any other provision of this section,
no temporary occupancy permit may be issued nor shall remain in effect for an
effective duration longer than 180 days from the date of issuance of the
permit; provided, however, that, the City Council may issue renewed permits
upon new application by the permit holder, including, but not limited to,
payment any application permit renewal fee. Each temporary occupancy permit
shall state a commencement date and termination date for the permit subject to
the provisions of this division (B)(2). The temporary occupancy permit shall
automatically terminate upon expiration of the termination date stated in the
permit unless the permit is renewed prior to expiration of the current
temporary occupancy permit as provided under this division (B)(2).
         (e)   Conditions. The City Council may attach conditions to temporary
occupancy permits issued as deemed in the best interest of the city, including,
but not limited to, any conditions authorized under Idaho Code Title 67,
Chapter 65, as amended.
      (3)   Judicial review. Judicial review of any final decision of the city
under this section may be taken in the same manner as provided for judicial
review of final local land use planning decisions under Idaho Code Title 67,
Chapter 65, as amended.
      (4)   Applicability/non-transferability of permits. Unless otherwise
provided in the issued temporary occupancy permit, a temporary permit issued by
the city shall apply to the applicant and permitted occupants for the subject
lot specified in the permit for the duration of the permit only. A temporary
occupancy permit is not transferable to any other person, recreational vehicle
or from one lot to another. A temporary occupancy permit shall not be
considered as establishing a binding precedent to renew any existing occupancy
permit or grant other or additional temporary occupancy permits.
      (5)   Violations.
         (a)   It shall be a violation of this subchapter for any person to
violate any term or condition of this chapter, or any temporary occupancy
permit issued by the city pursuant to this chapter.
         (b)   In addition to all other remedies of the city, which shall be
non-exclusive and cumulative, the city may revoke any temporary occupancy
permit in the event the permit holder is in violation of terms or conditions of
the permit or is otherwise in violation of the provisions of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.166 ENFORCEMENT; VIOLATIONS.
   The provisions of this subchapter may be enforced by the city in the same
manner as provided for enforcement of the city’s Building Code as set forth in
§§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
BUILDING CODE
§ 155.180 TITLE.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall be known as the “Nezperce Building
Code”.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.181 APPLICABILITY.
   The provisions of this subchapter, including, but not limited to, all
adopted codes, shall be applicable to all lands, buildings, structures and
improvements situated within the city in accordance its provisions.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.182 CODE ADOPTION.
   (A)   Copies of adopted codes. One copy of each code adopted under division
(B) below shall be kept in the office of the Clerk/Treasurer of the city and
shall be made available for public inspection in the Clerk/Treasurer’s office
during normal business hours.
   (B)   Adopted codes. The following codes are hereby adopted by the city for
regulation of the erection, construction, enlargement, alteration, repair,
moving, conversion, occupancy, use, height, area and maintenance of all
buildings and structures situated within the city, including, but not limited
to, installation of manufactured homes in accordance with the provision of
Idaho Code Title 44, Chapter 22, excluding all fee schedules contained in said
adopted codes.
      (1)   State codes.
         (a)   Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, the city hereby
adopts the current editions of the following codes, published by the
International Code Council, as adopted and amended by the state’s Division of
Building Safety, state’s Building Code Board or otherwise by the state,
together with any amendments or revisions set forth in Idaho Code § 39-4109, as
amended, and including subsequent versions of said adopted codes:
            1.   International Building Code, including all rules promulgated
by the Board to provide equivalency with the provisions of the Americans with
Disabilities Act, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 12101 et seq. accessibility guidelines and
the Federal Fair Housing Act, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 3601 through 3619
accessibility guidelines;
            2.   International Residential Code, parts I through IV and IX; and
            3.   International Energy Conservation Code, excluding all fee
schedules, and excluding any reference to the flood requirements which shall be
governed by Chapter 154 of this code of ordinances. The adopted versions of the
foregoing codes shall be deemed superseded by successive versions of the codes
as they are amended and adopted by the state or state’s Building Code Board.
         (b)   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, the adopted versions
of the foregoing codes as set forth above shall be deemed superseded by
successive versions of or amendments to said codes when the same are adopted by
the State Division of Building Safety, State Building Code Board or otherwise
by the state, for application within the state.
      (2)   Additional adopted codes.
         (a)   Except as otherwise provided in this chapter, the city hereby
adopts the current editions of the following additional codes and regulations
as published by the publishers of said codes as of the date of adoption hereof,
excluding all fee schedules, and excluding any reference to flood requirements
which shall be governed by Chapter 154 of this code of ordinances: the latest
edition of the Uniform Code for the Abatement of Dangerous Buildings prepared
by the International Conference of Building Officials (ICBO).
         (b)   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, the adopted versions
of the foregoing codes as set forth above shall be deemed superseded by
successive versions of or amendments to said codes when the same are published
by the publisher of said codes.
   (C)   Mobile homes, manufactured homes and modular buildings. The
installation, erection and/or assembly of mobile homes, manufactured homes and
modular buildings, shall be governed and performed in compliance with all
applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances, including but not limited
to all regulations and standards of the state’s Division of Building Safety. In
addition:
      (1)   No mobile home, manufactured home or modular building over 20 years
old shall be installed on a building site unless the same is in compliance with
all applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances, including, but not
limited to, all rules and regulations of the state’s Division of Building
Safety; and
      (2)   Unless otherwise provided in this chapter, any manufactured home or
mobile home installed within the city after enactment of this chapters,
including within a manufacture/mobile home court or park, or recreational
vehicle court or park, must have a roof or self-supporting roof structure
covering the entire roof (i.e., a ramada) of said manufactured home or mobile
home with no less than 65 pounds per square foot snow-load capacity. Design and
construction of the self-supporting roof cover shall be subject to all
applicable laws, regulations, codes and ordinances.
   (D)   Exemptions.
      (1)   Agricultural buildings. Agricultural buildings shall be exempt from
the requirements of this chapter; provided, they are situated on land actively
devoted to agricultural pursuits as defined by Idaho Code Title 63, Chapter 6,
and are, at the time of application, being assessed as lands actively devoted
to agriculture. An AGRICULTURAL BUILDING is defined as any structure on land
actively devoted to agriculture that is used solely for growing, raising or
producing plants, animals or crops, and not primarily for human occupation or
habitation. An agricultural exemption permit is still required, and the permit
shall be governed by the laws in effect at the time a complete permit
application is received. An agricultural exemption permit will be processed in
the same manner as a building permit application and will be subject to
compliance with all other laws, ordinances and department procedures in effect
at the time. Signoffs from other public agencies and an initial erosion and
storm water risk assessment may be required. No building permit plan review fee
or building inspections will, however, be required. In the case of a high-risk
site, a site disturbance plan will be required.
      (2)   Industrial chemical process and mineral extraction and processing
equipment exemption. Equipment used primarily for industrial chemical process
purposes and for mineral extraction and mineral processing shall be exempt from
the requirements of this chapter. This exemption does not include the erection
and fabrication of new boilers, pressure vessels and other equipment required
to condition a building for personnel or human comfort and safety, which shall
mean facilities or installations for heating, ventilating, air conditioning,
refrigerating equipment, elevators, dumbwaiters, escalators and boilers and
pressure vessels associated with building heating systems.
      (3)   Federal snow load standards; manufactured/mobile homes. Any
manufactured homes or mobile home constructed in compliance with any snow load
standard established under federal law in effect and applicable to construction
of the manufactured home or mobile home at the time of its construction is
exempt from the provisions of division (C)(2) above; provided, however, that,
all porches, roofs, additions and other structures and buildings attached to or
affixed to any such exempt manufactured home or mobile home shall remain
subject to all applicable laws, codes, regulations and ordinances, including,
but not limited to, any applicable snow load standards.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.183 FEE SCHEDULE.
   (A)   Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter or any codes
adopted pursuant of this chapter, the City Council may, from time to time, by
resolution adopt and amend a schedule of fees for applications, permits,
inspections and all other services performed or permits or licenses issued by
the city pursuant to this chapter.
   (B)   The current fee schedule in effect at the time of adoption hereof
shall remain in effect until later amendment by the City Council.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.184 SETBACKS FOR PUBLIC BUILDINGS.
   Notwithstanding any other provision of this chapter, the city may alter the
setback line in case of a public or government building after a public hearing
if the City Council determines that such alteration is in the best interest of
the city.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.185 VARIANCES.
   A variance of any requirement, specification or standard under this chapter
may applied for and be granted in the same manner as provided for variances
under §§
155.005, 155.130 through 155.148, 155.200 through 155.204 and 155.215 through
155.217 of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
VARIANCES
§ 155.200 DEFINITION.
   (A)   A VARIANCE is a modification or waiver of:
      (1)   The bulk and placement requirements of the ordinance as to lot
size, lot coverage, width, depth, front yard, side yard, rear yard, setbacks,
parking space, height of buildings or affecting the size or shape of a
structure or the placement of the structure upon lots, or the size of lots; or
      (2)   Any other requirement, specification or standard under this
chapter.
   (B)   A VARIANCE shall not be considered a right or special privilege, but
may be granted to an applicant only if:
      (1)   Undue hardship, including, but not limited to, undue economic
hardship, because of characteristics of the site or conditions not the fault of
the applicant would result if the variance is not granted; and
      (2)   Granting the variance is:
         (a)   Consistent with the city’s Comprehensive Plan; and
         (b)   In the best interest of the city.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.201 AUTHORITY TO ISSUE.
   The City Council may grant variances subject to the provisions of this
section and as otherwise authorized by law, including, but not limited to,
Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.202 APPLICATIONS; FEES.
   Applications for variances must be filed with the City Clerk/Treasurer and
shall be referred to the City Council for hearing and decision as hereafter
provided. Applications must be signed by the applicant and the record fee title
owner of the subject lot consenting to the application. The applicant shall
provide the city all information deemed necessary by the City Council to
process the application. The City Council may, by resolution, from time to time
establish and amend a fee schedule for applications for conditional use
permits, including fees sufficient to pay the cost of any notices, publications
or inspections required by law or otherwise deemed necessary by the city to
process the application. The applicant shall pay the applicable variance
application fee at the time the application is filed with the city. The city
shall have no obligation to process any application filed with the city unless
the applicable application fee is paid in full by the applicant. The City
Council shall have the authority to waive all or any portion of the applicable
application fee when it deems such a waiver to be in the best interest of the
city.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.203 HEARING; DECISION; CONDITIONS; JUDICIAL REVIEW.
   (A)   Prior to granting or denying a variance, the city shall comply with
the notice and hearing requirements applicable to hearings on conditional use
permit applications under this chapter. Unless otherwise determined by
resolution of the City Council, the public hearing on the application shall be
initially commenced within 30 days after all notices required by law have been
duly given.
   (B)   In addition:
      (1)   The approval or denial of any variance shall be based upon
standards and criteria which are set forth in the Comprehensive Plan, this
chapter, other applicable city ordinances, and as otherwise provided by law,
including, but not limited to, in Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended;
      (2)   The approval or denial of any application provided for in this
section shall be accompanied by a written decision of the city in compliance
with Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended;
      (3)   The City Council may impose conditions upon any variance granted as
deemed in the best interest of the city, including, but not limited to, any
conditions authorized under Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65, as amended; and
      (4)   Judicial review of any final decision of the city under this
section may be taken in the same manner as provided for judicial review of
final local land use planning decisions under Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65,
as amended.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.204 APPLICABILITY/NON-TRANSFERABILITY.
   Unless otherwise provided in the issued variance, a variance issued by the
city shall apply to and shall run with the lot for which the permit is issued
only, and shall inure to the benefit of owner and owner’s successors in
interests to said land. A variance is not transferable from one lot to another.
A variance shall not be considered as establishing a binding precedent to grant
other variances.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
§ 155.215 VIOLATIONS.
   Violation of any provision this chapter, any term or condition of any
conditional use permit, variance or other permit issued or granted by the city
pursuant to this chapter or any term or condition of any development agreement
made by the owner or developer of a lot pursuant to §
155.148 of this chapter, shall constitute a misdemeanor, and shall be
punishable by a fine, jail, or both, as provided by state law.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.216 ENFORCEMENT GENERALLY.
   The provisions of this chapter may be enforced by the City Mayor, City
Building Official, City Attorney and any state peace officer; provided,
however, that, nothing in this section is intended to, nor shall it, prohibit
the city from pursuing all remedies for any violation of this chapter as may be
provided under this chapter or as otherwise provided by law, with all said
remedies of the city being cumulative and not exclusive.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.217 ADDITIONAL REMEDIES; AMENDMENT, TERMINATION OR REVOCATION.
   In the event any lot owner or developer is in violation of any term or
condition of any conditional use permit, variance or request to rezone issued
or granted by the city pursuant to this chapter or any term or condition of any
development agreement made by the owner or developer of a lot pursuant to §
155.148 of this chapter, the city may after notice and hearing as provided
under Idaho Code § 67-6509, as amended, modify, amend, terminate or revoke, in
whole or in part, said conditional use permit, variance, rezone or development
agreement as deemed in the best interest of the city. Said remedy of the city
shall be in addition to all other remedies of the city for such violations;
provided, however, that, the city shall not commence proceedings to modify,
amend, terminate or revoke, in whole or in part, said conditional use permit,
variance, rezone or development agreement pursuant to this section prior to
giving the lot owner and/or developer, as may be applicable, written notice of
said violation at least 30 days prior to commencement of such proceedings,
unless the City Council finds that a lesser notice period is reasonable under
the circumstances then existing.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
§ 155.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   It shall be a violation of this chapter for any person to violate any
term or condition of any variance issued by the city pursuant to this chapter.
   (B)   It shall be a violation of §
155.161 of this chapter for any person to violate any term or condition of §
155.161 of this chapter or any term or condition of any RV park permit issued
under §
155.161 of this chapter. In addition to all other remedies of the city, which
shall be non-exclusive and cumulative, the city may revoke any RV park permit
in the event the permit holder is in violation of terms or conditions of the
permit or is otherwise in violation of the provisions of this chapter.
   (C)   (1)   The following provisions shall apply to enforcement of the
city’s Building Code, per §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter.
         (a)   Building Official. The Mayor, with the consent and approval of
the City Council, may appoint one or more Building Officials and Deputy
Building Officials to enforce §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter. Each duly appointed Building Official and Deputy
Building Official shall have the authority to enforce all provisions of this
chapter. The city may enter into any agreements with such appointed persons to
act as Building Officials and Deputies as deemed necessary and proper by the
City Council.
         (b)   Enforcement and penalties. In addition to all other remedies
provided under this chapter and as may be provided by law, the following
remedies are available to enforce compliance with the provisions of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter.
            1.   Injunction; public nuisance. The city may seek relief from a
court of competent jurisdiction to restrain any conduct in violation of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter, to compel compliance with §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter, or to abate any nuisance arising from or existing by
reason of a violation of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter. Said remedies may be pursed in addition to all other
remedies provided by this chapter or by law. Any condition or activity in
violation of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter, including any code adopted under §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter, or in violation of any stop work order or no occupancy
order issued under §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter, is hereby declared to be a public nuisance.
            2.   Criminal penalties. Violation of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter by any person, including, but not limited to, any
violation of any term or condition of any stop work order, no occupancy order
or permit issued pursuant to §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter, shall constitute a misdemeanor, and shall be
punishable by a fine, jail, or both, as provided by state law. Each structure
that is in violation of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter, and each day a violation continues, will be considered
a separate violation.
            3.   Stop work/no occupancy orders. The Building Official may issue
stop work orders to prohibit any work, activity or condition in violation of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter. The Building Official may issue an order of no
occupancy to prohibit occupancy of any works, building or structures in
violation of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter. Such orders may be combined in a single document. Such
orders shall be written, and direct that work be stopped, and/or that the
affected works, structure or building may not be occupied, as may be
applicable. Such orders shall be served by posting the order in a prominent
location on the affected premises, works, building or structure with such
service effective upon posting, or personal service upon any occupant of the
affected premises, works, building or structure with service being effective
upon personal service. All persons engaged in doing or causing such work to be
done, or occupying the affected premises, works, building or structure, shall
stop work and not occupy the work, structure or building as ordered until
authorized by the Building Official to proceed. Stop work and no occupancy
orders may be appealed according to the procedure provided in this chapter for
notices of Building Code violations. Nothing in this section shall prohibit or
limit the authority or reasons the building official may issue stop work or no
occupancy orders otherwise permitted under §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter, or any other provision of law.
            4.   Withholding permits. The Building Official may withhold
issuance of any permits, including building permits, on lots or parcels of land
with buildings, structures or activities in violation of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter.
            5.   Compliance agreements. The Building Official may enter into
formal compliance agreements on a case-by-case basis, subject to the following
provisions or conditions.
               a.   The Building Official finds that the violations that are
the subject of the compliance agreement do not pose an imminent threat to
people or property.
               b.   The party responsible for compliance agrees to remedy the
violation(s) in an expeditious manner by a certain date.
               c.   The party responsible for compliance agrees to hold the
Building Official and the city harmless and to defend against any claims
arising through operation of the compliance agreement. The responsible party
shall provide evidence of general liability coverage for person injury and
property damage for the premises subject to the compliance agreement, with the
city named as an additional insured.
               d.   The responsible party shall pay any costs and/or attorney
fee by the city incurred to enforce a compliance agreement.
            6.   Notice of violation. In addition to all other remedies, if a
permit issued under §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter expires prior to the final inspection, or if the
applicant, owner or occupant fails to obtain a certificate of occupancy or
certificate of completion as required by §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter, the Building Official may issue and record a notice of
Building Code violation in the official property records of the county, subject
to the following provisions.
               a.   The Building Official shall prepare and serve said notice
of violation upon the owner or occupant of the affected lot or structure,
either by certified mail, personal service or posting in a conspicuous place on
the premises. The notification shall include:
                  i.   The name of the property owner and the legal description
or street address of the affected property;
                  ii.   The nature of the violation;
                  iii.   The remedial action that must be undertaken to resolve
the violation; and
                  iv.   The length of time allotted, if any, to resolve the
violation.
               b.   The notice of violation shall advise the owner of the
appeal process. The city may consider a written appeal, submitted by the
property owner, and received no later than 20 days after the notice of was
mailed to the owner. The appeal shall be heard by the City Council on a date
specified by City Council. If the appeal is denied, the City Council may, in
its discretion, specify an exact number of days to gain compliance with §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter before the notice of violation is recorded. If the
appeal is approved, the city will specify actions to be taken by the building
official to release the violation. The city may elect to add or remove
conditions of remedial action as it deems necessary and appropriate to secure
compliance with §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter.
               c.   At such time the violation is resolved, the owner shall pay
the fee specified in the current adopted fee schedule and the building official
shall record a release of notice of violation in the official property records
of the County Recorder. A copy of the recorded release shall also be mailed to
the owner via certified mail.
      (2)   Nothing herein is intended to, nor shall it, prevent the city from
taking such other lawful action as is necessary to prevent or correct any
violation of §§
155.180 through
155.185 of this chapter.
(Ord. 2022-3, passed 7-25-2022)
CHAPTER 156: COMPREHENSIVE LAND USE PLAN

156.01   Comprehensive Land Use Plan adopted by reference
§ 156.01 COMPREHENSIVE LAND USE PLAN ADOPTED BY REFERENCE.
   (A)   The City Council hereby adopts the “City of Nezperce Comprehensive
Land Use Plan”, dated 1-10-2022.
   (B)   Said adopted plan is a final print of prior drafts which have been the
subject of the public hearings referenced above and which reflect responses to
public comments upon the proposed amendments.
   (C)   Copies of said Comprehensive Land Use Plan shall be maintained on file
in the office of the City Clerk/Treasurer. Individual copies may be purchased
at the cost of production from the city. An electronic copy is available free-
of-charge.
(Res. R2022-3, passed 1-10-2022)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 157.001 SHORT TITLE.
   These regulations shall be known and cited as the City of Nezperce
Subdivision Regulations, hereinafter referred to as this chapter.
(Ord. 2025-07, passed 3-10-2025)
§ 157.002 AUTHORITY.
   This chapter is adopted pursuant to authority conferred by Idaho Code Title
50, Chapter 13 and Idaho Code Title 67, Chapter 65.
(Ord. 2025-07, passed 3-10-2025)
§ 157.003 PURPOSE.
   The purposes of this chapter are to promote the public health, safety and
general welfare of present and future residents by ensuring that the
subdivision of land results in:
   (A)   The harmonious development of the area;
   (B)   Patterns of lots, blocks, streets, open space and sites for public
facilities that are consistent with the city’s Comprehensive Plan;
   (C)   New developable lots having networks of utilities that are efficient
and cost-effective to maintain;
   (D)   Systems of open space and stormwater drainage, and other natural areas
that connect with and complement similar areas on adjacent lots where possible;
   (E)   To provide standards for such development;
   (F)   Adequate open space for travel, light, air and recreation;
   (G)   Adequate provisions for water supply, drainage, sanitary sewage and
other health requirements;
   (H)   Prevention of noise-sensitive land uses or other uses that would
conflict with operations of the airport;
   (I)   The facilitation of real property transfers by accurate description;
   (J)   The conservation of land by encouraging its most effective and
economical use;
   (K)   The avoidance of scattered subdivisions of land that would result in
any of the following:
      (1)   Lack of essential public services; or
      (2)   Unnecessary imposition of excessive expenditure of public funds for
the supply of such services.
   (L)   Logical procedures for achieving all of these purposes.
(Ord. 2025-07, passed 3-10-2025)
§ 157.004 SCOPE.
   (A)   This chapter is to be in full force and effect from and after its
passage, approval and publication according to the state statutes.
   (B)   If any one or more of the sections, divisions or any other part of
this chapter is for any reason held to be unconstitutional or invalid, such
decision shall not affect the validity of the remaining portions of this
chapter and the same shall remain in full force and effect.
   (C)   Regulations of this chapter shall apply to all real property,
structures or fixtures attached thereto in the city, except as may be altered
under Idaho Code §§ 67-6525 (annexation) and 67-6526 (area of impact) or their
successors. All persons, the United States, the Nez Perce Tribe, the state,
county, city and all their respective agencies, boards, departments,
institutions and local special purpose districts, shall comply with this
chapter unless otherwise excepted by law.
(Ord. 2025-07, passed 3-10-2025)
§ 157.005 JURISDICTION AND COMPLIANCE.
   (A)   This chapter shall apply to the subdividing of all land within the
incorporated city, including property within one mile outside the limits of the
where an adopted city subdivision ordinance will prevail or as mutually defined
by both city and county under requirements of Idaho Code § 50-1306, as amended
or subsequently codified.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful hereafter to make a subdivision of land, as
defined in this chapter, or to set apart land for any public street, road,
alley or any part thereof, until plans of the proposed subdivision have been
submitted to and approved by the City Council or any committee as authorized by
the City Council.
   (C)   No person, firm, corporation or other legal entity shall hereafter
sell, lease or offer for sale or lease any lot, piece or parcel of land which
is within a subdivision as defined by this chapter, without having first
recorded a plat of said subdivision in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter and state law.
(Ord. 2025-07, passed 3-10-2025) Penalty, see §
157.999
§ 157.006 INTERPRETATION.
   All subdivisions as herein defined shall be submitted for review and
recommendation by the City Council and shall comply with the provisions of this
chapter. This chapter shall not apply to any lot or lots forming a part of any
subdivision created and recorded prior to the effective date hereof, except to
the further dividing of lots; nor is it intended by this chapter to repeal,
abrogate, annul or in any way impair or interfere with existing private
restrictions placed upon property by deed, covenant or other private
agreements, or with restrictive covenants running with the land to which the
city is a party.
(Ord. 2025-07, passed 3-10-2025)
§ 157.007 ADMINISTRATION.
   The Council shall carry out the provisions as herein specified. The Council
shall receive and make recommendations on all subdivision applications or other
issues related to city planning and zoning. The Council may choose to designate
a Planning and Zoning Committee to receive and make recommendations on all
subdivision applications or other issues related to city planning and zoning.
The Council shall appoint an Administrator to carry out the provisions as
herein specified and to serve at the pleasure of the Council. The Administrator
shall receive and process all subdivision applications.
(Ord. 2025-07, passed 3-10-2025)
§ 157.008 COMBINING OF PERMITS.
   The Council may coordinate with other departments and agencies concerning
all permits which may be required in this chapter and previously or
subsequently adopted city ordinances. A one-step permit application and
processing procedure may be developed with the respective department and
agencies for the purpose of reducing errors, misunderstanding, confusion and
unnecessary delay for everyone involved.
(Ord. 2025-07, passed 3-10-2025)
§ 157.009 SEVERABILITY.
   (A)   This chapter shall supplement all other regulations, and where at
variance with other laws, regulations, ordinances or resolutions, the more
restrictive requirements shall apply.
   (B)   Where any word, phrase, clause, sentence, paragraph, section or other
part of this chapter is held invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction, such
judgment shall affect only that part so held invalid.
(Ord. 2025-07, passed 3-10-2025)
§ 157.010 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   ACCESSORY BUILDING. Any structure not intended for human occupancy but that
serves as an accessory function to the principal building on the property.
   ADMINISTRATOR. An official, having knowledge in the principles and practices
of subdividing who is appointed by the Board to administer this chapter.
   AFFECTED PERSON. One having an interest in real property which may be
adversely affected by approval or disapproval of a proposed subdivision or
development.
   AGRICULTURAL USES. Farming, dairying, pasturage, cultivation, tillage,
horticulture, floriculture, silviculture, viticulture, vermiculture, animal,
poultry and fish husbandry, as the principal land use and the necessary
accessory uses for packing, treating or storing the produce. AGRICULTURAL USES
shall not include commercial riding stables, race tracks, slaughterhouses,
plants, factories, works for the reduction of animal matter (rendering plant)
or commercial poultry, kennels or feed lots.
   BLOCK. A group of lots, tracts or parcels within well-defined boundaries,
usually streets.
   BUILDING. Any structure securely fixed to the land, and which is designated
or intended for the shelter, enclosure or protection of persons, animals,
material goods for commercial or industrial uses, or property of any kind.
   CEMETERY. A lot that has been platted for the setting of sites for the
burial of animal or human remains.
   CITY. The City of Nezperce, Idaho
   COMMERCIAL USE. A use other than agriculture that involves the sale of
products or services for profit or compensation.
   COMPREHENSIVE PLAN. An adopted document that herein may be referred to as
the Comprehensive Development Plan or the Plan. The document shall show the
general location and extent of present and proposed development, including, but
not limited to, housing, industrial and commercial uses, streets, parks,
schools and other community facilities.
   CONDITIONAL APPROVAL. An affirmative action by the Council that a
recommendation of full approval will be granted upon satisfaction of specified
stipulations by the subdivider.
   CONDOMINIUM. An estate consisting of undivided interest in common in real
property in an interest or interests in real property or in any combination
thereof.
   COUNCIL. The City Council of Nezperce, Idaho.
   COUNTY RECORDER. The Office of the Lewis County Recorder.
   COVENANT. A written promise, pledge or agreement, especially one specifying
restrictions or conditions imposed by the seller of land upon its subsequent
use by the purchaser.
   CULVERT. A drain that channel water under a bridge, street, road or
driveway.
   DEDICATION. The setting apart of land; or interests in land, for use by the
public by ordinance, resolution or entry in the official minutes as by the
recording of a plat. Dedicated land becomes public land only when accepted by
the Board as a public DEDICATION by the passage of an ordinance, a resolution
or an entry of approval in the official minutes of the Board.
   DEVELOPER. Authorized agent(s) of a subdivider or the subdivider himself or
herself.
   DEVELOPMENT. Any grading, vegetation removal, construction activity or any
other activity excluding maintenance that changes the existing character or use
of the land or has any impact on adjoining properties.
   DWELLING UNIT.
      (1)   Any building or other structure proposed or built for occupancy by
people, or a portion of such building proposed for occupancy by people.
      (2)   A pre-fab DWELLING UNIT which is a building or other structure,
proposed or built for occupancy by people that is designed for initial
transportation on streets and highways which arrives at a site where it is
installed on a permanent foundation.
   EASEMENT. Authorization by a property owner for the use by another, and for
a specified purpose, of any designated part of his or her property. Also, a
right acquired by prescription.
   ENGINEER. A person licensed by the state to practice professional
engineering.
   FLAG LOT. An irregular lot, the purpose of which is to allow access to an
otherwise landlocked lot and whose shape resembled a flag and a pole. That
portion of the lot connecting to a street is represented by the pole and shall
not be less than 25 feet in width.
   FLOOD; FLOODING. The temporary inundation of normally dry land areas by
overflow from streams or by unusual and rapid accumulation of surface waters
from any source.
   FLOODPLAIN. The floodplain includes the channel, floodway and floodway
fringe, as established per the engineering practices as specified by the Army
Corps of Engineers, as following:
      (1)   CHANNEL. A natural or artificial watercourse of perceptible extent,
with definite bed and banks to confine and conduct continuously or periodically
flowing water.
      (2)   FLOOD. The temporary inundation of land adjacent to and inundated
by overflow from a river, stream, lake or other body of water.
      (3)   FLOOD OF 100-YEAR FREQUENCY. A flood magnitude which has a 1%
chance of being equaled or exceeded in any given year.
      (4)   FLOODWAY. The channel or a watercourse and those portions of the
floodplain adjoining the channel, which are reasonably required to carry and
discharge the floodwater of any watercourse.
      (5)   FLOODWAY FRINGE. The part of the floodplain which is beyond the
floodway, such areas will include those portions of the floodplain which will
be inundated by a flood of 100-year frequency.
   GOVERNING BODY. The Mayor and Council of the City of Nezperce.
   GREENBELT. Planted and landscaped area designed to act as a buffer area
between non-compatible use area, as well as providing, in some cases,
recreational or conservation open space. GREENBELTS are generally wider and of
a more multi-purpose nature than screening or planting strips.
   HEALTH AUTHORITY. The North Central District Health Department, the State
Department of Labor and Industrial Services, Plumbing Division, and the State
Division of Environmental Quality.
   HIGHWAY. A street designated as a highway by an appropriate state or federal
agency or as defined by law.
   HILLSIDE SUBDIVISION. Any subdivision, or portion thereof, having an average
slope of 12% or more, or where adverse conditions associated with soil
stability, erosion or sedimentation are present.
   IMPROVEMENT. Any alteration to the land or other physical construction
associated with subdivision and/or building site development.
   LARGE SCALE SUBDIVISION. A subdivision, the size of which consists of 30 or
more dwelling units.
   LOT. A parcel or plot of land held under fee ownership by one or more
owners, inclusive of any open spaces required by this chapter. Without
limitation of the foregoing general definition, the term LOT shall also be
deemed to include, but is not limited to, any parcel or plot of land; platted
and identified as a separate LOT or parcel on any duly recorded townsite or
subdivision plat; or assessed as a unique tax parcel by the County Assessor for
real property tax purposes.
   LOT AREA. The total area of a lot measured on a horizontal plane within the
boundary lines exclusive of public and private roads, and access easements to
other property.
   LOT TYPES.
      (1)   LOT, CORNER. A lot situated at the intersection of two or more
streets.
